<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Considerations

<!-- PAGE=? -->
AAA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
High risk surgery with the potential for perioperative complications including cardiac (MI/HF/death), and renal (ARF)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for large fluid shifts, temperature fluctuations, blood loss and hemodynamic instability requiring invasive monitoring and vasoactive medications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hemodynamic, metabolic, and end-organ effects of aortic clamping/unclamping with potential for ischemic insults to heart, brain, kidneys, and spinal cord

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Comorbid disease (CAD / DM / CKD / HTN / Smoking/Advanced age)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-operative pain management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize perioperative myocardial O2 supply-demand relationship by

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o minimizing HD changes of AoX and unclamping

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o minimizing stress response to induction. emergence, and post-op pain

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Minimize distal ischemic complications specifically

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o renal dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o visceral ischemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o spinal cord ischemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Adequate post-operative pain control

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Determine comorbidities, assess end organ perfusion/sx's, identify clinical risk factors, functional capacity Assess renal function (best predictor of PO Renal dysfx). Determine cross clamp location, aneurysm anatomy PE: Assess peripheral pulses, BP, U/O. Focussed cardiopulmonary exam, document neurodeficits Investigations: CBC/Coags/Lytes/Crt/ECG/Echo as per AHA guidelines/CT for aneurysm anatomy/X-clamp location

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: For ruptured: optimize volume, hgb, cross match, coagulation. Elective: cardiology consult for risk stratification, consider BB for intermediate or high-risk patients, hold ACEi. Discont ASA/Plavix/Coumadin and bridge as necessary. Conisder EVAR for high-risk patients not likely to tolerate open procedure. Consider autologous blood donation or ANH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: GA + TEA for elective cases, Avoid epidural in unstable hemodynamics (no morbidity/mortality benefit). GA / Regional for EVAR.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: 5lead, temp monit, foley, 4U PRBCs, fluid warmers, cell-saver, invasive lines, vasopressors, antihypertensives, forced air warmers. PAC/TEE if severe LV dysfx or supra-celiac X-clamp.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Stable induction, have pt prepared and surgeon available if ruptured. Prior to X-clamp, minimize fluids, give heparin 100U/kg. Mannitol .25g/kg prior to cross clamp for renal protection. May need afterload reduction (BB/NTG/ ↑ anesthetic) if high X-clamp, distal perfusion techniques. Anticipate hypotension with clamp release, volume resuscitation, ↓ anesthetic, pressors, reverse heparin.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Ventilate if ruputured/large fluid shifts, pulmonary comorbidities, obese esp with supraceliac clamp. Otherwise extubate, HDU.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Timing of procedure: Between 5.5-6.0 cm, risk of surgery = 1 year risk of rupture, clear benefit > 6.0 cm. 1 year risk of rupture = 9.4%, 10.2%, 32.5% for aneursyms bw 5.5-5.9 cm, 6.0-6.9cm and > 7.0cm respectively.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential difficult airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
difficult BMV, subglottic stenosis, facial anomalies, cervical spine instability (odontoid hypoplasia)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Neurologic complications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Spinal stenosis, hydrocephalus (cervical kyphoscoliosis)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiopulmonary complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Kyphoscoliosis, OSA and central sleep apnea, RLD with Cor-pulmonale

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Difficult neuraxial anesthesia: kyphscoliosis, narrow epidural space, prolapsed discs, deformed vertebral bodies

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Difficult IV access, monitoring and positioning

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Safe establishment of airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Identification and optimization of cardiorespiratory complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Goals for pHTN if applicable

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Achondroplasia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Acromegaly

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential difficult intubation and ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Large tongue, mandibular hypertrophy, thickened vocal cords / glottic stenosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for increased ICP, brain mass - pituitary tumor

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Coexisting Disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Cardiac dysfunction: HTN, LVH, diastolic dysfunction, acromegalic cardiomyopathy; Conduction defects; CAD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Resp: OSA in 70% of males with potential for RV failure (Cor pulmonale)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CNS: Susceptible to peripheral neuropathies → ensure correct positioning

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Misc: Glucose intolerance; vascular ischemia (hand) Osteoporosis; Osteoarthritis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Postoperative: Post-extubation subglottic edema

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize perioperative endocrine function (stress dose steroids), consult endocrinology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Assess and Manage any inc. ICP, avoiding aggravating factors

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Provide still field for microscopic surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Controlled emergence (minimizing bucking / coughing / vomiting to decrease risk of bleeding and CSF leak)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Monitor for postoperative complications eg: DI, SIADH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Addisons's Disease (Adrenal Insufficiency)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential life-threatening Addisonian crisis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o SHOCK, dehydration, hypotension, N/V, anorexia, acute abdomen, hypoglycemia, fever

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Highest risk postoperatively

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiovascular abnormalities

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypotension with dec SVR and dec LV stroke index

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Cardiac conduction abnormalities d/t hyperkalemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypovolemia (2-3L)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Electrolyte imbalance

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hyponatremia, Hyperkalemia, Hypoglycemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pharmacologic considerations

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Risk of hyperkalemic arrest with succinylcholine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Decreased response to circulating catecholamines

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Perioperative steroid replacement

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Anticipate and prevent cardiovascular collapse secondary to Addisonian crisis with appropriate supplemental steroid dosing

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Preoperative correction of fluid and electrolyte abnormalities

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx/Px: assess disease severity - dental caries, reduced exercise tolerance, postural hypotension, arrhythmia, hypovolemia, muscle weakness, fatigue, abdominal pain, N/V, anorexia, confucion, seizures (hyponatremia), weightloss, azotemia, hyperpigmentation (primary AI only), hypoglycemia, infections; adequacy of steroid replacement - 20mg/d prednisone x 5 days at risk for HPA suppression (5-20/d x 4 weeks)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Inv: CBC, Electrolytes, BUN / Cr, ACTH stimulation test (stop all steroids besides dex x 24 hrs, test cortisol 30 - 60 min post ACTH (250ug), normal is level > 25ug/dL; ECG, CXR (cardiopenia), ECHO

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Correct hypovolemia, hyperkalemia, hyponatremia, hypoglycemia, Steroids - hydrocortisone 300mg/d (adequate mineralcorticoid activity) - add fludrocortisones 0.05-0.1 mg/d PO once hydrocortisone is tapered to 15-20 mg PO q am and 5-10 mg PO q pm, acute adrenal insufficiency - IV fluids (NS or D5/NS) 2-3 L or more, Correct electrolytes (Hyperkalemia, hyponatremia, hypoglycemia, Metabolic acidosis), Identify and correct precipitating factors

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Local, regional, general

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Setup: Standard emergency drugs, Hydrocortisone, Standard CAS, Consider arterial and PAC catheterization if cardiac filling pressures indicated / major surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Management of Anesthesia: No specific anesthesia regimen superior, Avoid etomidate (adrenal suppression), Myocardial sensitivity to drugs (narcotics / barbiturates), Muscle weakness / weight loss may require a reduced muscle relaxant dose, May not see changes in HR despite decreased SVR, Check electrolytes, glucose intraoperatively; emergence may be prolonged

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: CXR for pneumothorax if adrenalectomy (up to 20%), Pancreatitis risk with left adrenalectomy, Consider ICU d/t risk of Addisonian crisis postoperatively, monitor for respiratory weakness post-op

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Airway Syndromes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations for the pediatric patient (physiology, pharmacokinetics, cooperation)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential difficult intubation and/or ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o dynamic A/W status as patient grows or disease progresses

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Possible co-existing Pathology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Potential aspiration risk

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Potential for unstable or immobile cervical spine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Developmental Delay

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Obstructive sleep apnea

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 pHTN and cor pulmonale

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o hydrocephalus with inc. ICP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Multiple congenital anomalies

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CHD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Metabolic D/O - hypoglycemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Identify co-exisiting Pathology:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Difficult intubation / ventilation; Aspiration risk; Cervical spine stability; Presence of OSA; Associated anomalies

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Plan A/W management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Appropriate equipment & personnel

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Minimize anesthetic related post operative respiratory depression

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Goal of Preop assessment is to identify pre-existing pathology Hx: Determine airway anomaly and assoc'd syndrome, assess for aspiration risk, OSA, unstable c-spine, Associated conditions (dev delay, hydrocephalus, congenital cardiac disease) PE: Careful airway exam. Predictors of difficult BMV (midface hypoplasia, macroglossia), predictors of difficult intubation (small mandible, decr'd neck ROM, MP score).  Good cardiac exam - CHD, pHTN.  Check for ease of IV access. Investigations: Dictated by procedure. Glucose of neonate. Consider c-spine x-rays for stability, ECHO  to r/o congenital cardiac disease. Sleep study/oximetry if suspected OSA. Optimization: Aspiration prophylaxis if appropriate (ranitidine 0.5 mg/kg IV; metoclopramide 0.1 mg/kg) no preop sedation if risk of airway obstruction, antisialigogue (glycopyrrolate 5-10mcg/kg or atropine 10-20 mcg/kg). Room Setup: Standard monitors and IV placed prior to induction or airway management.  Preoxygenate if possible. Difficult a/w cart with FOB. Consider ENT in the room, neck prepped and draped, rigid bronch available. Induction: Awake vs. SV induction (IH vs. TIVA), consider lidocaine neb pro-op to topicalize, lidospray to cords. BACK UP! Intraoperative Mgt: Minimize long acting respiratory depressants. Post-op: Often more difficult airway after the surgery - similar preperation as preop; Consider post-op ventilation, HDU. Complications: Loss of airway, aspiration. Syndromes assoc'd with potential difficult BMV or intubation:  Treacher Collins, Pierre Robin, Apert,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Special: Down s., Crouzon, Goldenhar, Klippel Feil, Beckwith-Wiedemann, Hurler syndrome, laryngeal webs, cystic hygroma, choanal atresia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Amyloidosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multisystem infiltrative disease with potential for:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Difficult Airway: Macroglossia, laryngo-tracheo-bronchial tree involvement.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CVS: Restrictive cardiomyopathy, complete heart block, risk of sudden death, autonomic neuopathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Resp: Rare pulmonary interstitial disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Renal: Nephrotic syndrome and renal failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
GI : Increased risk of aspiration secondary to autonomic/peripheral neuropathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Amyloid associated illnesses

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multiple myeloma, RA, hypothyroidism, chronic infection or inflammation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations for medical therapy:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Steroids/Chemotherapy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Amyotrophic Lateral Sclerosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Degenerative disease of motor ganglia in anterior horn of the spinal cord and spinal pyramidal tracts (upper and lower motor neuron death), and muscle atrophy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of Aspiration - Bulbar weakness

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Respiratory dysfunction - weakness +/- chronic aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Autonomic instability - orthostatic hypotension and resting tachycardia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Altered response to NMB - Hyperkalemic response to succinylcholine - NdMB sensitivity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Meds: Pyridostigmine, riluzole (liver dysfunction)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Anticipate need for postoperative ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maximize respiratory function with muscle strength, secretion management, pain management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevent aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid hyperthermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Conflicts: RSI vs. avoidance of NMB, regional vs. neurological deficits

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Evidence of respiratory embarrasemnet, pneumonia, ability to cough, functional capacity. Bulbar dysfunction, swallowing difficulty, dysphagia, dysarthria, gag reflex Autonomic symptoms: orthostatic hypotension, syncope, resting tachycardia. Medications: Riluzole - reduce damage to motor neurons by decreasing release of glutamate, can be hepatotoxic, pyridostigmine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
focused neurologic exam / respiratory exam / cardiac (orthostatic BP)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Usual bloodwork, consider PFTs/ABG/CXR/ECG

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Neurology consult, physiotherapy, aspiration prophylaxis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
All options ok, regional/neuraxial preferred, RSI, judicious use of NMBs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Assistant for RSI, CAS + PNS, consider arterial line.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Fully reversed, may require respiratory support

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Special: Usual age 40-60, men:women 1.5:1

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Association with lung carcinoma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Upper and lower motor neuron dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Fasciculations,asymmetric muscle weakness, autonomic dysfunction, leg cramps

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Sparing of sensory apparatus, coordination, intellect, extraocular muscles, sacral PNS innervating bowel/bladder sphincters

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anaphylaxis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic emergency characterized by Hypotension, Hypoxemia, and inc. Airway pressures

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DDx Tension PTX, Dynamic hyperinflation, PE, Bronchospasm, Aspiration, Pulmonary embolism, Transfusion reaction, Mediastinal mass, Carcinoid

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency Management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Stop administration of antigen and inform surgeon - prepare to terminate procedure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Scan monitors: rate, rhythm , BP, EtCO2, SaO2, PIP, Temperature

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hand ventilate with 100% O2, discontinue anesthetic agents

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Secure the unsecured A/W - edema, difficult intubation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Temporize with vasopressors and fluids

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Examine patient for flushing, uticaria, wheezing, and adequacy of CO

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Move quickly to administration of Epinephrine , 10-20ug boluses (1-3ug/kg) titrated up to 500ug

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o 0.3 - 0.5 mls SC of 1:1000 (300 - 500 mcg)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o 10ug/kg (0.1ml/kg 1:10000) in PALS

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Secondary Management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Catecholamines : Epinephrine infusion 5-10ug/min (1ug/kg/min in PALS), Levophed 5-10ug/min

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Bronchodilators for bronchospasm

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Antihistamines : Benadryl 25 - 50 mg IV q4-6h reg (0.5-1mg/kg), Ranitidine 50 mg IV q8h reg

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Corticosteroids : Hydrocortisone 100 mg IV q6h reg, methylprenisolone 1mg/kg IV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Inc. HD monitoring, refractory shock - vasopression, glucagon (1-2mg q5min), bicarb, TEE

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Serum tryptase (within 1-2 hrs), monitor in HDU x 24hrs, A/W prior to extubation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Presentation: CV (74%), cutaneous (70%), bronchospasm (44%)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: After anaphylaxis episode:  a detailed history is important to determine what agents were administered and what was the temporal sequence

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Cardiovascular collapse:  persistent hypotension, pulmonary hypertension, RV dysf'n, tachycardia. Resp: lower resp obstruction, laryngeal edema/obstruction (may persist 5-32 hours despite vigorous therapy).  Derm: flushing, pruritus, uticaria, angioedema; GI - cramps, N/V, diarrhrea; Heme - DIC

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: After resuscitation: red-top tube for mast cell tryptase (preferably within 1-2 hrs of reaction) Repeat 24 h later. Consider blood and urine for histamine concentrations.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: pre-treatment with steroids and anti-histamines NOT effective in preventing anaphylaxis; test dose Abx and other potential allergens; latex free environment

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Options: Neuroaxial - Patients under neuraxial anesthesia may be partially sympathectomized, requiring even larger doses of epinephrine.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: ICU setting.  These patients can relapse - don't send them home for at least 24 hrs. Consultation with immunology re: biochemical testing

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Special:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Muscle relaxants, latex, antibiotics.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
FOOT SURGERY, NOT ANKLE! NEVER USE EPI!

<!-- PAGE=? -->
No Specific Contraindications , disadvantages include high failure rate, slow onset 10-25mins and calf tourniquet pain not covered (ankle tourniquet ok).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anatomy:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
5 nerves, 3 superficial, 2 deep

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Nerve inj (19% transient), 0.4% permanent, local pain 40%, hematoma, infx, LA toxicity or cardiac arrest < 0.01%

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Technique: CAS monitors, leg on pillow to elevate foot, 3 x 10cc LA (25G needle)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Posterior Tibial N: Lies posterior to posterior tibial artery, gives off lateral and medial plantar. Insert needle in grove behind medial malleous and advance until bone contacted. Withdraw 1-2mm and inject 2-3mls local. Withdraw again to skin, fan lateral and medial with 2mls each time.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Deep Peroneal: Lateral to EHL tendon and medial to anterior tibial tendon. Needle perp. to skin until it contacts bone, withdraw 1-2 mm, inject 2-3 cc

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Superficial Peroneal:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Saphenous Nerve:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
From same site as DP block, skin wheal to sup aspect of lateral malleolus ~ 10mls

<!-- PAGE=? -->
From same site as DP block, skin weal to sup aspect of med malleolus ~ 10mls

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ankle Block

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Sural Nerve: Located midway between lateral asp. of the Achilles tendon and the sup asp of the lateral malleolus.  Point needle anteriorly towards fibular, inject 5-7mls in a fan like pattern

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Rescue with either popliteal or sciatic NB.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cutaneous nerve innervation of the {oot

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Femoral Nerve

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Saphenous

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Deep Peroncal nerve

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Anticipate difficult airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Trauma/Neuro: Need to rapidly secure difficult A/W in an unstable patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Laparoscopic may be optimal given restrictive disease but AI and apical bullae may complicate

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ankylosing Spondylitis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for difficult airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Decreased C-spine mobility

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Possible TMJ disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for cervical spine instability with AA subluxation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Axial spine fusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Neuraxial anaesthesia may be technically difficult

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Care with patient positioning

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multisystem disease with extra-articular features:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Cardiac: AI, cardiomyopathy, conduction defects, pericardial effusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Respiratory: RLD with Pulmonary fibrosis, pHTN, apical fibro-bullous disease (1.5-15%)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Neuro: Spondylolisthesis (cord compression), uveitis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Renal dysfunction - NSAID nephropathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications - NSAIDS, Steroids, MTX, TNF-alpha

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Marrow suppression, platelet dysfunction, renal impairment, steroid coverage

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx/Px: Airway for ease of intubation; AAI; assess axial mobility - positioning, neuroaxial; identify comorbid disease - functional capacity, AI, CHF/cor pulmonale, palpitations, RLD, evidence of pHTN; Meds Investigations: CBC, Lytes, BUN, Cr, ECG (condution Dz, pHTN), CXR, +/-PFTs / ABG, ECHO

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Aspiration prophylaxis, Laparosopic procedure preferred for RLD, aggressive multimodal analgesia; There is no clear consensus regarding the management of anti-TNF-a blockers in the perioperative period

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: Neuraxial techniques may still be used but likely to be difficult. Brachial plexus blocks are relatively contraindicated given RLD; GA with ETT (AFOI, awake DL, lightwand), LMA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: Difficult airway cart, CAS + 5, consider A line. Transcutaneous pacer if conduction Dz; further invasive lines may be indicated depending on extra-articular features; SSEPs for spine surgery Intraoperative Mgt: Consider comorbidites (AI, pHTN…) Careful positioning/padding; Rapid desaturation with RLD; Caution with inc. vent pressures with bulla (pneumothorax);

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Low threshold for post-op ventilation if significant restrictive lung (RF - poor pre-op resp func, upper abd/thoracic surgery, long procedure) - HDU

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: failed intubation (LMA); respiratory failure; failed regional (may need to control difficult A/W), tension pneumothorax

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Parturient: no improvement in symptoms with pregnancy; most have vaginal delivery; difficult regional; conflict = difficult regional vs. Difficult A/W & aspiratioin risk

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anorexia, BMI <17.5

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Delayed gastric empyting and risk of aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Fluid and electrolyte abnormalities

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypovolemia (dehydration)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hyponatermia, hypokalemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiac Dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Low-output cardiac failure - decreased cardiac muscle and contractility

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential cardiac arrhythmias - electrolyte abnormalities, prolonged QT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Autonomic disturbances

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Malnutrition: Anemia, thrombocytopenia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications: Antidepressants

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevent aspiration - prophylaxis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Conflict RSI vs. hemodynamic instability

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Identifiy underlying cardiac dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Restore electrolytes and volume pre-operatively

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Aortic Stenosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased risk of perioperative cardiac complications : Ischemia/MI/arrhythmias/CHF

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Identify severity of disease and high risk markers (angina, syncope, CHF)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiac physiologic changes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
fixed LVOT obstruction with limited ability to inc. CO

<!-- PAGE=? -->
hypertrophied ventricle with diastolic dysfunction (reduced ventricular compliance)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Sensitive to volume depletion, Dependent on atrial kick, subendocardial ischemia (↑ muscle mass, ↓ coronary perfusion pressure)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
altered myocardial oxygen supply / demand

<!-- PAGE=? -->
systolic dysfunction (impaired contractility) occurs late in disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Co-existing disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CAD / other valve disease / pHTN / Advanced Age

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ineffective CPR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hemodynamic goals of Ao Stenosis: HR 60-90 (avoid tachycardia; avoid bradycardia), Strict NSR, maintain or augment preload, maintain contractility, avoid decreases in afterload (LV perfusion)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Monitor for ischemia, and optimize favorable myocardial oxygen supply/demand relationships

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Pregnancy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o inc. risk of CHF d/t inc. volume, ischemia with dec. afterload and tachycardia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o early slow epidural to limit tachycardia, avoid spinals d/t dec. afterload

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Determine sx's: angina, syncope or CHF (50% mortality <5, 3, 2 yrs respectively without Sx). Determine valve area Normal AVA 2.6-3.5cm 2 , Mild >1.5cm 2 , gradient <25mmHg, Mod AS 1.0-1.5cm 2 , gradient 25- 40mmHg, Severe <1.0cm 2 , Critical <0.7cm 2 . Functional capacity. Associated CAD/pHTN/arrhythmias

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Narrow pulse pressure, pulsus parvis (reduced pulse volume) et tardus (slow) usually with AVA<0.7cm. Displaced apical impulse, murmer of Ao stenosis (SEM late peaking crescendo-decrescendo, radiating to the neck) Reduced or silent S2. Evidence CHF. S4 (atrial kick into non-compliant ventricle). S3 (filling into non- compliant ventricle). Rales, wheezes, elevated JVP, hepatosplenomegaly.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: CBC, LFTs, Coags, BUN, Cr, CXR, ECG: LVH +/- strain, LBBB, Echo for

<!-- PAGE=? -->
AVA/gradient/EF/pHTN, subvalvular vs valvular. Cardiac Cath: Assess coronaries and AV gradient.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Cardiology Consult. Consider AVR repair/replacement prior to elective sx. Volume resuscitate vs diuresis for CHF. Rate Control.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: Any that maintain hemodynamics (avoid SAB), slow titrated epidural. Severe AS maybe a relative contraindication to neuraxial anesthesia.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: 5 lead ECG/invasive lines, PAC relative contraindication dt risk of arrhythmias, TEE. Short acting BB's, phenyl, lido/amiodarone for ectopy, defibrillator pads.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Opioid based induction, judicious etom/keta/benzo, avoid excessive drop in SVR or contractility (volatiles assoc. with junx rhythm.  Avoid tachycardia on emergence.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Monitor for ischemia, adequate analgesia.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Note acquired vWF due to proteolysis of largest multimers of vWF due to high shear forces through stenotic valve.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Aortic Regurgitation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
AR can be acute or chronic resulting in pressure and volume overload of the LV and reduced forward CO

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased Risk of perioperative cardiac complications (CHF/MI)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hemodynamic alterations associated with AR and associated hemodynamic goals

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Acute - volume/pressure overload, sympathetic stimulation, increased LVEDP / ischemia and arrhythmias, cardiogenic shock

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Chonic - ventricular dilation and hypertrophy, pulmonary hypertension, LV/RV failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Associated co-morbidities:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Other valvular pathology (MS of rheumatic heart disease)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ischemic heart disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Endocarditis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Aortic dilation / dissection

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Connective tissue diseases (rheumatoid arthritis, ankylosing spond.)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Marfan's syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Management of medical therapy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Fast, full, and forward

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain forward flow: High N HR (~90bpm), NSR, maintain, adequate preload (may require augmentation), decrease afterload (maintain adequate CPP), maintain contractility

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Evaluate underlying etiology, onset, severity, symptoms ( CHF /orthopnea/PND), arrhythmias. Assess for comorbidities: Aortic stenosis , CAD , MCTD, pulmonary hypertension .

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Assess volume status, JVP, edema, rales. Displaced LV impulse = cardiac enlargement. Wide pulse pressure, decreased diastolic blood pressure, bounding perph. pulse. De Musset's sign - head bobbing with systole, Corrigan's sign - waterhammer / collapsing.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Auscultate for mumur: Diastolic -blowing‖ mumur at LSB. Abdominal distention and pain - splanchnic ischemia. PE findings pHTN.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: usual BW, ECG - LVH, conduction disorders, CXR - cardiomegaly ECHO -EF/severity of AR, PAP.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Cardiology consult, Consider valve replacement or valvulplasty prior to elective surgery Class 1 indications for repair/replacement: 1) NYHA III-IV HF w/ N syst fnx, 2) NYHA II w/ N syst fnx but progressive dilatation 3. Patients with angina 4. Patients with mild-mod LV dysfunc 5. Patients undergoing cardiac sx for other reason consider light anxiolysis to avoid increase in SVR. Ensure adequate afterload reduction. Hold diuretics and ACEi. Manage anticoagulation for a. fib. Arrange post-op monitored care

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: GA / Neuraxial (anticipate and avoid significant drops in preload) Pregnancy - early epidural to avoid adrenergic inc. in SVR during labour

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: Intropes (milrinone, dobutamine, epinephrine), nipride/NTG, 5lead, +- PAC/TEE

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Induction, preserve preload & contractility / NSR / HR~90bpm / slight afterload reduction. Avoid myocardial depressants or increased SVR. Post AVR may require inotropes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: CSICU or ICU for post-op cardiac monitoring. Observe for: hypotension, ischemia/infarct, LV failure, cardiogenic shock, pHTN +/- RV failure.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 RSI and HD instability

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain oxygenation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevent complications: Pneumonia, ARDS, sepsis, barotrauma secondary to high PIP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Preventable perioperative event with no definitive treatment and significant mortality

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Conflict between aspiration risk and:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Airway quality

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Cardiopulmonary reserve

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Feasibility and tolerance for regional techniques

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Consider aspiration in differential diagnosis of bronchospasm with hypoxemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx & Px: RF for aspiration:  Hx of difficult airway, H&N surgery/radiation, DM, NM D/O, reflux, dysphagia, peptic ulcer disease, Cardiopulmonary - exercise tolerance, edema, angina Manifestations: gastric contents in oropharynx, hypoxemia, inc PIP, bronchospasm, copious tracheal secretions, coughing, laryngospasm, rales, chest retraction, dyspnea, CXR changes Optimization: avoid GA, antacids, H2 antagonist, metoclopramide, ng suctioning prior to induction and extubation, cricoid pressure, consider awake intubation, extubate awake GA, local, regional (avoid depression of laryngeal reflexes by excess sedation )

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: Intraoperative Mgt:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Perform immediate tracheal suctioning prior to positive pressure ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 If ETT is in the trachea, place the patient head down, with right lateral tilt (protect left long)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Pass a suction catheter down the ETT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain oxygenation:  PPV with 100% FiO2 , PEEP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Perform bronchoscopy if particulate aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Cancel elective surgery.  Emergency surgery should be restricted to the minimum procedure consistent with patient safety

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op :  If patient remains stable throughout event without significant desaturation/hypotension etc. could consider discharge from PACU after 2 hours of observation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Provide supportive care:  fluid mngt, H2 blockers, intermittent pulm toilet

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Empiric antibiotics if compromised patient, fulminant course, high bacterial load

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Prophylaxis is indicated for known aspiration of feculent material

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Bronchodilators to relieve large airway closure in less damaged areas of the lung

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Consider ECMO support if oxygenation cannot be maintained

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Asthma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
reversible expiratory obstruction due to hyperactive bronchi with inflammation, mucous hypersecretion and bronchoconstriction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
High risk for perioperative respiratory complications including respiratory failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 FEV1 < 40% indicates severe obstruction,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Normal or high PaCO2 suggestive of fatigue and impending failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Perioperative Bronchospasm

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Barotrauma and Pneumothorax

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for Status Asthmaticus & Pulmonary Tamponade

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Identify patients at risk: previous attacks, freq hospitalizations, steroids, can't speak, inc. WOB, silent chest, confusion, increasing or N CO2.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Ddx Wheezing: FB, aspiration, anaphylaxis, cardiogenic edema, tracheal stenosis or malacia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Medical Management Salbutamol/Ipratropium/Epinephrine/Corticosteroids/ Aminophylline/MgSo4/SEVO/Heliox/ glycopyrolate/atropine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Ventilatory strategies and consideration for ECMO

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Early, aggressive management of bronchospasm, and frequent assessment for need for intubation and ventilation.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Indication of intubation: pH <7.2, unremitting hypoxia SaO2 <90%, progressive exhaustion, decreased LOC. Hypercarbia although a marker of severe disease is not an indication for intubation.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid Thiopental/Histamine releasing narcotics/NdMR. Watch for tachydysrythmias due to Rx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Salbutamol: MDI 4-20 puffs/hour, Neb 5-10mg q 15mins prn, IV 4mcg/kg load then 0.1-0.2mcg/kg/min Epinephrine (1:1000) 4-8mcg/min

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ipratropium: MDI 4-20 puffs/hour, Neb 0.5mg  q 30-60mins prn

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Corticosteroids: Methylpred 40-125mg/ q6h or Hydrocortisone 500 mg IV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Aminophylline: 3-6 mg/kg load and 0.2-0.9 mg/kg/hr infusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
MgSo4: 2-4 grams over 20 mins, then 1gram/hour infusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intubations: Ketamine/Lidocaine/Benzo's/Narcotics, avoid STP/Histamine release/NDMBs such as mivacurium/cis-atracurium. Avoid Cholinesterase inhibitors.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ventilator: FiO2 = 1, TV 6-8ml/kg, RATE 6-8/min, PEEP <5, Keep PIP < 50 cm/h20, Square wave flow (increases VI). May need to disconnect patient for for dynamic hyperinflation and chest compression. If severe bronchospasm on intubation and can't ventilate, confirm tube placement, r/o pneuo and then give IV adrenaline. Maintain with Volatile, consider ECMO!

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Bronchospasm:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimize preop with bronchodilators

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid histamine release

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Morphine, Atracurium

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Deep plane of anaesthesia prior to airway manipulation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Consider bronchodilating anaesthetic agents: ketamine, sevoflurane

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Extubation plan

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Deep extubation +- LMA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Opioids prior to emergence - remifentanil

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ASRA Consensus (2002)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
General: Use extreme caution in neuroaxial blocks on patients taking more than one anticoagulant

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Thrombolytics:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Don't do neuraxial technique . If administered inadvertently, fibrinogen level may be helpful

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Unfractionated Heparin

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Low dose SC prophylactic dosing not a contraindication but hold until after administration of block

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Check platelets after > 4 days of UFH (HIT)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Intraoperative IV dosing  (e.g. vascular surgery) acceptable 1 hour after needle

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Remove catheter with 2 conditions:  1) 2-4 hours after last heparin dose; 2) Patient's coagulation status documented . Restart anticoagulation 1 hour after catheter removal

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Bloody/difficult insertion + UFH may increase risk but not contraindication to proceeding

<!-- PAGE=? -->
LMWH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Don't monitor Xa; peak effects 2 hours after administration .

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 If bloody tap - inform surgeon, avoid LMWH for 24 hours

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Low dose (prophylactic) LMWH:  delay needle for > 10-12h

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Enoxaparin 0.5 mg/kg every 12 hours

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Dalteparin 5000 units every 12 hours

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 High dose (treatment) LMWH:  delay needle for > 24h

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Enoxaparin 1 mg/kg every 12 hours

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Enoxaparin 1.5 mg/kg daily

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Dalteparin 120 U/kg every 12 hours

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Dalteparin 200 U/kg daily, or

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Tinzaparin 175 U/kg daily

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Post operative BID LMWH (high dose):  delay at least 24h after needle; not compatible with catheters left insitu and may start 2h after catheter removal

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Post operative daily LMWH (low dose):  delay at least 6-8h after needle; compatible with catheters left in situ but must be removed >10-12 h after last dose and restarted > 2h after removal

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Oral Anticoagulants (Warfarin)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Discontinue therapy 4-5 days preoperatively, document normal INR (<1.5)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 If warfarin intitiated > 24h preop, check INR prior to block

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Document INR < 1.5 prior to catheter removal, monitor daily if on therapy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Monitor neurological status minimum 24h after catheter removal, longer if INR > 1.5

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Antiplatelet Agents

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 NSAIDs (including ASA) do not increase risk of spinal hematoma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Discontinue clopidigrel > 7 days; Ticlopidine > 14 days before needle

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Glycoprotein IIb/IIIa inhibitors - Eptifibatide (integrillin) and Tirofiban (Aggrastat) delay > 4-8h after administration; Abciximab (ReoPro) delay > 24-48h after administration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid neuraxial technique in patients on more than one antiplatelet agent

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Herbal Drugs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 No data and no contraindication to block (do not increase risk of hematoma on their own)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Thrombin Inhibitors (Desirudin, lepirudin, bivalirudin, argatroban)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Increased risk of bleeding, but no specific recommendations

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Fondaparinux (Arixtra)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Minimal data, but increased risk of hematoma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Recommend single atraumatic pass, no indwelling catheters

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Interscalene:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Brachial Plexus Blocks 1/2

<!-- PAGE=? -->
for shoulder surgery, ulnar sparing

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Specific Contraindications: Unable to tolerate reduced FEV1 by 25% (interscalene) ie FEV1 < 1L; Contralateral vocal cord paralysis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: 100% Phrenic, Pneumo 0.2%, Horners, Intravascular injection, 13-24% hypotension/brady, inadvertent SAB, Epidural block.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anatomy: Roots/Trunks

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Approach: Palpate interscalene groove with head supine and rotated 30 deg away. EJ crosses the groove at the level at the cricoids cartilage. Skin wheel at the level of the CC, 22g 1.5‖ needle inserted perpendicularily in slightly medial and caudal direction.  Stimulating Phrenic = Too anterior, Trapezius = posterior. Look for motor activity of the arm, wrist or hand, but deltoid OK.  30-40mL local.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
for any upper extremity surgery that does not req the shoulder

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Supraclavicular:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Specific Contraindications : avoid bilateral due to risk of bilateral pneumos or phrenic nerve block.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Phrenic Nerve (50-60%), Horners, Nerve Injury 0.02-0.4%), Cardiac arrest 0.01%, Hematoma, local pain (40%). Highest incidence of pneumothorax, however should be less than 5%

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anatomy: Trunks at the lateral boder of Ant. Scalene, most reliable U/E block

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Approach: Palpate interscalene groove at its most inf point, just post to subclavian pulse (SP); the latter can be felt in a plane just medial to the midpoint of the clav. After a skin wheal, a 22g 1.5‖ needle is directed just ↑ and post to the SP and directed caudally at a very flat angle against the skin. Obs for muscle contrac. of the forearm. 25-40mL. If U hit rib, the needle is withdrawn and reval path. The ‗plumb-bob' techn is another SC approach. The needle entry site is immed. sup to the clavicle, just lat to the point where the SCM is attached to the clavicle. The angle of needle entry is 90° to the table. If you contact rib, try manipulating in an ant to post direction or walk along rib.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Infraclavicular: Misses skin of axillae and prox medial arm (intercostobrachial, Medial brachii cut nerves)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anatomy: Cords, beyond the first rib Specific contraindications: None , safer than supraclavicular Complications: Pneumo(rare), hemo, and chylothorax (with a left-sided block) are possible and occur at a higher rate than with the supraclavicular approach. Phrenic = rare.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Approach: When performing, the patient lies supine with the head slightly turned away from the side of the procedure. The operative limb is abducted to 90° and the axillary pulse is identified. The midpoint of the clavicle is identified and 2 cm caudal to this point a needle is inserted at a 45° angle and directed toward the axillary art pulsation. With a 4-in, 21-gauge insulated nerve stimulator needle, motor activity in the hand is sought. Or you may use the coracoid approach which is 2cm medial and inf. to the coracoid process. Needle insertion is perp. to floor. If no twitch aim cephalad then caudad.  Do not accept musc. N as it may leave the sheath at this point in 50% of pts. Axillary: Musc nerve has already left the sheath at this point and is in coracobrachialis, good for procedures distal to elbow. Can block with 5-10ml in CB abv artery, fanning technique or at elbow.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anatomy:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Terminal Nerves

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hematoma, IV injection, Nerve injuries

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Approach: The pulse of the axillary artery is identified as high (proximal) in the axilla as possible. Using an "immobile needle" technique, a 22-gauge, 1.5-in needle is inserted until bright red blood is aspirated. The needle is then slightly advanced or withdrawn until blood aspiration ceases. Injection can be performed posteriorly, anteriorly, or in both locations in relation to the artery. A total of 40 mL of local anesthetic is usually injected; distal pressure on the sheath during the injection may promote better cephalad spread of the solution within the sheath.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intercostabrachial Nerve Block (T2):

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Brachial Plexus Blocks 2/2

<!-- PAGE=? -->
for anesthesia to medial arm/tourniquet pain

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Approach: T he intercostobrachial nerve derives from the T2 somatic intercostal nerve, whereas the medial brachial cutaneous nerve derives from C8 and T1. Both become superficial and cutaneous at the pectoral ridge over the humeral head. They are easily blocked, with the arm abducted, by means of a linear injection (field block) from the deltoid prominence superiorly to the most inferior aspect of the medial upper arm (Figure 17-3). A total of 5 mL of local anesthesia is used.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Nerve Blocks at the Elbow:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ulnar Nerve: Flex elbow 30degrees, 2 cm proximal to groove bw medial epicond and olec. Process. 5ml of LA.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Median Nerve: Intercondylar Line, Medial to Biceps Tendon and 1 cm medial to brachial artery at this IC line. Elicit paras. or motor resp. or hit periosteum and withdraw 0.5-1cm. Inject 3-5 ml.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Radial Nerve: Same Intercondylar line, 2 cm lateral to BT. Nerve is deep, can elicit parasthesia move in a fan shape or hit bone and withdraw 0.5cm. Inject 5ml. Aim towards lateral epicondyle on insertion.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Lateral Cutaneous Nerve of the Forearm: Branch of MSC N. Inject just below fascia lateral to BT and medial to radial nerve. 2-3ml LA.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medial Cutaneous Nerve of the Forearm: Branch of medial cord. SC infiltration from biceps tendon to medial epicondyle.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Brain Death and Organ retrieval

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Confirm the diagnosis of brain death and confirm wishes of patient and family

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o NDD by 2 physicians not involved with transplant (see below)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Physiologic Consequences of Brain death

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hemodynamic instability (myocardial dysfunction, vasomotor tone, hypovolemia - )

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Pulmonary dysfunction - ARDS and Hypoxemia (pulmonary edema - Neuro vs. cardiac, VAP)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Neuro-endocrine dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 DI (70%), hypokalemia, Hypothyroid, hypocortisolemia, Hyperglycemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Coagulopathy / DIC (brain release of thromboplastin)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Poliokothermia secondary to hypothalamic dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Etiology of Brain Death and secondary injuries

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Trauma (potential for multi-organ involvement, pulmonary / cardiac contusions)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 maintain end-organ perfusion (monitoring, fluids, vasopressors & ventilatory support)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o SBP > 100 mmHg, pO2 >100 mmHg, U/O 100 mL/h (1-1.5 ml/kg/h), Hb > 100 g/L, CVP 5-10 mmHg, FiO2 < 40% for lung retrieval

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Strategies for organ preservation using free radical scavengers including mannitol, superoxide dismutase, and the free radical synthesis blocker allopurinol

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Consider hormone replacement therapy (improve solid organ retrieval)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Methylprednisolone 15 mg/kg q24h

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Tetra-iodothyronine (T4) IV: 20 mcg bolus followed by 10 mcg/h infusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Vasopressin: 1 unit bolus followed by 2.4 units/h infusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Minimal clinical criteria for NDD : etiology of NDD in absence of conditions mimicking NDD, Deep unresponsive coma & bilat absence of motor response (excludes spinal reflex), No corneal/pupil responses (pupils mid-size or greater) with no brain stem reflexes (gag/cough, vestibulo-ocular, facial motor response), Positive apnea test (PaCO2≥60 or ≥20mmHg inc.) Absent confounding factors.  Minimal T=34  C.  Ancillary test if Unable to determine min criteria: 4 vessel angio of common/internal/vertebral arteries.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Brain death hemodynamics - intial ischemia results in unopposed vagal stimulation (brady,blocks, hypotension, low CO), progression to midbrain results in vagal stimulation with marked sympathetic activation (tachy, arrhythmias, HTN), finally complete brainstem ischemia - loss of vagal tone with unopposed sympathetic activation, Herniation of brainstem - loss of sympathetic activation with profound hypotension Hx/Px: Review history preceding NDD (etiology, e.g. trauma), secondary injuries, current meds/ventilation to maintain organ perfusion, Vitals/Temp, U/O

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: CBC, Lytes, BUN, Cr, Group & Screen, ABG (looking for anemia, electrolyte abnormalities (DI), renal insufficiency, acidosis). Imaging: CXR (lines & tubes, pulmonary edema, aspiration etc.), ECG (rhythm, ischemia), ECHO (EF, wall motion abnormalities, contusions)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Lung protection ventilatory strategy, (Vt 6-8, plat < 30 mmHg, PEEP to minimize FiO2, SaO2 > 95%, colloids > crystalloid), triple hormone therapy, glycemic control, euthermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: volatile & narcotic with inotrope/vasopressors for hemodynamic ctrl only (no Awareness) Room Setup: CAS, 5 lead, A-line, CVC, Foley, temp probe

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Vasopressors (epinephrine, vasopressin) to support blood pressure, DA and phenylephrine suggested to improve splanchnic perfusion. Vasodilators (phentolamine, alprostadil [lung retrieval]) to improve perfusion during cross-clamping, heparin prior to x-clamp, Active warming Direct chronotropes ( isoproterenol, DA ) to treat brady as brain dead patient unresponsive to vagolytics Post-op: appropriate disposition of remains

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypoxia, hypercarbia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Drugs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Anesthetic drugs  SCh, anticholinesterases, opioids, Neuraxial blockade

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Cardiac drugs   -blockers, CCB, Clonidine, Digoxin, pheynlephrine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiac

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 ischemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 conduction system disease  SSS, heart block

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Nerves

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Vagal mediated  pain, occulocardiac, peritoneal stretch, ECT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Baroreceptor mediated  ICP, HTN, carotid sinus manipulation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Endocrine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 hypothyroidism

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 hypothermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency Management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Inform surgeon, Scan monitors: rate, rhythm , BP, EtCO2, SaO2, temperature

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hand ventilate with 100% O2

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Examine patient for pulse or signs of adequate perfusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Develop DDx and treat as per ACLS protocol

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Bradycardia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Does the patient have a pulse ?  if not, immediate ACLS Most important Question is sinus bradycaria or not?

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DDx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Bronchiectasis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk for severe Respiratory Complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Auto-PEEP & pulmonary tamponade

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mucus plugging d/t impaired mucociliary activity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Recurrent lung infections / abscess

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Massive hemoptysis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Chronic Hypoxemia & Hypercarbia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
pHTN & RVF

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Associated therapy: Postural Drainage, Abx's, Chest Physio.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Underlying etiology: Cystic Fibrosis, congenital cartilage defn, HIV, TB, infection, inflammation, Rheumatoid arthritis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize pre-operative lung function with postural drainage and Abx therapy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevent contamination of good lung with purulent sputum (consider lung isolation)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid instrumentation of the airway or nasal intubations (chronic sinusitis)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Bronchopleural Fistula

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Possible life-threatening emergency from ineffective PPV, tension pneumothorax or lung flooding

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Requirement for lung isolation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Minimizes air leak and facilitates ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prevent soiling of contralateral lung if abscess/ empyema present

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Comorbid disease / etiology for BPF

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Lung abscess/ empyema

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o SIRS, MOF, EtOH abuse, IVDU, steroids, DM

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post lung resection

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o COPD, arrhythmia, malignancy, CAD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Trauma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Spontaneous pneumo/ bullous disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals / Conflicts

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 isolation of affected side to support ventilation and prevent cross-contamination

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 prepare for and be ready to resuscitate from cardio or respiratory collapse

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 facilitate early extubation post-thoracotomy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: acute or chronic; stable or unstable; post-op resection vs. infective vs. trauma; airleak, dyspnea, fever, pleuritic pain, purulent sputum or drainage, Comorbidities - 4Ms, COPD (severity, meds, exacerbations, smoking), RHF (SOB, syncope, jaundice, fatigue, edema), functional capacity PX: VS, ?SIRS, A/W - ease of intubation/lung isolation; Resp - WOB, Tracheal deviation, subcu emphysema; Comorbid disease - COPD (inc AP diameter, prolonged expiration, wheeze); Estimate the loss of VT through the fistula (bubbling through the chest tube), Quantify the difference between inhaled and exhaled tidal volumes (spirometry); CVS - pHTN/RHF: loud P2, RV heaves, TR murmur, elevated JVP, hepatic congestion, peripheral edema; Trauma: other injuries Inv: CBC (sepsis), Lytes, Bun, Cr (paraneoplastic syndromes), INR/PTT (epidural), ABG, x-match; CXR/CT (pneumothorax, chest tube, bullae, empyema, chronic lung disease), ECHO (RHF), ECG (RVH - R > S in V1, p-pulmonarale, atrial arrhythmia, demand ischemia if septic), PFTs (baseline) Optimization: chest tube, drain empyema, aspiration prophylaxis, antisialogogue (FOB), Resuscitate Anesthetic Setup: 5 lead, +/- TEA, Artline, +/-CVC, FOB, multiple ETT (DLT, SLT, blockers), CPAP,, HFJV, Chest tube tray and thoracic surgeon in room Management: D/C chest tube suction (dec. leak), SV lung isolation with DLT ideal (AFOI vs. asleep SV induction vs. RSI with DLT / bronchial SLT, if PPV - low Vt, low pressures, watch for contralateral lung contamination; HFJV allows ventilation with lower Pk pressures; surgeon can pack the lung once the chest is open; early extubation, good analgesia (TEA, Paravertebrals, intercostals, PCA) Complications: ·Tension pneumothorax, Inability to ventilate with hypoxemia and hypercarbia (Consider briefly clamping chest tube), Outpouring of pus and lung flooding, Complications from OLV: hypoxemia, Sepsis, Pain, Persistent air leak

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Burns (>10% BSA 3 rd  degree or 25% 1-2 nd  degree)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Trauma Pt / Emergency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential Difficult A/W with inhalational injury (ALI)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Coexisting CN & CO Toxicity necessitating 100% O2 and early potentially hyperbaric chamber

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypovolemia: Volume Resuscitate with Parkland formula - 4cc/kg/%BSA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multi-organ dysfunction:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiogenic shock (circulating mediators, inc SVR, dec.CBF)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ALI/ARDS, A/W sluffing, ARF, Rhabdomyolysis, Sepsis, hypothermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Altered Pharmacology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Sux hyperkalemia > 24 hrs, resistance to NdMRs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Susceptibility to myocardial depressants

<!-- PAGE=? -->
High analgesic requirements

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Recurrent Procedures: Difficult IV Access & monitoring; bld loss; pain; remote location

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 ATLS approach to all patients

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Early and safe airway management: Avoid Sux > 24 hrs - 2 years after injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Assume inhalational injury and provide 100% O2, investigate for cyanide and CO toxicity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Volume resuscitation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid End-organ damage, U/O 1ml/kg, ARDS ventilation stratetgy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Provide adequate analgesia - multimodal approach

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ATLS: Assess for inhalational burn, early intubation, 1.0 FiO2, stop burning process (brush chemicals off, copious water), large bore IV access in non-burmed area (groin), volume resuscitate. Transfer: >10%, extremes of age, sensitive areas (face, hands, perineum), comorbidities Hx: AMPLE history, tetnus status, Type & location burn - chemical (alk worse than acid), thermal, electrical (deep muscle necrosis, rhabdo, ARF); Associated trauma (covert injury).  Inhalational injury - dyspnea, hoarseness, carbonaceous sputum, singed facial hair. CN toxicity (H/A, dizzy, tachycardia, tachypnea, lethargy, Sz, coma); CO Toxicty (H/A, dizziness, confusion, N/V, visual changes, CNS dysfunction). PE: Vitals +temp, ABCDE, A/W for ease of intubationU/O, C-spine. CNS exam for CO toxicity vs head trauma. CVS: Volume status, cap refill Resp: focused airway exam for inhalational injury. Burn area (%BSA - Rule of 9's; palm = 1%TBSA); burn severity Investigations: CBC, Lytes, Coag Profile, urine myoglobin, ABG (lactic acidosis with CN toxicity), Cooximetry, Serum Cyanide (tox >0.2mg/L, lethal >1mg/L), ECG, CXR, Diagnostic FOB Optimization: 100% O2, volume resuscitation as per Parkland formula 4 cc/kg/%BSA - 50% in 1 st  8hrs, 50% in next 16 hrs. Consider HBO for CO (>30%); CN- toxicity - HBO, amyl nitrate, Na nitrite (5mg/kg), Na thiosulfate (150mg/kg), hydroxycobalamin. Maintain U/O 1cc/kg/hr - Consider mannitol if myoglobinuria, Alkalinize urine to inc. solubility (correct met acidosis). Consider inotropes for volume resistant shock. ARDS ventilation strategy. Early enteral feeding. Room Setup: CAS +5lead, temp, Hot OR, Art line (sampling), CVC (fld status), needle electrodes, foley, vasopressors, PRBC.  Large bore IV's, difficult airway cart. Avoid early surgical airway due to poor outcomes. Intraoperative Mgt: Regional vs GA. Avoid Sux > 24 hrs, consider larger dose of NdMRs (peak resistance 2-6 wks, starts 48hrs) Difficult A/W - AFOI vs. SV induction if uncooperative; RSI if OK; Avoid ++ propofol due to myocardial depression. Conisder Ketamine. ++ analagesia; lung protection; volume resuscitate. Post-op: Burn unit; HDU; ICU; multi-modal analgesia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
C1 Esterase Inhibitor Deficiency (Hereditary Angioedema)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential airway emergency with complete airway obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Disease of acute airway edema

<!-- PAGE=? -->
refractory to conventional treatment of airway edema ( corticosteroids, epinephrine, antihistamines)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
precipitated by emotional stress, trauma, oral surgery, or direct laryngoscopy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevent recurrent episodes with long-term prophylaxis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o anabolic steroids , anti-fibrinolytics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevent acute perioperative episode

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Avoidance of airway instrumentation (regional anesthesia favoured)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o short-term prophylaxis with C1 esterase inhibitor infusions (25 units/kg one time dose), FFP (2-4 units)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Treatment of an acute attack

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Early tracheal intubation, preparation for surgical airway, treatment with C1 esterase inhibitor infusion or FFP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Caesarian Section

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential Emergency - no time for optimization, aspiration risk

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pregnancy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
potential difficult airway, full stomach

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mallimpatti >1, short neck, receding mandible, prominent incisors (overbite)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
physiologic changes including

<!-- PAGE=? -->
dec. FRC - rapid desaturation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
anemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
dec. anesthetic requirements

<!-- PAGE=? -->
aortocaval compression

<!-- PAGE=? -->
potential massive bleeding

<!-- PAGE=? -->
maintenance of fetal oxygenation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Postpartum Hemorrhage - atony, products, accrete, coagulopathy, inversion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Neuroaxial - High spinal, PDPH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Embolism - PE, VAE, AFE

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Determine urgency of situation - Continuous fetal monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Administer safe, time-sensitive anesthetic with emphasis on mother

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Conflicts

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Difficult A/W vs. STAT section

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hemodynamic instability vs. Regional anesthesia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Urgency of situation; reason for C/S; AMPLE Hx; Ob Hx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Investigations: Optimization:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
airway, cardiopulmonary exam, fluid status and back exam for ease of neuraxial technique

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CBC, diff, G&S, coags if applicable (PIH or prophylactic anticoagulation)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Aspiration prophylaxis ; LUD ; IV fluids if necessary

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Standard; emerg drugs and equipment available for GA if neuraxial fails

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Difficult a/w cart if difficult a/w anticipated

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Oxytocin, nitro available

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 For neuraxial: frequent BP checks after spinal

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Oxytocin after delivery of neonate

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Good communication with mother and surgeon

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 For GA: anticipate potential difficult ventilation/intubation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 PPH;  Aspiration (Extubate awake); pain management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Special:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Anesthetic complications:  Hypotension, high spinal, failed spinal, PDPH, awareness

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Surgical complications:  Hemorrhage, atony, difficult extraction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Carcinoid

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Carcinoid is the most common GI endocrine tumor (1-2 per 100,000); 2-5% of patients will exhibit carcinoid syndrome:  flushing with diarrhea, hemodynamic instability +/- bronchospasm; carcinoid heart disease is present in 20-40% of patients with carcinoid s

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Malignancy (mass, medications, metastases, metabolic)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of perioperative carcinoid crisis - hypotension & bronchospasm

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Flushing, diarrhea, hemodynamic instability (serotonin - HTN, histamine - hTN, bronchospasm, hyperglycemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Associated carcinoid heart disease (20-60%)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Right-sided valvulopathy, 10% L sided valvular disease (MR, AR)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o constrictive pericarditis, SVT, Intramyocardial metastases

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Other endocrinopathies

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Cushings, acromegaly (bronchial carcinoid)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid perioperative carcinoid crisis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Avoid triggers:  Avoid SNS (hypoxia, hypercarbia, hypovolemia, sympathomimetics), histamine release, pain/anxiety, tumour manipulation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Premedicate with octreotide (prevent vasoactive mediator release)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Treatment of perioperative bronchospasm

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Avoid B-agonists, epinephrine, theophylline

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Responds to octreotide, corticosteroids, histamine blockers

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Carcinoid Symptoms (flushing, syncope, headache, hypertension, hypotension, nausea, vomiting, diarrhea, bronchospasm); Mass effect (malnutrition, obstruction - endobronchial, GI); Cardiac dysfunction (palpitations, syncope, edema, HTN); location of tumour; S/S of cushings, acromegaly; medical therapies PE: vitals + posturals, volume status, Resp - Wheeze endobronchial lesion or bronchospasm, CVS - valvular Dz (TR-inc. JVP, canon V, RV heave, S3; PS-large A wave, split S2, SEM LUSB right sided), RVF; Derm: Pellagra (niacin def: dermatitis diarrheam dementia), hyperkeratosis, hyperpigment, venous telangiectasia Investigations: CBC, coags, lytes, BUN, Cr, Mg, Ca, alb, LFTs, G&S, CXR; ECG +/- ECHO; U/A: 5-HIAA Optimization: Consult endo/cardio, anxiolysis, preop octreotide (50-300 mcg SC 30 minutes preop or 25100mcg IV three minutes preop - infusion of 100ug/hr may be required). Possible long acting IM formulation. Anesthetic Options: All techniques OK for asymptomatic pts - Epidural good for postop analgesia - avoid epinephrine; GA is indicated for symptomatic pts or with tumor manipulation Room Setup: CAS +5, foley, art line (preinduction), CVP, large bore IV, fluid warmer, Baer hugger. Avoid SNS agents (indirect, beta agoinists, reflex activation - epi, norepi, ephedrine, dopaime, isoproterenol); Phenyl, esmolol, phentolamine for HD derangement; octreotide; dilute vasopressin; avoid histamine release Intraoperative Mgt: Titrated and deep induction - Goal is stable hemodynamics. Avoid hypotension (reflex SNS). Maintain normothermia. Communicate with surgeon and pre-empt hemodynamic shifts following tumour manip with doses of octreotide - 25-50ug bolus (no ceiling - inc. until desired effect); frequent lytes & glucose Bronchospasm is best managed with octreotide (other agents include steroids, antihistamines). Carcinoid Crisis : stop stimulus, 1.0 FiO2, fluids, phenylephrine, vasopression, octreotide 100-200ug boluses titrated to effect; vasopressin, H1 or H2 blockade, serotonin antagonists (ondansetron) Post-op: Good multimodal analgesia. Aggressive prophylaxis of N&V. HDU for true carcinoid syndrome or intraoperative crisis. High risk of delayed awakening secondary to serotonin (decreased MAC …); Wean octreotide post-op (endocrine consult)

Cardiac Assesment for Non-cardiac Surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->

<!-- PAGE=? -->

<!-- PAGE=? -->

<!-- PAGE=? -->

<!-- PAGE=? -->
nklcort

<!-- PAGE=? -->
LOE B

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Stepwise approach

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Step 1: Determine urgency of surgery Step 2: Identify unstable syndromes (5): Recent MI < 30d, Unstable angina, decompensated HF, Severe valvular disease, Severe dysrhythmias Step 3: If no unstable syndromes and low risk surgery, proceed … Step 4.. Assess functional capacity: 1 MET = ADLS, 4 METs = light housework, ie washing dishes, >4 METs = climbing 1 flight of stairs, walking at 4mph or 6.4 km/hr. 1 MET is energy consumed by the body at rest and is equal to 3.5 ml/kg/min. Step 5: Assess clinical predictors (5): Stroke, stable angina, compensated HF, renal failure, DM. Step 6: Determine path depending on number of predictors and risk of surgery as per guidelines.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiac Risk: Vascular ~5%, Intermediate 1-4%, Low < 1%

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: Echo Class 1 for CHF, diastolic, continuous, holosystolic, late systolic murmurs, ejection clicks, radiation to neck, or murmurs with infarction, syncome, endocarditiis. MIBI(dobutamine/persantine): More sens/spec than stress test for ischemia Dobutamine Stress Echo: Best predictor of perioperative cardiac morbidity: cautions with serious arrhythmias, obesity, severe hyper/hypotension.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Consult Cardiology, Consider angiography, Cancel Surgery, Modifiy surgical procedure (less invasive), consider pre-op stenting.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
For PTCA surgery should be delayed  2 weeks to allow healing, and before 8 weeks (before restenosis) DES may require anti-platelet therapy for 6-12 months, vs BM stents which req 4 weeks.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Denervated Physiology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Pre-load dependent , altered response to medications : direct-acting (+); indirect-acting (-), pacemaker in 20%

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Allograft function

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Accelerated CAD : silent ischemia secondary to denervation, Rejection , Arrythmogenic , cardiac transplant vasculopathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Co-existing end-organ disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 renal dysfunction, HTN (~90%), DM, Malignancy (~30%)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Immunosuppression therapy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 steroids (stress dose), cyclosporine, tacrolimus, azathioprine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 inc. risk of infection; Anemia; Thrombocytopenia; hepato-nephrotoxicity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased risk of alloimmunization

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Use irradiated CMV negative blood

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals / Conflicts

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hemodynamic Goals

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Preload: normal or high preload - transplanted heart increases CO by increasing SV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Rhythm:  avoid pro-arrhythmic states

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Afterload:  maintain perfusion to potentially ischemic myocardium

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Use direct-acting sympathomimetics (isoproterenol & dilute epinephrine must be available)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid infection - adherence to strict sterile technique

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiac Transplant:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Heart transplant Hx (indication, surgical & medical compliations, pacemaker) / Functional capacity (rejection, arrythmias, CHF, CAD - dyspnea may be only symptom, no angina) / Mediactions (immuno - Cyclosporine / Tacrolimus: HTN, renal dysfunction, hepatotoxicity, seizure threshold, Azathioprine: bone marrow suppression) / co-existing disease (HTN, DM, renal dysfxn, malignancy) / infections PE: Vitals / Airway - cushingoid with inc. soft tissue / Resp - rule out infection / Cardiac - s/s of CHF (crackles, inc. JVP, hepatiomegaly, HJR, edema, S3/S4) Investigations: Labs - dec. K, Mg (diuretics, dysrhythmias), inc. Cr (anti-rejection drugs and renal insufficiency), inc. LFTs (anti-rejection drugs), Pancytopenia  (anti-rejection drugs or sepsis), glucose (steroids, DM), coags (dysfxn from drugs) / ECG - RAD, incomplete RBBB, pre-1994 - two P waves (native P unrelated to QRS), Q waves / CXR - failure / ECHO - LV/RV fxn / Dob stress ECHO for CAD (Exercise Stress Test not useful d/t blunted HR, MIBI not useful d/t diffuseness of disease) / Endomyocardial Bx Optimization: LV fxn - adequate preload, manage rejection & ischemia / Co-existing dysfunction - HTN, DM CRF / transplant MD to manage transplant medications / Steroids / Abx for prophylaxis if valvopathy Anesthetic Options: Local / Regional - check coags, maintain preload, direct acting vasopressors / GA - more predictable changes in preload & afterload, caution with renally excreted drugs, assess depth with BP not HR, avoid hyperventilation (cyclosporine and tacrolimus lower seizure threshold), Azathioprine antagonizes NdMB activity Room Setup: 5 lead, +- A-line, CVP based on Surgery, TEE based on preop fxn, PNS, crash cart, Drugs - Phenyl, isoproterenol (2-10 mcg/min) and dilute epinephrine (10 mcg/ml) Intraoperative Mgt: Aseptic, hemodynamically stable induction, use BP to monitor depth, avoid myocardial depression with high volatile / Ensure adequate reversal Post-op: continue anti-rejection Tx ASAP - consult transplant team Re: levels

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiogenic Shock

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiogenic Shock:  SBP < 90mmHG x 30 mins + Cardiac Index < 2.2L/min/m2 + PCWP >15mmHG

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency situation with potential for perioperative mortality (>50%)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Etiology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Acute MI - maximize myocardial O2 supply / demand

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medical therapy, IABP, VAD, invasive monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ii) Complications: CHF/Acute MR/Wall Rupture/Dysrhythmias

<!-- PAGE=? -->
iii) Early revascularization (PCI/CABG)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Systolic and/or diastolic HF, RVF , Valvular disease, Arrhythmias

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Co-morbid illnesses: HTN, DM, hyperlipidemia, Smoking, Advanced age, CVA, CKD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of bleeding 2◦ to thrombolytics, GIIb/IIIa inhibitors, LMWH/heparin, clopidogrel

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Resuscitation stabilizing ABC's, optimizing O2 suppy / demand, & maintaining end organ perfusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Early consideration for IABP/VAD/PCI/CABG

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hemodynamic goals: to maintain/augment contractility, NSR, avoid tachycardia, reduce afterload, and maintain adequate preload

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ventricular interdependence - fluids, inotropes, dec. PVR (avoid PPV ect.) in RVF

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Rule out other causes of shock - Hypovolemic, Distributive, Obstructive

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Diagnose mechanical complications that may necessitate urgent surgical intervention

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o MR, VSD, Free wall rupture

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Consult CVT & Cardiology - optimal revascularization technique given risk of postoperative bleeding

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Confirm etiology - cardiogenic vs. others - Focused cardiac history, sx of CP, CHF, dysrythmias, functional capacity. CRFs: DM/HTN/lipids/smoking, pvs revasc. + interventions + investigations. Check for contraindications for thrombolytics: pvs hemm. Stroke, known CNS neoplasm, active bleeding, susp. Aortic dissection, severe uncontrolled HTN, recent trauma, non-compressible vasc punctures, recent trauma. Check for contraindications to IAB: Severe vasc dx, AI, aortic aneurysm, irreversible cardiac/brain dmg. PE: Vitals, U/O, poor pulses and cap refill, cool, cyanotic extremities, inc. JVP, new murmurs S3 +/- S4, pulsus paradoxus from R heart failure; MR - high pitched apical holosystolic murmur; VSD - harsh holosystolic murmer LSB, O2 step-up on PA; Rupture - PEA arrest, tamponade (JVD, muffled HS, pulsus paradoxus) Investigations: CBC/Lytes/Ca+/Mg+/LFTs (congestion), Troponin, lactate, SVO2/ ABG, ECG (arrhythmia, ischemia), CXR (effusions edema), ECHO (valvular, VSD, rupture, effusion, EF), Consider urgent Angiography Optimization: Acute MI - Cardiology, MONA, If hemod stable - ASA, heparin / LMWH / BB blockers (avoid if CHF), ACE, NTG (for recurrent angina). Thrombolysis vs PTCA (90 mins) vs emerg CABG Shock: Nitrates and BBs contraindicated in shock. Invasive lines, IABP preoperatively, fluid challenge to PCWP 15-20mmHg for optimal CO, dopamine, dobutamine, Epinephrine, Milrinone. Optimize Hgb. Early intubate to reduce -WOB‖; FFP / octaplex if recently anticoagulated; Aspiration prophylaxis Room Setup: CAS 5lead + invasive lines (PAC); IABP; crash cart; Inotropes; Perfusion services; blood; TEE Intraoperative Mgt: Modified RSI (hemodynamics vs full stomach), ketamine/etomidate/opioid/roc. Post-op: ICU, opioid infusions for pain control in ICU vs boluses. Post-op cardiac monitoring. Complications: Arrhythmias (afib most common >10%), bradys, ventricular arrhythmias, Vfib 3-5% peaks within 4 hours of MI, MR due to pap rupture, Free wall rupture = 2 nd  most common cause of death post-MI (15- 30%) pks 1 weak post MI.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiomyopathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Classification: Dilated/Restrictive/Hypertrophic/Arrythmogenic RV cardiomyopathy (fibrofatty replacement of RV myocardium with sparing of LV/septum), risk of sudden death, RHF/unclassified

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of peri-operative Systolic/diastolic dysfunction with impaired CO

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations for underlying etiology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Dilated: Ischemia, HTN, Viral, ETOH, toxins, Idiopathic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Restrictive: Amyloidosis, Sarcoidosis, Hemoochromatosis, Idiopathic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
peripartum : Autoimmune, Idiopathic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
HCM: inherited, idiopathic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of perioperative complications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
MI, Ischemia, hypotension, arrhythmia, systemic embolism

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of dysrhthmias and considerations of pacemaker / AICD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of systemic embolism, and considerations of anticoagulation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Dilated: Maintain preload / avoid dec. contractility / maintain NSR / dec. afterload

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Restrictive: Maintain preload / maintain NSR / avoid brady / maintain afterload

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Peripartum: Maintain preload / avoid dec. contractility / maintain afterload while pregnant, dec. postpartum / maintain NSR / Titrated epidural (be mindful of anticoagulation)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Functional capacity, etiology, type of CM, investigations, sx's of CHF, substance abuse (EtOH/cocaine), medications, pacemakers/AICD settings, hx of embolic complications, hx of arrhythmias, conduction defects, valvular dysfunction. Systemic complications related to infiltrative disorders.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Pulse (prominent in HOCM), Displaced apical beat, LV heave (HOCM), S3 for CHF, S4 for infiltrative disorders. Regurgitant murmers for dilated CM, cresc-decrescendo SEM b/w apex and LSB for HOCM increasing with valsalva/standing ( ↓ preload). Exam findings of CHF/pHTN. Increased JVP with restrictive and fail's to fall during inspiration (Kussmaul's). Rapid x and y decent also seen in restrictive CM. Neuro. Investigations: CBC / Lytes (diuretics) /Cr (hypoperfusion) Coags/CXR (LV/LA enlargement)/ECG - HOCM (LVH, q waves, ST changes, arrhythmias), Dilated LVH/ST changes/BBB's, PVCs, Restrictive - BBBs, low voltage Echo - HOCM (SAM 25%), Dilated, decreased EF, restrictive, diastolic dysfunction, increased wall thickness, ↓ EF.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Cardiology consult, ? CTU for infiltrative/pacemaker/AICD management/ BB for HOCM Anesthetic Options: Caution with spinal/epidural with HOCM/consider regional Room Setup: Crash cart, pacing pads, invasive lines preinduction, 5 Lead ECG, TEE, PAC, inotropic meds Intraoperative Mgt: See hemodynamic goals above, consider cardiac induction, avoid SNS with HOCM. Post-op: HDU for cardiac monitoring/ischemia/hypotension/arrhythmias. Post-op pacemaker interrogation. Peri-partum CM: 4 criteria, develops within 6 months of preg after delivery, no identifiable cause, new diagnosis with no prior heart disease, ECHO shows findings of dilated CM (EF<45%). Unknown etiology, Possibel RF - multiple gestation, obesity, advanced maternal age, breat feeding; management similar to any form of HF. 20-80% Mortality.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CEA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
High risk of peri-operative complications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ischemic/hyperperfusion neurologic injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
cardiac ischemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
airway obstruction from hematoma / patch disruption

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Significant peri-operative hemodynamic changes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
X-clamp:  HTN, tachycardia, inc myocardial O2 demands

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Carotid sinus manipulation:  bradycardia, hypotension

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Co-existing medical illness (CAD, DM, HTN, PVD, CKD, smoking, advanced age)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications (ASA, plavix, antiHTN)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain stable hemodynamics to optimize perioperative cerebral perfusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Protect brain and heart from ischemic injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Smooth emergence:  avoid coughing, bucking, straining on emergence

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Awake patient at end of surgery for neuro assessment

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Carotid Stenting

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Remote location, comorbidity, perioperative complications (HD instability, Ischemic injury, a/w obstruction, MI), monitor for hyperperfusion syndrome postoperatively

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Sedation vs. GA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Carotid bruits, pre-existing neuro deficit, baseline BP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CBC, lytes, BUN, Cr, G&S, EKG, review doppler U/S to assess extent of stenosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Beta blockade, cont antiplatelet therapy, consider discontinuing ACEi, ARBs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 GA, regional, LA + MAC (no diff in postop stroke with RA vs GA) Room Setup: CAS (5 lead EKG), A-line, cerebral monitor (EEG, stump, SSEP, transcranial Doppler)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Induction / Maintenance:  minimize risk of hypoperfusion and cerebral ischemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Emergence:  minimize coughing (hematoma), traheal lido, IV lido, narcotics, deep extubation.  Have nitroglycerin/nitroprusside infusions, labetalol, hydralazine ready

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Complications - thrombosis, intraop CNS ischemia, ICH, hyperperfusion syndrome / respiratory depression / airway obstruction - hematoma, RLN injury / hypertension  - denervated carotid body / hypotension - baroreceptor hypersensitivity / Periop MI

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Carotid stenosis: asymptomatic, symptomatic, hx, freq, manisfestations of TIAs/CVAs.  Uni vs bilat

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Comorbidities:  CAD - MI is leading cause of periop morbidity post CEA, HTN - Inc risk of neuro deficits after CEA with pre-op HTN, PVD, DM, COPD, smoking

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Medications for CAD and CVA (antiplt, antiHTN)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Indications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Neck surgery including carotid endarterectomy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Nerves blocked:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 C2,3,4 nerve roots

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Contraindications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 General: Infection, Coagulopathy, lack of consent, true local anesthetic allergy, lack of resuscitation equipment

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Specific: Contra-lateral recurrent nerve injury (?contralateral phrenic nerve palsy?), severe lung disease (FEV1 < 1L)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Equipment:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Routine monitors and prep supplies

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 1.5 inch 25 gauge needle, 1.5 inch 22 gauge needle for insertion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cervical Plexus Block

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Technique:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Identify the mastoid process, Chassaignac's tubercle and the posterior border of the SCM.  Draw a line from the mastoid to Chassaignac's tubercle. The insertion points for C2, C3 and C4 can be estimated as being 2,4 and 6 cm below the mastoid along this line. Then infiltrate the skin under this entire line and then, at each of the three points along the line insert your 22 gauge needle until the transverse process is contacted (perpendicular to skin with a slight caudad angulation).
