At each level aspirate and then inject 4 cc.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Glossopharyngeal branches need to be blocked as well for a CEA. This can be done by having the surgeon infiltrate the carotid (NYSORA).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Direct trauma: pneumo, esophageal perforation, carotid or IJ puncture, hematoma Local anesthetic effects: inadvertent epidural, brachial plexus, intrathecal, intravenous or verterbral artery injection with associated seizures, phrenic nerve block, bradycardia or RLN dysfunction (60%)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Chronic Obstructive Lung Disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
High risk for perioperative respiratory complications including respiratory failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Physiologic changes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Chronic hypoxemia / hypercapnea

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cor pulmonale and RV failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Reactive airways disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Bullous lung disease with the potential need for lung isolation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for hyperinflation and pulmonary tamponade

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Comorbid disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CAD, DM, HTN, smoking, OSA, Obesity, Cancer, Cystic Fibrosis, Bronchiectasis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased sensitivity to respiratory depressant effects of anesthetic agents

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Ensure optimization of COPD - delay elective cases as required

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Manage acute infections, steroids, bronchodilators

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize ventilation strategy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Prevent dynamic hyperinflation and barotrauma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Long I:E, low Pk pressure, low VT slow rate, permissive hypercapnia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Minimize peri-operative respiratory complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Avoid use of respiratory depressants

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Consider neuraxial or regional anesthesia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Determine disease severity and functional capacity; Dyspnea, wheeze, cough and sputum production; CHF Sx; Fever; Home O2; Meds; Recent exacerbations; ETT; ICU; Steroids;  Co-morbidities PE: Resp: Tachypnea; Barrel chest; Resp distress (accessory Ms); A/E bilat; Prolonged Exp; Wheeze; Crackles; CVS: JVD; HJR;  Hepatomegally; Pedal edema; RV heave; S3 or S4; Loud P2 Investigations: CBC, LYTES, BUN/Cr, CXR, EKG Also consider: ABG, sputum C+S, PFT; ECHO (RV dysfx)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Postpone surgery 4-6 weeks after exacerbation; +/- respirology; antibiotics, steroids (stress dose), bronchodilators, d/c smoking in advance  (8 wk to Dec risk); avoid sedatives

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: RA preferred but risk of high neuraxial block & ISB will cause Phrenic paralysis  dec in FEV1 30%; GA results in dec. FRC, depression of respiratory drive; Consider TEA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: CAS + 5 Leads; Temp; PNS; Spirometry; A-line (CO2); TEE, PAC for Cor pulmonale; OLV equipment

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Deep  GA; Use Ketamine/propofol/Sevo; Lung protective strategies; Bullous disease (SV induction vs standard induction with OLV (unilat & severe bilat);

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Extubate awake; Pain control; PAR; Extubation criteria include:  VC > 10 cc/kg, Vt > 6 cc/kg,  NIP > 20 cmH20, pO2/FiO2 > 200, A-a pO2 gradient on 100 % O2 < 350 mmHg

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Auto-PEEP (pulm tamponade)  D/C fom Ventilator; Bronchospasm - volatile, B agonists, Mg, Ketamine; pneumothorax - chest tube, possible lung isolation;  Post op resp complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased risk of aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Dysregulation of volume status, acid-base, and electrolytes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
End-organ dysfunction:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Autonomic dysfunction: hemodynamic instability

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiac: LV dysfunction, HTN, CAD, CHF, pericarditis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hematologic: anemia / thrombocytopenia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Altered pharmacokinetics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Decreased drug excretion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Etiology of renal failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize electrolytes, volume status, co-morbidities

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid precipitating acute on chronic renal failure (euvolemia, avoid nephrotoxins)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Coordinate perioperative dialysis if dialysis dependent

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid compromising dialysis access (AV fistulas, indwelling IV lines, PD ports)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Recognize increased risk of renal failure in certain surgeries (cardiac, aortic , vascular)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Conflict:  RSI and HD instability (hTN, hypovolemia)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Chronic Renal Failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Etiology and co-morbidities: HTN, CAD, DM, severity of CRF, U/O (normal, oliguric, anuric) , end-organ dysfunction (exercise tolerance, angina, CHF, palpitations, dialysis (mode, frequency, complications, access, duration, dry weight), GERD, bleeding tendency: GI, epistaxis PE: Vitals - orthostatic, IV access (avoid subclavians), AV fistulae (avoid IVs and BP cuff), generalized edema, A/W edema, LVH, dysrhythmias, pericardial rubs, volume status, pulmonary edema, tachycardia (autonomic dysfunction) Investigations: CBC (anemia, dysfxnal plt), lytes (hyperK, hyperPO4, hypoCa, hyperMg, hypoNa), serum glucose, serum proteins (hypoalbuminemia), BUN (not a reliable indicator of GFR unless protein catabolism is normal and constant), Cr , ABG (for acidemia) , U/A, CrCl - <60 x 3mon = CKD Imaging: EKG (LVH is common, arrhythmias on the basis of electrolyte abnormalities), +/- ECHO Optimization: Defer if in ARF, Aspiration prophylaxis, dialysis timing (if chronic, dialyze day before.  If acute wait til postop if possible - reduced hemodynamic instability), Empty PD pts, diabetes management, blood conservation strategies (Uremic bleeding: cryoprecipitate, DDAVP (0.3 mcg/kg IV), if borderline function and high risk surgery for postoperative RF: generous preoperative hydration, possible use of mannitol intraoperatively Anesthetic Options: Local, regional, GA OK.  Regional may be difficult b/c of AV fistulae, also dysfxn'l plt. Reflux risk makes sedation or an LMA less attractive Room Setup: CAS (5 lead EKG), +/- A-line, CVP Intraoperative Mgt: Avoid nephrotoxins (aminoglycosides, dye, NSAIDs, ACEi, metformin), careful attention to dose and choice of opoids (avoid Demerol - judicious doses of morphine / hydromorphone - fentayl OK), Check K+ prior to sux, NdMB - cis-atracurium, avoid hypervolemia, delayed emergence Post-op : postop morbidity (acidosis, hyperkalemia, infections, hTN / HTN, bleeding, dysrhythmias, clotted fistulas).  Complications:  ARF, volume overload, electrolyte abN, periop CV complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cocaine Intoxication / Pregnancy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of Aspiration - full stomach

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multi-system effects

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Airway - septal necrosis, thermal epiglottis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CNS seizures , hemorrhagic/ischemic stroke, SAH, delirium, paranoia , cerebral edema

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CVS - HTN, MI, Dysrhythmia , Aortic dissection, cardiomyopathy (chonic use)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Resp - aspiration, pneumonitis, bronchospasm, pulmonary edema

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Renal - ARF (infaction, rhabdomyolysis)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Heme thrombocytopenia , DIC

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Interaction with Anesthetic - potential for SNS stimulation (avoid ketamine, atrop),MAC inc. with intoxication, normal with chronic use, variable response to vasopressers (use direct agents, small dose)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Co-intoxicants - EtOH, MJ, heroin, opioids, amphetamines

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complex pain management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential IVDU and blood-bourne infections

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cocaine effects in pregnancy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Maternal placental abruption , dec. uteroplacental perfusion, spontaneous abortion, premature labor, premature ROM, decreased plasma cholinesterase (dec. cocaine metabo)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Fetal - increased congenital abnormalities, IUGR, cardiomyopathy, MI, intra-cerebral bleeding, CNS irritability

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Supportive and hemodynamic management of acute cocaine intoxication

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Conflicts: Potentially full stomach (RSI) vs hemodynamically stable induction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Uncooperative patient / Thrombocytopenia with regional techniques

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Hz/duration of use, co-intoxicants, infectious disease, sequelae of use: stroke, MI, HTN, cardiomyopathy, pulmonary edema, bowel ischemia, renal failure, hepatic failure (hepatitis), bleeding, easy bruising. + Obstetric hx: prenatal care, abstinence, spont abortion, abruption, PROM, fetal well being, anomalies, IUFD, cardiomyopathy. R/o  coexisting PIH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Standard PE - vitals, focused on symptoms, FHR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: CBC, plts, lytes (RF), Coags if suspect liver failure, X-match (risk of abruption), Toxicology, TSH, ECG, CXR (pulm edema, infx, dissection), ECHO (cardiomyopathy), fetal U/S, NST, HR Optimization: -Delay if possible with acute intoxication - duration ~120 min HTN : 1 st  line benzo's 2 nd  line NTG/SNP/alpha blockade (phentolamine 1mg IV q3mins/hydralazine. No BB's HD stable VT or SVT: 1 st  line Benzo's 2 nd  line Lido(competes for Na+ channels), HCO3- 1-2meq/kg shows benefit in animals. CCB is controversial, verapamil 2.5-5mg IV over 2 mins q5-10 max 20 for rate control. Vfib or unstable VT: Defib/CPR > unknown role for Epi, Vasopressin preferred, Lido + HCO3 as per above, unknown role for amiodarone. Chest Pain: O2, monitors, 1 st  line Benzo's + NTG 2 nd  line phentolamine, ASA. 3 rd  consider CCB/labetolol. Anesthetic Options: All possible if cooperative, consider thrombocytopenia, hypotension with neuraxial Consider HTN with SNS activation Room Setup: CAS + 5lead, large bore IV, artline , Temp (hyperthermia), vasoactive meds, FHR mont Nitro 0.5-1mcg/kg/min, SNP 0.3-10mcg/kg/min, verapamil 2.5-5mg over 2 mins q5-10mins (max 20). Intraoperative Mgt: Increased MAC, deep laryngoscopy, pre-treat HTN , Avoid SNS drugs (ketamine/atropine/potent volatiles), used direct vasoactive meds (smaller dose phenyl)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Ongoing monitoring, risk of arrhythmias, MI, withdrawl, hard to manage pain

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CO Poisoning/Smoke Inhalation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for evolving respiratory compromise

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 loss of airway from edema/obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 ALI / ARDS

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Coexisting injuries - Burns & trauma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CO and/or CN poisoning

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Sepsis, Rhabdomyolysis, lactic acidosis, Renal failure, Thrombocytopenia, Consumptive coagulopathy, Electrolyte disturbances

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Rapidly assess need to establish definitive airway - 1 or more are present:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Stridor

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ii) Use of accessory respiratory muscles

<!-- PAGE=? -->
iii) Respiratory distress

<!-- PAGE=? -->
iv) Hypoxia or hypercapnia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Deep burns to the face or neck

<!-- PAGE=? -->
vi) Blistering or edema of the oropharynx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Support oxygenation with 100% O2, consider HBO chamber early

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Volume resuscitation as required

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Events surrounding the inhalation injury, Closed-space environment, Type of fuel (plastics), Sx's of dyspnea, change in voice,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Vitals (inaccurate SaO2 with COHb), A/W exam: singed nasal hairs/eyebrows, cutaneous burns on head/neck/torso. Carbonaceous sputum. Resp: edema, wheeze. CVS: dysrthymias.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: CBC, lytes, BUN, Cr, glucose, lactate, ABG: PaO2, SaO2, carboxy-Hb level (co-oximetry) CN level, Anion gap. CXR (often initially normal) FOB (96% PPV of findings if COHb>10%, closed-space fire, and carbonaceous sputum.  Look for: erythema, edema, ulceration of the airways, and carbonaceous debris.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Early intubation, High FiO2 (especially if concomitant CO or CN poisoning), Parkland formula 4 ml/kg / BSA burned, Give ½ in first 8 hrs and the rest over the next 16 hours (underestimates requirements of infants < 10 kg - use 6 ml/kg/% burned per 24 hrs); overly aggressive resuscitation can worsen supraglottic edema, Bronchodilators. Steroids are ineffective and can increase the risk of infection

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
depends on pt's condition, often early ETT/  FiO2

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CAS monitors, uncut ETT, FOB/Difficult Airway cart

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 FiO2 for CO treatment

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op : post-op ventilation until recovery from airway/lung injury and edema

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complex Regional Pain Syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Chronic pain with its associated psychological, cognitive, and behavioural effects

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Requires accurate diagnosis while ruling out other pathology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Initial presentation represents a relative medical emergency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Need for early, aggressive, multimodal therapy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications associated with CRPS

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Opiate tolerance

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Primary Goal is return of function

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Assessment:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 General Categories: Sensory, Motor, Vasomotor (temp, colour), and Sudomotor (fluid balance)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hx : initiating event, severity and duration of symptoms, previous treatments and their impact, rule out other etiologies (malignancy, infection etc…), functional impact

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Px : Vitals, allodynia, hyperalgesia, skin colour and temperature,  hyperhidrosis, presence of skin atrophy, nail and hair changes, edema, joint stiffness, muscle weakness, dystonias

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Etiology:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Trauma, neurologic insults, HSV, MI;

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk Factors:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
female, trauma, nerve injury, WCB, surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
EMG, sweat tests, 3 phase bone scan, XRay, MRI/CT, diagnositic sympathetic blocks

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Treatment:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Early referral to specialist, Multiple modalities with goal of facilitating physio/OT - TCA, gabapentin, opioids, non-opioids (prazosin, clonidine, phentolamine, NMDA antagonists), TENS, IVRA, sympathetic blocks, neuraxial treatment (SCS, intrathecal pumps), surgery (sympathectomy)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Conn's Syndrome (hyperaldosteronism)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypertension and end-organ dysfunction:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiac dysfunction, CVA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Fluid and electrolyte abnormalities

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Volume overload

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypernatremia, Hypokalemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications: Spironolactone

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Perioperative normalization of fluid and electrolyte status

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Perioperative control of hypertension

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Unstable C-spine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Urgent/Emergent airway management with risk of aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Difficult airway management: limited cROM, other head and neck trauma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prevention of secondary spinal cord injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Airway management, transfers and positioning

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hard collar, manual in-line stabilization, Mayfield pins, full spine precautions

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Predisposing Comorbidies: Congential  /Acquired / Trauma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Acute pinal cord injury (if appropriate)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Neurogenic shock

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Respiratory insufficiency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Succinylcholine contraindicated

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Loss of thermal regulation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Adequate preoperative identification and optimization of unstable cervical spine if elective surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Safely secure airway with prevention of secondary spinal cord injury through immobilization during airway  management, transfers and positioning

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential conflicts:  Uncooperative, intoxicated or pediatric patient vs. awake FOI

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Identify etiology and screen for associated comorbidities, aspiration risk fx, if trauma other injuries PE: Vitals, airway exam (mouth opening, dentition, TMD, neurological symptoms with neck mov't if appropriate), usual CVS  and respiratory exams

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Consider any of lateral neck film (flex/ex if appropriate), 3 views (lateral, AP, open mouth

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: odontoid), CT neck.  Ant ADI > 4-5mm abnormal.  MRI  useful for ligamentous injuries. Optimization: Aspiration prophylaxis or fasting as appropriate, glycopyrrolate

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: Spine stabilization during airway management and positioning through manual in-line stabilization (MILS), awake FOI, Mayfield pins (after intubation).  FOI with NETT may be technique of choice; DL with MILS  also acceptable for emergency cases. DL associated with maximal movement at odontoid-C1/2. Cricoid controversial (risk of aspiration vs. displacement of c-spine).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Difficult airway cart,skilled assistants, consider ENT surgeon present.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Dexamethasone may decrease airway edema

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Consider postop ventilation/ICU in head up position or extubation over tube exchanger depending on degree of airway edema, prone positioning and instrumentation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DDx: Congenital (Down's syndrome - 15%, odontoid abn, mucopolysaccharidoses), Acquired (RA-30%, Still's disease, ankylosing spondylitis, psoriatic arthritis, Crohn's/UC, Reiter's Syndrome) and Trauma (odontoid #, other bony #, ligamentous disruption, 5% of TBI have a c-spine injury)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
No c-spine imaging acceptable after trauma if:  A & O; no head injury; no intoxication; no neck pain; no abn neurology; no distracting injury; neck examination normal

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Croup/ Laryngotracheobronchitis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Acute but self-limiting viral infection causing narrowing of subglottic structures and rarely airway compromise requiring intubation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pediatric patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Association with bacterial trachieitis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Airway obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals / Conflicts

<!-- PAGE=? -->
safely secure airway if necessary

<!-- PAGE=? -->
avoid precipitatnts of complete airway obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
r/o other conditions

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx & Px

<!-- PAGE=? -->
6 mo to 6 yo; onset 12 hours to 3 days; low grade fever/ generally do not appear toxic; barking cough; coryza, rhinorrhea

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations

<!-- PAGE=? -->
AP neck films: -steeple‖ sign (not specific); CBC, blood cultures

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 intubation rarely  istula

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 humidified air/cool mist

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 nebulized epi 0.5 ml/kg of 1:1000 max 5 ml (racemic no longer available) q15-20 min

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 dex 0.6mg/kg PO

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 nebulized budesonide (2 mg [2 mL solution] via nebulizer)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 heliox

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Disposition

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PICU

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Can generally be extubated in 4-7 days after confirmation of leak, resolution of other symptoms

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Extubate in OR after visualization

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cushing's Syndrome (hypercortisolism)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Difficult airway: Obesity / OSA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Coexisting Disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Cardiac:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o HTN / Volume overload (increased renin and glucocorticoid vascular reactivity)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o LVH, pHTN/RVF, systolic and diastolic dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CNS: Psychosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Meabolic:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypokalemic metabolic alkalosis - mineralcorticoid affect of glucocorticoids

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o DM - insulin deficiency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Osteoporosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential difficult IV access

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Perioperative Steroid replacement

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pharmacologic considerations: Sensitivity to NMB, catecholamines

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations of pituitary tumours (4M's)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Minimize risk of adrenal insufficiency during perioperative stress, particularily during resection of pituitary

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cyanotic Heart Disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Right to Left Shunt (Qp:Qs < 1) (TOF, tricuspid/pulmonary atresia, TGV, truncus arteriosus, TAPVR, hypoplastic Lt Heart)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Shunt dependent on RVOT obstruction and PVR / SVR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Optimize CO and tissue oxygenation by balancing SVR and PVR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Chronic hypoxemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o pHTN & cor pulmonale

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Polycythemia - risk of thrombosis with HCT > 55, avoid dehydration and Fe deficiency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Risk of paradoxical air embolus (prevent air in IV, avoid N2O)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Treatment: Maintain PDA, palliation with BT shunt + Glenn / Fontan vs. primary repair

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 General - dec. growth, developmental delay, increased metabolic rate

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Cardiac  - hypertrophy, arrhythmias, RV failure with ischemia, volume overload with CHF

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Pulmonary

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Dec. PBF:  TOF, Tricuspid or Pulm atresia w/o VSD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Inc. PBF:  TGV, hypoplastic L heart, TAPVR, Truncus

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Heme (polycythemia, hyperviscosity, coagulopathy - dec. Vit K)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CNS (brain abscess)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Assess anatomy/surgical repair/residual shunts and ventricular function

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 SBE prophylaxis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Associated syndromes (Down's) + defects (craniofacial, skeletal, GI / GU)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
1. Hemodynamic goals:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o TOF : full preload, high SVR, low PVR, low contractility, low HR, avoid dehydration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o BT shunts : PBF dependent on MAP and PVR - maintain SpO2 <85% - balance of systemic and pulmonary blood flow - avoid high FiO2 / hyperventilation- pulmonary vasodilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Fontan : PBF / CO depends on preload and PVR Full preload, low PVR, normal SVR (prevent R - L shunt), N contractility, and NSR (dec. pulmonary venous congestion)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Consider factors that increase PVR : hypercarbia, hypoxia, acidosis, SNS stimulation, lung hyperinflation (PVR is lowest when lung is at FRC  large Vt and low freq), increased HCT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid air bubbles (important for R to L shunts)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid hypothermia (left shift of O2Hb curve - less available O2, Plt dysfunction, hyperviscosity and metabolic acidosis)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ANESTHETIC GOALS:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pathophysiology: Incidence: 8:1000 live births; 25% have other abnormality; 8.5% syndromic (most commonly w/ endocardial cushion defect, VSD, TOF)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Clinical diagnosis, surgical repair, residual lesions; Functional status ; weight gain if infant; NYHA classification; Prolonged intubation (subglottic stenosis); Strokes (hyperviscosity syndrome in cyanotic lesions); Associated syndromes (Down's, VACTERL, DiGeorge); Medications: inotropes, diuretics, afterload reducers, digoxin (0.8-2 ng/mL therapeutic)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Px: weight, height, VS, SaO2, cyanosis, clubbing; signs of CHF (elevated JVP, pedal edema, crackles, tachypnea, hepatomegaly in infants), BP descrepancies (coarctation); inc. WOB (nasal flaring, increase RR, chest retractions, accessory muscle use); Shock - cap refill, peripheral perfusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Inv: If repaired lesion, doing well, on no medications → only routine investigations dictated by the surgical procedure; If uncorrected lesion: CBC Polycythemia in cyanotic lesions (Hb = 200 g/L) - Consider phlebotomy; Thrombocytopenia; Coags ( coagulopathy 2 nd  to low levels of vitamin K dependent factors); Lytes if on diuretic, digoxin, history of arrhythmia; ABG if cyanosis or respiratory failure; Imaging: EKG, CXR, ECHO : define anatomy of lesion, exclude other lesions, cath

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Clear fluids to 2 hrs preoperatively, optimize preload, SBE prophylaxis, anxiolysis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: Local vs. regional vs. general depending on lesion and procedure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Setup: Emergency drugs; CAS monitors; NIBP and IV on opposite side of shunts; capnography: dead space will underestimate PaCO2 in R → L shunts; Consider A-line, CVP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Management: Regional - Consider the type of cardiac lesion (decreased SVR in TOF undesirable); Improves peripheral blood flow, decreased DVT, reduced perioperative blood loss; Coagulation status

<!-- PAGE=? -->
General anesthesia: Slower inhalation, faster IV induction, potential for overdose in R → L shunts; Ketamine useful: minimal myocardial dysfunction, maintains SVR, little effect on PVR; Avoid N2O; Avoid high PAPs and PEEP in patients with decreased pulmonary blood flow; PEEP may be of value in patients with high pulmonary blood flow (truncus arteriosus, TAPVR); Early extubation may be appropriate in patients with uncomplicated anesthetic and surgical courses

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Disposition & Monitoring: Depends on lesion/repair/procedure; Most will require some type of post-op monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cyanotic Neonate

<!-- PAGE=? -->
O2 responsive  Hyaline membrane disease, Meconium aspiration, GBS pneumonia, PTX, Diaphragmatic hernia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Not O2 responsive - PPHN, Truncus Arteriosus, TAPVR, TGA, Ebstein's anomaly, Right heart obstruction including TOF (may present late unless severe RVOT obstruction)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PDA dependant lesions

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Systemic Flow: Coarctation, Interrupted aortic arch, Hypoplastic left heart, Critical aortic stenosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Shock: Poor distal perfusion with closure of ductus

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Pulmonary Flow: Tricuspid/Pulmonary atresia, RVOT obstruction (pulmonary stenosis, TOF)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cyanosis: R to L shunt with ductus closure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Management: Depends on age of presentation and clinical manifestations

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o R to L shunts - goal is to increase pulmonary blood flow

<!-- PAGE=? -->
If duct dependent: start PGE

<!-- PAGE=? -->
If not duct dependent; balance between PVR and SVR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Shock - goal is to improve systemic cardiac output

<!-- PAGE=? -->
If duct dependent: start PGE

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o CHF - Implies L to R shunt with increased pulmonary blood flow and volume overload - need to decrease pulmonary blood flow

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Supportive - Intubation, Glucose: can become hypoglycemic d/t hepatic congestion, Consider bicarbonate to improve metabolic milieu, PGE1

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cystic Fibrosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of aspiration - GERD, Mechanical ileus

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of perioperative resp dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Mixed obstructive and RLD with potential for pHTN, RVF, and cor pulmonale

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Thick secretions; chronic pneumonia; bronchiectasis; bullous disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Inc. risk of periop pulmonary complication: hypoxemia, bronchospasm, PTX, massive hemoptysis, resp failure requiring ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Other Co-morbidities : Malnutrition with anemia or chronic disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Coagulopathy - Vit K deficiency, obstructive hepatobiliary dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Pancreatic insufficiency with DM

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Meds: O2, insulin, Bronchodilators, Steroids, mucolytics, Abx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Postop: pain management; aggressive resp therapy; HDU/ICU

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Minimize periop pulmonary complications: optimization of preoperative respiratory function, hydration, and control of secretions; Lung protection ventilation strategies; avoid bronchospasm;; pain control

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Minimize lung contamination (hemoptysis or abscess)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid precipitants of pHTN

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Conflicts: emergency surgery in CF with active infection & regional anesthesia in the setting of potential coagulopathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx & PE: severity of Cardiopulmonary disease - vitals with SaO2, inc. WOB, dyspnea, cyanosis, Clubbing, orthopnea, adventitia, hyperinflation, infection, pHTN & RV failure (edema, inc. JVP, S3/S4,  P2, heave), functional status; GI Diease - cachexia, GERD, hepatic dysfunction (jaundice, coagulopathy), bowel obstruction; Other Organs - DM Current Treatment : physio, O2, bronchodilators, mucolytics, steroids, Abx, insulin/PO hypoglycemics Investigations: CBC; Lytes; Ur; Cr; Glucose; Coags; LFT; Sputum C/S; ABG; CXR/CT; ECG plus ECHO if evidence of pHTN; PFTs (inc. RV, FRC; dec. FEV1,PEF, FEV1/FRC, VC) Optimization: Consults (resp, cardio, endo, peds, ICU); Delay elective surgery if active infection; Pulmonary function - chest phsyio and postural drainage, Abx, Bronchodolators, steroids; cardiac meds; correct coagulopathy; aspiration prophylaxis Anesthetic Options: LA vs RA vs GA or GA/RA Room Setup: CAS monitors + 5-Lead ECG, PNS,  Art line, +/-CVP & TEE if pHTN & RV dysfx; Meds: vasopressors, pulm vasodilators, bronchodilators, large ETT, suction catheter, DLT, FOB, Chest tube Avoid: Anticholinergics; ketamine, nasal intubation Intraoperative Mgt: PreO2 with RSI; spont ventilation if bullous disease; use short acting NMB and anesthetics (remi) ; frequent suctioning; lung protective ventilation strategy (minimize PIP, long E time); Avoid precipitants of pHTN; avoid long acting resp depressants Emergence : Crisp emergence; completely reversed & suctioned prior extubation; pain control with adjuvants; Post-op: HOB 30-40 o , Resume aggressive Chest physio; Monitor in HDU for periop pulm complication Complications: Hemoptysis; PTX; Post induction cardiopulmonary collapse (hypoxemia, PPV, pHTN, RVF); Hypoxemia; High PAP; Failure to wean Special: 1:30 carrier; 1:3000 births CF: autosomal recessive mutation of CF gene on Ch 7; Abn CFTR (Cl channel  thick secretion; plugging of Exo glands

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DDx:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Drugs - absoulte or relative overdose

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Volatile, Hypnotics, Narcotics, Nonanesthetics - Phenothiazines, α 2 agonists, TCA, NdMBs, illicit drugs, ETOH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Infections

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Encephalitis, Meningitis, abscess, Sepsis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Metabolic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypoxia / hypercarbia, Hypo/hyperglycemia , myxedema coma, adrenal insufficiency, Electrolytes (Sodium, Calcium, Magnesium), Toxins (Uremia, hepatic encephalopathy)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypothermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Structural

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o CVA, ICH, Tumor, Cerebral edema, Postictal, hydrocephalus, pneumocephalus, hypoperfusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Severe pain

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Most frequent causes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Relative Overdose, Incr'd sensitivity (extremes of age), Drug interactions, Hepatic/renal disease,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Consider opioids, MAOi's, NdMBs, acidosis, Mg, drugs that potentiate NdMBs, recent withdrawal from EtOH or illicit drugs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Pediatrics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hypoxemia, Ingestion, Meningitis, TBI (abuse)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Delayed Emergence

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Management:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Inform surgeon

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Ensure the patient is hemodynamically stable with adequate axygenation and ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Scan monitors for HR, rhythm, EtCO2, SaO2, cycle BP, Etagent, temperature

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Ensure that all anesthetic agents, volatile and IV are stopped

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Stimulate obtunded patient, restrain combative patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Diagnosis and treat metabolic derangement

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Blood glucose , electrolytes, ABG

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Review medications and dosages - Check for syringe or ampule swap

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Consider reversing specific agents

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Naloxone - 0.04mg IV titrated to effect

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Flumazenil - 0.2mg q 1 min titrated to effect (max 3mg/hr)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Physostigmine - 1mg q 3 min titrated to effect (max 4mg)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hx & Px including neurologic evaluation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o collateral history, chart review (drugs, diabetes, lytes, injuries, infection, seizures, endocrinopathy, renal/hepatic impairment); -at risk‖ procedure (bypass, open ventricle, CEA, craniotomy). Anesthetic - duration, drugs, doses

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Focal neurologic findings - PERL, corneals, gag, Limb reflexes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Investigations: CBC, lytes, glc, BUN, Cr, Mg, Ca, PO4, LFTs, blood/urine culture, tox screen, TSH, fT4, Serum osmolality, lactate, ABGs, ECG, CXR, CT head, consider LP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Early consultation with neurology or neurosurgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 If no improvement, arrange transport to ICU for continued care

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Etiology and Co-existing Disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Neurogenic - posterior pituitary surgery, tumour, head trauma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Nephrogenic - CRF, drug induced (Lithium), fluoride toxicity, hypoK, hyperCa, sickle cell anemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 DDx of hypernatremia- (any cause of excessive water loss, renal disease, mineralocorticoid excess, hypertonic NG feeds)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hemodynamic instability due to volume depletion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypernatremia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Thirst, altered LOC, lethargy, Seizures, Coma, Hypovolemia, Shock

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 risk of ICH from acute, severe hypernatremia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 risk of correction (cerebral edema, volume overload, water intoxication)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Preoperative normalization of serum sodium when possible: correct < 0.5 mEq/hour

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o IV fluid, DDAVP (neurogenic), Chlorpropamide (nephrogenic)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Restore intravascular volume

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o replace ongoing losses with hypotonic IV solution

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Treat underlying etiology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Diabetes Insipidus

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: U/O > 100ml/hr of dilute urine with hypernatremia. Search for etiology:  surgical history (esp. pituitary), toxicities, renal failure, trauma; symptoms of DI & hypernatremia; previous treatment medications (Lithium, glyburide, ampho B, methoxyflurane), electrolytes (hypoK, hyperC, sickle cell anemia), PE: Vitals, postural BP, volume status, focused neurological exam for localizing signs, signs of trauma, other pituitary abnormalities Investigations: Serum and Urine lytes, urine osmolality < 300mOsm/L and serum Na > 150, urine specific gravity < 1.002, Renal function, Calcium (hypercalcemia), Other hormonal deficiencies, CT head for CNS etiology; Water deficit = TBW x ( [Na]/140 - 1) Optimization : aim for euvolemic but avoid rapid correction (replace water deficit with hypoosmolar fluid (D5W) over 24-48 hrs, not more than 0.5-1 mEq/L/hr), DDAVP for Neurogenic DI (1-3ug IV bid, 5-20ug IN bid), d/c offending drugs. Nephrogenic DI - chlorpropamide 200-500mg/d (potentiates renal effects of vasopressin, A/E hypoglycemia), clofibrate, carbamazepine- enhances vasopressin secretion, HCTZ- potentiates renal effects of ADH Anesthetic Options : none preferred. Note: higher MAC with hypernatremia Room Setup: vasopression (.1-.2U/hr infusion), consider Art line to monitor Na, foley, Consider CVP to monitor volume status Intraoperative Mgt: Fluid management - NS bolus to euvolemia, maintanence plus 2/3 previous hour U/O as D51/2NS, if hourly fluids >400ml, add DDAVP, consider vasopression infusion Post-op: Hemodynamic instability, intracranial hemorrhage, water intoxication from therapy, Cerebral edema

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Diabetes Mellitus

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential difficult airway with risk of aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
stiff joint, obesity, autonomic neuropathy (gastroparesis)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
End-organ dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Macrovascular - CAD, HTN, PVD, CVD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Microvascular - nephropathy, retinopathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Neuropathy - peripheral, autonomic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased perioperative risk

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Related to end organ dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Related to DM and its treatment

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypo/hyperglycemia, DKA, HONK

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Periop management of oral hypoglycemic and/or insulin

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Identify and optimize end-organ dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize perioperative glycemic control - 6.5-10 mmol/L

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o hold oral hypoglycemic, ½ NPH dose - 100cc/hr D5W, avoid extremes of hypo-/ hyperglycemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid and manage glycemic complications - DKA, hypokalemia, hypoglycemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
OB Considerations : inc. maternal risk (DKA, difficult A/W, aspiration, nerve injury, hypoglycemia, PIH, polyhydramnious, preterm, infection c-section, dystocia,); Fetal risk - CVS, CNS, GI

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: DM type and duration, meds, insulin, Glycemic control (average BS, HbA1C), Previous episodes of DKA/HONK; End-organ disease (CAD, HTN, PVD, CKD, CVD), Functional Capacity , Neuropathy (have they seen ophthalmology)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: VITALS (postural), Airway assessment (Stiff joint syndrome, prayer sign); Focused physical based on history of associated co-morbidities (cardiac / CNS); Autonomic neuropathy hypotension, absent beat-beat variation in HR with breathing, prolonged QT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
autonomic (orthostatic hTN, lack of HR variability) and peripheral (burning pain, parasthesia); Retinopathy - resting tachycardia, orthostatic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Inv: CBC , lytes, Ur, Cr (renal insufficiency), fasting glucose, ECG; cardiac work-up as per AHA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: end-organ dysfunction, Management of meds - stop metformin 48hrs preop, hold hypoglycemic, ½ NPH dose and give D5W preop; glycemic control , 1st case of day, involve endocrine if brittle; consider B-blockers as per AHA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Options: Neuroaxial (reduced stress response, but reduced insulin secretion); higher risk of neuropathy with regional (worse with epi); GA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: CAS +5 lead; Art line (sampling, neuropathy); Direct acting agents if autonomic neuropathy, glucometer -consider IV insulin infusion to maintain BS 5.0-11 mmol/L; Appropriate airway preparation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: neuropathy)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Glucose intra-op monitoring - avoid hypoglycemia; Appropriate padding (prone to dependant on case and comorbidity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications :  Periop MI, ARF, hypoglycemia , DKA, HONK, autonomic instability, infection, sepsis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DKA & HONK

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DKA in type I DM, NKH in type II DM - Both due to precipitating event: hypovolemia, trauma, infection, MI, CVA, pancreatitis, drugs (diuretics). HONK - no ketones due to residual basal insulin secretion which impairs lipolysis.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency situation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
aspiration risk, limited time for optimization

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Metabolic derangement

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hyperglycemia with dehydration, hyperosmolarity and coma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Metabolic acidosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Electrolyte disturbances - hypokalemia, hyponatremia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations of DM (neuropathy, nephropathy, airway, CAD)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of cerebral edem with rapid reduction in serum osmolality

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Volume replacement with NS until end-organ perfusion restored

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o 1-2 L in DKA; 3-8L in HONK

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Humulin R 0.1U/kg bolus then Humulin R 0.1U/kg/hr infusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Continue insulin until anion gap resolved - switch to D51/2NS when BS 15 mmol/L

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Monitor Na & replace total water deficit over 24-48 hr - urine output as a guide

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Start KCl infusion (40mEq/L) when U/O > 0.5ml/kg/hr, and K < 4.5

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Monitor glucose q30-60min; lytes, AG and Phosphate q 60 min - phosphate will need repleation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Identify etiology (sepsis, MI, poor compliance, new diagnosis)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Standard DM history when applicable; usually precipitated by poor patient compliance with insulin; hx of any precipitating factors; symptoms - polyuria, polydipsia, wt loss, lethargy, visual changes, stupor, coma, Sz, N/V, abd pain, fruity odor on breath

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Vitals (posturals - osmotic diuresis and vomiting); Kussmauls respirations (severe acidosis); Decreased LOC, coma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: CBC (polycythemia), lytes (Hyperglycemia (HONK > DKA), metabolic acidosis  with anion gap (pH< 7.3, HCO3 < 15) hyponatremia with hyperosmolarity, hyperkalemia initially  hypokalemia with treatment, hypophosphatemia), Cr (ARF), osmolarity, urine ketones,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
treat the DKA before O.R. unless an emergency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: continue to manage the DKA with appropriate infusions

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
HDU for intensive monitoring of electrolytes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypokalemia, Hypophosphatemia, Cerebral edema

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Disseminated Intravascular Coagulation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Widespread systemic activation of coagulation  intravascular thrombosis & consumptive coagulopathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency situation with  high mortality requiring urgent evaluation and management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multisystem complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Bleeding (ICH, tamponade, hemothorax, hematuria, surgical wounds etc.)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Thromboembolism (CNS ischemia, ARF, ARDS, PE, liver failure)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations for underlying etiology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Sepsis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Trauma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
obstetrical conditions (AFE, inutero death, abruption, pre-eclampsia)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Diagnose and treat underlying cause

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Replace consumed coagulation factors/platelets and lost RBCs as required

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Support multi-organ system failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: AMPLE, details of critical illness

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Vitals, GCS, Airway, CV-Resp exam, look for bleeding, end-organ failure - dec. LOC, shock, ARDS, ARF, liver dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: CBC, coags, fibrinogen, FDPs, D-dimer, ABGs, ECG, CXR; DIC is suggested by a clinical condition consistent with DIC, thrombocytopenia (< 100 x 109/L), prolonged PT and aPTT, presence of FDP/D-dimer

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Correct underlying etiology and physiologic derrangment, Plt>50, FFP to keep INR<1.5-2, Cry to keep fibrinogen>1.5, PRBC to maintain perfusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: Standard CAS, large bore IV, fluid warmer, +/- Artline & CVP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: GA, Neuraxial contraindicated.  Potential conflict of need for RSI with possible hemodynamic collapse on induction.  Need for continued supportive management, keep up with consumptive coagulopathy, keep warm, repeated intra-op bloodwork.  Replacement of factors/blood when needed.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Ongoing coagulopathy, likely need SPAR/ICU setting

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Special: Complications include massive hemorrhage, ongoing bleeding, and multi-organ failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Difficult Airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Expected difficult intubation 2° to history and/or physical

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Previous anesthetics, Hx of OSA, radiation to head and neck, tumours of head and neck, previous longterm intubation (stenosis); short -bull‖ neck, prominent incisors, limited ROM of neck or TMJ, pregnancy, congenital syndromes, airway infections, trauma, anaphylaxis, morbid obesity, obvious anatomical abnormalities, stridor, subcutaneous emphysema, blood in oro- nasopharynx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Assess for difficult surgical a/w (obesity, tumor, burns, dec. neck mobility)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Consider alternatives to GA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Airway management will still be a problem if complications arise

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prepare basic airway equipment plus contingency plan

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Multiple blades and ETT sizes, stylet, bougie, lightwand, glydscope, LMA +/- fastrac,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Equipment for transtracheal jet ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Readily available and connected to O2 source

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o FOB; Cricothyrotomy set and skilled clinician; Consider CPB standby

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Perform awake intubation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Judicious IV sedation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Conflict btw cooperative patient and awake patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Topicalize airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 0.2 mg glycopyrrolate

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 5cc 4% cocaine with 15cc 4% lidocaine in atomizer

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Base of tongue, tonsilar pillars, posterior pharyngeal wall, hypoparynx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Lidocaine to vocal cords

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Awake direct laryngoscopy - If adequate view, induction, paralytics, intubate

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Fiberoptic laryngoscopy - Induction once ETT confirmed in position

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Lightwand - Upright patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Failed intubation - two failed attempts by experienced clinician

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Emergency situation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Call for help and difficult intubation cart

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Multiple blades and ETT sizes, stylet, bougie, lightwand, glydscope, LMA +/- fastrac,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Equipment for transtracheal jet ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Readily available and connected to O2 source

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o FOB

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Cricothyrotomy set and skilled clinician

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Attempt to mask ventilate with 100 % O2

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Adequate

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 wake patient and either cancel or proceed as with expected difficult intubation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 if NdMR given optimize position, equipment, and clinicain

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Inadequate mask ventilation (oral airway, two person)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o LMA placement → adequate?

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o If inadequate move to emergency cricothyrotomy, or tracheostomy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications :  damage to airway, bleeding, airway obstruction, hypoxemia, esophageal intubation, gastric distention and regurgitation/aspiration, C-spine injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Airway abnormalities

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Difficult BMV - macroglossia, Choanal atresia / narrow nasopharynx, prominent tonsils & adenoids (population risk of difficult intubation - 0.5%)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Subglottic stenosis - require a half-size smaller ETT than predicted by age

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Possible unstable C-spine - 31% A-A (20% asympt) and A-O instability

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Congenital Heart Disease (40%)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
AV canal defects (50%), VSD (~25%), secundum ASD, PDA, Tetralogy of Fallot (4%)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Accelerated CAD, adult onset valvular disease, SBE prophylaxis, Bubble-free IVs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
OSA - sensitive to respiratory depressants; risk of pHTN and RV failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Uncooperative patient - Developmental Delay, Early onset Dementia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Associated conditions: DM, Hypothryoid, Obesity, Cataract's, Reccurant Otitis Media, Immune Deficiency, Duodenal atresia, difficult IV access

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Identify presence of A-A instability and manage the A/W safely

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Identify and manage comorbidity that inc. perioperative risk

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o OSA, post-op stridor - minimize respiratory depressants, post-op monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o CHD, pHTN, DM

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Down's Syndrome Incidence: 1 in 800 livebirths.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: History of OSA, C-spine instability (neck pain, altered fine motor, gait, B&B, vertigo, syncope). Cardiac evaluation, functional capacity, mental capacity, previous surgeries. Co-existing disease: Cataracts, recurrent OM, hypothyroid, DM, Duodenal Atresia, TEF, Hirschsprung's disease, leukemia, GERD/aspiration PE: A/W examination, AAI > neurologic symptoms (spasticity, gait, neck tenderness), cardiac exam: heart failure, pHTN (Loud P2, RV Heave, JVP), PDA - Harsh Holosystolic murmer LSB (VSD) vs continous at LSB. ToF - Cyanosis, clubbing, palpable LSB heave (RVH), systolic ejection murmur (LUSB), loud A2, IV Access Investigations: ECG, ECHO

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op complications: obstruction, stridor, bronchospasm, Severe bradycardia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
BW & TSH as dictated by Sx, Flex/ex c-spine (no screening, new symptoms, ENT procedure), Optimization: Cardiac Consultation, Resp consult for sleep study/overnight oximetry. Neck xrays preoperatively; if neuro sympts - delay and refer to NSx; c-spine precautions; Midazolam (0.5mg/kg max 20mg) may have unpredictable response - monitor for A/W obstruction, IM Ketamine for uncooperative patient, antisialogogue (glyco 0.01mg/kg), EMLA cream for IV placement, SBE Prophylaxis. Room Setup: Based on medical condition, airway adjuncts (macintosh maybe better than miller for tongue management) smaller ETT tubes for subglottic stenosis. Invasive monitoring for CHD Intraoperative Mgt: Regional probably not feasible with uncooperative patient, IH vs IV, c-spine precautions manual inline stabilization, Bubble-free IV's, Prone to Brdaycardia - Atropine 20ug/kg, MAC unchanged in Down's Syndrome. Careful head / body positioning (lax joints) Avoid long acting opioids, use multimodal analgesics, full reversal. high incidence of agitation - family presence, Monitoring for OSA, airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Trauma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
C-spine injury & aspiration, occult life-threatening injuries, hypovolemia, hypothermia, Intoxication

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypothermia: Rewarming, Arrythmias, Hypovolemia, Coagulopathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multi system organ dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ALI/ARDS

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypoxic brain injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypoxic cardiomyopathy, shock, arrhythmias

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Acute renal failure (ATN)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Electrolyte abnormalities (hypo/hyperK)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mechanism of drowning: Trauma / Intoxication

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Children: Lack of supervision, Abuse,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Adults: MI, arrhythmia, hypoglycemia, CVA, Seizure, intoxication

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Primary Resuscitation to ensure adequate oxygen exchange and perfusion pressure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prevent secondary injury: C-spine precautions

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Correct hypothermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Drowning

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: AMPLE, mechanism of drowning (trauma, stroke, MI, intoxicants etc), location and duration of drowning (water temp), arrest time and resuscitation measures to date PE: Vitals including temperature, airway, Resp (aspiration, contusion, ARDS), Cardiac (arrhythmias), neurological (hypoxic brain injury, intoxication) Investigations: CBC, lytes (hypokalemia d/t shift), Ca/Mg (hyper in salt water near drowning), CK (Rhabdo), coagulation profile, Tox screen, ABG, ECG, CXR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Resuscitation -  istula tio, ventilation, correct acidosis and lytes, re-warming Room Set-up: CAS monitors + 5L ECG + arterial line + CVL (for vasopressors/inotropes), large bore IV access (coagulopathy, bleeding), core temperature monitoring, warming devices (see below) Intraop Management: Consider RSI for aspiration risk but watch for increased ICP, continue rewarming, lung protective ventilation Post-op: HDU, likely post-op ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Warming:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ATLS recommendations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Limit to 1 shock for pulseless VF/VT if temp < 30˚C, give meds with longer intervals

<!-- PAGE=? -->
34-36˚C: passive rewarming, active external rewarming

<!-- PAGE=? -->
30-34˚C: passive rewarming, active rewarming of truncal areas only -electric warming devices, hot water bottles, heating pads, radiant heat sources, warming beds/blankets)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
<30˚C: Active internal rewarming > Warm IV fluids, humid oxygen, peritoneal lavage (KCL-free fluid), Extracorporeal rewarming, esophageal warming tubes>> discontinue when core temp > 35˚C

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ECMO

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Critically ill patient with multi-organ system failure, at high perioperative risk

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 hypoxia and hemodynamic instability prior to bypass

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Indications and underlying pathologic process

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Etiology of respiratory or cardiac failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anatomy of ECMO circuit (VA / VV)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Contraindications to ECMO

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications related to ECMO

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Embolism:  air, MI, CVA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Tamponade

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Atelectasis, pneumothorax

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 ARF

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Sepsis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hemorrhage, consumptive coagulopathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intensive monitoring for complications, adequacy, and weaning from ECMO

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoidance of complications; specifically bleeding

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Minimize procedures, avoid removing lines

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Close monitoring of all body systems and avoidance of secondary injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Others as determined by underlying pathologic process

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Identify indications for ECMO (acute, reversible, severe hypoxemia with failure of convential therapy, failure to wean from CPB, neonatal PPH/RDS/CDH/mec asp, post-traumatic resp failure, post lung tx), identify multi-organ dysfunction, Identify contraindications to ECMO (mech. Ventn > 7d, irreversible underlying disease or cardiac fxn, severe pulm HTN, cardiac arrest, age >60 or <34 wks or <2kg, immunosuppression, contraindication to anticoagulation)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Contraindications: Gestational age <35 weeks, Weight <2000 g, Preexisting intracranial hemorrhage, Congenital or neurologic abnormalities incompatible with good outcome, >1 week of aggressive respiratory therapy, Congenital heart disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Vitals, ECMO settings, Ventilator settings (when applicable), neurological, CVS, RESP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Full labs, coags, recent ABG, CXR, echocardiogram

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
May be cannulated in OR (post-CPB), under local or sedation in ICU

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ICU setting with full invasive monitoring.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anticoagulation:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Heparin 100-150 U/kg, target ACT of 200, keep platelets >100.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Hemorrhage, ICH, seizures, coagulopathy, multiorgan dysfunction, PTX, tamponade, sepsis. Special: V-V ECMO has better outcomes in adults than V-A ECMO and is preferable whenever the patient does not require CVS  support.  Neonatal ECMO is most often VA.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Eisengmenger's Syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Reversal of chronic L-R shunt caused by increased PVR to a level that equals or exceeds SVR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Occurs in approx 50% of pts with untreated VSD, 10% of pts with untreated ASD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
High risk of morbidity and mortality

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pathophysiology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of hemodynamic collapse with profound hypoxemia on induction / PPV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Inc. PVR, inc. R to L shunt, RV dilation, LV impairment, hypoxemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Polycythemia - with thrombosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Arrythmias - Afib / flutter

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Sudden Death

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of paradoxical emboli

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
pHTN medications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
anticoagulation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
SBE prophylaxis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hemodynamic Goals

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Maintain SVR , Avoid Inc. in PVR (limit PAWP, avoid PEEP, early extubation, avoid hypoxia/hypercarbia/acidosis), Full preload, Maintain NST (reduce pulmonary venous congestion)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Meticulous de-airing of IV tubing

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals / Conflicts

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Establish severity and etiology of disease - functional capcity; syncope, current treatments; hemoptysis; Px: vital signs including RA SaO2; Resp - inc. WOB, cyanosis, clubbing, Cardiac - pHTN (P2, RV Heave) RVF (peripheral edema, hepatic congestion); ASD/VSD murmur disappears when Eisenmenger's develops Inv: CBC (polycythemia) lytes, Ur, Cr, Coags (anticoagulation), CXR, ECG (signs of RVH, pHTN), ECHO

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Consult respiraology and cardiology; high risk of mortality with anesthesia - defer surgical treatment if at all possible; may benefit from normovolemic hemodilution with phlebotomy preoperatively for polycythemia; optimize pHTN treatment

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Options: Dependant on surgical procedure; Irreversible increased PVR contraindicates surgical correction of original defect; minimally invasive with LA preferred, Regional with titrated epidural - no epinephrine to avoid dec. SVR (avoid sedation); GA as required (high risk); Laparoscopic procedures are contraindicated

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Monitors: CAS, 5 lead, preinduction artline and CVP, available TEE Anesthetic Management: Absolute maintanece of SVR to prevent inc/ R to Lshunting with hypoxemia; Early tracheal extubation is preferable

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pregnancy: vaginal birth is the goal; labor analgesia with a slowly titrated epidural (avoid epi), maintain SVR. C/S can be accomlishe with GA or epidural. IV drugs have rapid onset while IH is slow d't R to L shunt

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Electroconvulsive Therapy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Physiological changes from ECT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
HD instability, risk of arrhythmia, inc ICP, IOP, intragastric pressure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potentially uncooperative psychiatric patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
psychotropic meds:  management & altered response to sympathomimetics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Contraindications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pheochromocytoma (absolute), inc. ICP, intracranial tumor, recent CVA, cardiovascular conduction defects, high-risk pregnancy, and aortic and cerebral aneurysms

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Out-of-OR location

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
headaches, myalgias, confusion, memory loss, CVA, malignant arrhythmias, myocardial infarctions (67% of ECT mortalities), pulmonary edema, emboli, obstructions, aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Attenuate hemodynamic and autonomic response

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevent awareness & injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize seizure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Rapid emergence

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Standard anesthetic history (may be difficult to obtain), Indication, Old anesthetic records & previous ECT treatments & doses required, Assessment of cardiopulmonary and neurologic status, Review medications : TCAs - block reuptake of Catecholamines → deplete central adrenergic stores → unpredictable response to indirect agents, direct-acting may cause exaggerated response; anticholinergic effects, MAOIs - irreversible complex with MAO → prevents breakdown of norepinephrine, 5-HT, dopamine → indirect agents can cause HTN crisis, direct acting may cause exaggerated response, Lithium - prolongs effects of dMR, certain NdMR, and sedatives (barbiturates); R/O contraindication to ECT - CAD, pacemakers/ICDs, afib Px: vitals including postural BP, A/W for ease of intubation & BMV, inc. ICP, CHF

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Inv:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
labs as directed by comorbidity, ECG (previous MI, arrhythmia), CT if query inc. ICP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Aspiration prophylaxis, disable ICD (clinic, magnet), asynch pacemaker

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Equipment: CAS, PNS, A/W equipment, Emergency drugs (atropine, vasopressors, vasodilators)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Induction: Preoxygenation, Mild hyperventilation (hypoxia, hypercarbia reduce seizure), Bite block, control A/W if difficult, pregnant, aspiration risk, consider management of HD (atropine, esmolol), Thiopental 2mg/kg (↑ seizure threshold, delayed awakening), Propofol 2-3 mg/kg (↓ seizure duration, rapid awakening but no difference in outcome, pain on injection), Etomidate may prolong seizure duration (can be useful), Ketamine prolongs seizure duration but exacerbates sympathetic response, avoid benzodiazepines, SCh (0.5mg/kg), NdMR if SCh contraindicated (intubate and ventilate)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: monitor in PACU, Supplemental O2,  acetaminophen, NSAIDs may alleviate ECT-induced myalgia Complications: Confusion, agitation, amnesia, headache, Rare - Aspiration, myocardial ischemia, neurological vascular events, fracture/dislocation, status epilepticus, death (Current mortality rate is 1 in 10,000-30,000 treatments)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Epiglottitis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency with potential for complete airway obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ENT, difficult A/W cart, urgent transport to OR, avoid agitating patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential sepsis with need for fluid resuscitation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
pediatric patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Postoperative management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
disposition, treatment of infection, need for specialized pediatric care

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Rapid assessment and diagnosis transport to OR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Safe and timely A/W management, avoiding precipitants of airway obstruction :

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o position changes, crying, airway exam

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o KEEP CHILD CALM

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Early antibiotics once IV access secured (this may have to wait until airway secured)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Need for fluid resuscitation vs need to avoid agitating child

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Risk of aspiration vs need to maintain spontaneous ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Differential : croup, foreign body, abscess, caustic aspiration, anaphylaxis Assessment : Classic presentation of "Toxic, drooling child", often maintaining upright sniffing position (tripod); Generally age 2 - 7; Acute, rapidly progressive onset: 2-4 hrs; Fever, sore throat  may be initial symptoms; If high suspicion -  AMPLE history andimmediate transport to the OR signs of fatigue, impending failure which would precipitate urgent transfer to OR.  Assessment of volume

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Px: status

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: Diagnosis is clinical. If any concern go to OR; if stable and no signs of impending A/W obstruction - CBC, bld cultures, lateral neck xray

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization Oxygen, Fluid resuscitation; Antibiotics to cover HiB and beta-hemolytic strep; Steroids; ENT; PICU

<!-- PAGE=? -->
EARLY TRANSFER TO OR, ENT, DIFFICULT AIRWAY CART, TRACH/CRIC KIT AVAILABLE

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Management: Moribund: awake DL; Stable child: SV GA, IH - 4% ET sevo, TIVA - Propofol infusion at 200 u/k/m, Remi 0.1-0.2 u/k/m; DL when unresponsive (may take ~10min); ETT placed (use 0.5-1.0 size smaller); Topicalize A/W prior to rigid bronch (lido 3mg/kg)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Disposition: Keep intubated for 2 days or until response to medical Rx observed and cuff leak/ETT leak occurs. Extubate in OR using same spontaneously ventilating technique and direct observation of larynx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DDx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Dec. Elimination

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Rebreathing

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Increased Dead-space

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Inspiratory valve failure (if PPV, if SV, could be either IV or EV)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CO2 absorber exhaustion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Alveolar hypoventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Inc. Production

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Sepsis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o MH / NMS / Serotonin Syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Thyrotoxicosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Cocaine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Pheochormocytoma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Transfusion reaction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hyperthermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Reperfusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Exogenous (e.g. laparoscopy)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased EtCO2

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Emergency situation - simulataneous diagnosis and treatment

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Inform the surgeon and call for help

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Scan my monitors: rate, rhythm , BP, EtCO2, SaO2, temp, PIP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o CO2 waveform

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o eliminate rebreathing as etiology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 high fresh gas flow

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 hand ventilate

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Ensure adequate minute ventilation - decompress belly if required

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Rule out other etiologies

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Femoral Nerve Block (L2,3,4)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Indications: Analgesia for hip or knee surgery. Combined with Sciatic for entire lower extremity. Contraindications: Usual + possible compartment syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anatomy: Lateral to femoral artery, beneath Fascia Lata and Iliaca, anterior to iliopsoas. Ant branch gives of sensory to anterior, anteromedial and medial aspects of thigh. Posterior branch gives motor to quads and sensation to knee, and medial leg (saphenous).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Vessel puncture, nerve injury, infection, LA toxicity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Technique: Standard CAS Monitors, Supine, along femoral crease, lateral to femoral artery, 5cm needle, perpendicular to skin, goal is patellar twitch, inject 20 ml LA. If Sartorius twitch, go slightly lateral and deeper. 3 in 1 block is the same approach, but needle insertion slightly cephalad, 40 ml LA w/ distal pressure. Unreliable in blocking LFCN 62% and obturator 52%. Fascia Iliaca block: Trisect inguinal ligament, insertion site is 1cm caudal to the point bw lateral and middle third, 5cm blunt needle, feel for 2 pops., inject 30ml. LFCN w/ FI block ~90%, Obturator 38%.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
LFCN block: Supine, 2.5cm inferior and medial to ASIS, 4 cm needle inserted perpendicular to skin, 1 pop through fascia lata, 10 ml injected above and below fascia lata in a fan wise approach. For sensory block of anterolateral thigh to knee.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Obturator Nerve: Pt is upine, leg slightly abducted. Landmarks 1.5 cm inferior and lateral to pubic tubercle. 10 cm needle, perpendicular to skin, contact bone (inferior ramus of pubis), withdraw, redirect slightly laterally and caudad to enter obturator foreman , advance 2-3 cm, look for adductor twitch.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Lumbar Plexus Block  (Psoas Compartment Block): Analgesia for hip and knee surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Contraindications: Usual

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Technique: Pt is lateral, kneeds flexed. Landmarks are 1. Midline 2. Parallel line along PSIS 3. Line between iliac crests . Insertion site 2/3 from midline to PSIS along iliac crest line. Nerve roots lie at a depth of 7-10cm almost always 2 cm past transverse process. Fascial click into perineural sheath. Patellar twitch at 0.5-1 mA. Inject 40 ml.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Trouble Shooting: If hit TP, redirect cephalad and go 2 cm deeper. If no twitch fan in cephalad-caudad plane. If paravetrebral muscle twitch, go deeper, if psoas stim, pull back. If hamstrings, too caudad.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: vessels, GI). IV, Subrachnoid, epidural, LA toxicity.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Nerve injury, retroperitoneal hematoma, injury to structures deep to LP (kidney, major

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ilac Crest

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PSIS

<!-- PAGE=? -->
L3

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Fetal Distress

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency situation requiring immediate maternal and IU fetal resuscitation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Etiology of the fetal compromise:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Aortocaval compression

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Maternal morbidity (Abruption / Hge / Ut rupture/PIH/hTN/Shock/ Sepsis)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Fetal morbidity (Cord prolapsed/Ut hypertonus/IUGR)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic plan for C/S - based on degree fetal compromise and maternal condition

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Preparation for neonatal resuscitation - Pediatrician present

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts :

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Resuscitation of mother to optimize UPP (O2, iv fluid, LUD, stop oxytocin, ?tocolytics)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Clear communication between services (anesthesia, OB, pediatrics)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Rapid assessment & initiation of delivery plan

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Facilitate prompt delivery without compromising maternal safety

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Be prepared for neonatal resuscitation (pediatrician, etc.)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Conficts

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypotension with RSI (hypovolemic) vs. Aspiration with titrated induction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Difficult A/W vs. STAT C/S

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypotension with SAB with hypovolemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Immediate Resuscitation: O2, LUD, Fluid Bolus, vasopressors, Stop uterine contractions (oxytocin, NTG 50100 ug bolus)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Etiology of distress - Maternal, fetal (Cord prolapsed, Footling breech, Massive abruption, Uterine rupture, Increased uterine tone, PIH, Hypotension/ shock/ sepsis); AMPLE Hx; obstetric hx PE: maternal VS, FHR (baseline, variability, and decels), maternal A/W, uterine tone Investigations: don't wait if severe distress - CBC, x-match, coags and fibrinogen for DIC

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Continued maternal resuscitation as directed by etiology; Asp. Prophylaxis, topicalize A/W as indicated, contiuous FHR monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: GA vs SAB vs insitu Epidural; Normal A/W - RSI GA; Diff. A/W - AFOI or SAB (begin topicalizing A/W while attempting SAB)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: NTG for uterine relaxation, pressors, oxytocin, hemabate; Diff. A/W cart, large bore IV, continuous FHR, OB/paeds in room

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Induction: Position Pt to optimize LUD and A/W management; De-nitrogenate with 100% FiO2; prepped and draped, surgeon scrubed, Cricoid, Thiopental 3-5 mg/kg (Ketamine 1-1.5 mg/kg), Sux 1.5mg/kg Intraoperative Mgt: consider TIVA/NO2 after the baby is out (decrease volatile after delivery); orogastric tube prio to emergence

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Extubate when awake; HDU/ICU/NICU; Postop pain - NSAIDS, PCA Complications: with LMA); HD compromise; Neonatal resuscitationPregnant Patient considerations

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Aspiration; Failure Intubation (BMV +- LMA, optimize and re-attempt, wake pt vs. continue

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Fontan's Circulation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Univentricular physiology - completed repair around 3 yrs of age

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Passive pulmonary flow (dependent on venous pressure - PVR)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardia Dysdunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
arrhythmias: SVTs , VTs - defib pads preoperatively

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ventricular dysfunction - 70% by 10yrs (pericardial and pleural effusions)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Late forming pHTN - d/t elevated pulmonary perfusion pressures

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of hypoxia with fenestrated Fontan - R to L shunt

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Paradoxical emboli - airless IV's

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Co-morbid illness: Protein losing enteropathy, Thromboembolism (30% at 10yr - anticoagulation)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Consideration of SBE prophylaxis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain full venous return, avoid pHTN triggers, avoid dehydration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hemodynamic goals:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Full preload

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o normal SVR - prevent R - L shunt

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o low PVR - avoid hypercarbia, excessive PPV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o normal contractility, and sinus rhythm (dec. pulmonary venous congestion)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Treat hypotension with pheylephrine (increases SVR > PVR)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Foreign Body

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potentially life-threatening emergency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Potential perioperative airway obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Barotrauma (ball-valve phenomena)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Bronchospasm

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Co-morbid disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Neurologic disease (aspiration risk)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Intoxication

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Post-obstructive pneumonia (if delayed)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Rigid bronchoscopy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Shared airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Maintenance of anesthesia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Ventilation and oxygenation during bronchoscopy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pediatric patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Minimize risk of aspiration (prophylaxis, fasting)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Minimize risk of airway obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Minimize distal displacement of FB through avoidance of PPV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Minimize ball-valve obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Facilitate retrieval of FB (Immobile patient with minimal coughing)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Effective communication with Surgeon

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Aspirated object/substance (if known; sharp vs. organic/inflammatory), time of aspiration, symptoms of airway obstruction or compromise (stridor, drooling, tachypnea), signs of infection (fever, productive cough, hypoxemia); risk fx for aspiration, last meal PE: Vitals - including RR/O2sat (respiratory distress) + temp (infection) + weight, airway exam, respiratory exam for distress (retractions, tracheal tug, stridor, wheezing, crackles) and cvs exam. Investigations: minimal if obstructing.  Consider CXR (90% of objects are radiolucent, so not sensitive), CBC (infection), ABG (unwell, pneumonia) Optimization: O2, ENT immediately available; Aspiration prophylaxis if urgent - delay for fasting guidelines if not acutely obstructed; Heliox, bronchodilators, racemic epi to temporize; Antisialogogue for pediatric; IV abx if infection; Position: Upper airway - position of comfort/sitting upright/leaning forward; Distal airway: affected lung down, to protect normal lung Anesthetic Options: May do adults under sedation local if flexible FOB.  Peds and rigid bronchoscopy must be done under GA.  With adults, obesity or other conditions which make SV difficult/impossible under GA, consider intubation w/ PPV, may have to leave bougie, extubate during brief periods for rigid bronchoscopy Room Setup: Difficult airway cart, FOB, jet venitlator and help available. Warming if peds.  Resusciation drugs. Intraoperative Mgt: ENT in room; IV vs. IH induction with SV; PPV may be necessary.  TIVA does not depend on surgical technique.  Consider intubating after retrieval of FB prior to emergence (minimize risk of aspiration). risk of laryngeal edma x 24hrs - O2, racemic epi, steroids, Abx, chest physio, possible postop vent

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Complications: Bronchospasm (ventolin, deepen anesthetic); inadequate ventilation (reposition bronch, consider PTX); A/W obstruction (consider PTX, push FB distal, thoracotomy); PTX; tacheobronchial trauma with hemorrhage; pneumonia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Three step approach

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Patient - ASA, comorbidity, A/W, monitoring requirements

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Procedure - Duration, invasiveness (pain), special requirements (monitoring, paralysis), complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Environment - equipment, patient access, personnel, hazards (radiation, magnet), temperature, interference

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Provide same standard of care of patient in the OR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o anesthesia equipment, monitors and procedures

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Identify and mitigate all environmental hazards

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Ionizing radiation, ferromagnetic radiation, contrast media

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Identify reasons why the patient requires GA or anesthesia-administered sedation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Familiarize yourself with the remote environment, staff and location of all necessary emergency equipment and drugs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Foreign Environment

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Preparation:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ensure the presence and proper function of all necessary equipment - central O2, cylinder,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
suction, lighting, gas scavenging, electrical outlets, resuscitative equipment;  Identify bulky and immobile

<!-- PAGE=? -->
equipment, assess need to monitor the patient remotely

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx & Px: Assess patient for comorbidities, potential complications and conflicts with procedure (sedation vs. GA, paralysis, limited access to patient, remote monitoring)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Monitors: CAS monitors + those dictated by the procedure and the patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Specific Procedures:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Angiography/intervention -

<!-- PAGE=? -->
minimal sedation vs. GA, contrast agents (nephropathy, allergic rxn - fish

<!-- PAGE=? -->
allergy), ensure lines / tubes free to allow the table to move

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CT -

<!-- PAGE=? -->
trauma, acute situations, resuscitate prior to scan, oral contrast

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Radiofrequency Ablation -

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Rx for tumors (liver, lung, adrenal etc..) likely endstage disease (4Ms), beware of

<!-- PAGE=? -->
complications (PTX, BPF, Hemorrage), pacemaker contraindicated (heat / burns)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
MRI -

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Peds, limited access, remote monitoring, need to exclude ferromagnetic components, interferences with

<!-- PAGE=? -->
monitors (ECG artifact - place electrodes close together), pacemakers contraindicated, burns possible from

<!-- PAGE=? -->
various monitors - run cables in straight lines (no coils), if emergency - stop sequence, rapidly remove patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
from MRI/scanner room (need for resuscitative equipment that is not magnet safe)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
G6PD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
G6PD deficiency is a enzymopathy that can result in hemolysis secondary to oxidative damage to susceptible red blood cells; X-linked; common in African Americans, Africans, Asians, and Mediterranean populations

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Chronic hemolytic anemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Need to avoid precipitants of hemolysis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Oxidative drugs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Infection

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Metabolic abnormalities (eg. DKA)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid precipitants of hemolysis:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Acetaminophen - safe in therapeutic doses

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Salicylates - safe in therapeutic doses

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Antibiotics: Nitrofurans; Penicillin; Streptomycin; Chloramphenical; Isoniazid

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Sulfonamides

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Antimalarial Drugs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Miscellaneous: Probenecid; Quinidine; Vit K analogues; Metheylene Blue; Nitroprusside

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: episodes of acute hemolytic anemia (usually asymptomatic in steady state; triggers can ppt hemolysis); Hx neonatal hyperbilirubinemia; Favism (d/t ingestion of fresh fava beans; ages 1-5yrs)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Pallor; Jaundice; ?hepatomegally

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: CBC (hgb may fall to 30-40); Diff; Blood film (Heinz bodies-clumps of ptn; With hemolysis: microsperocytes; eccentrocytes -bite cells; reticulocytosis)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hematology consult

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
No limitations

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CAS monitors

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: avoid oxidant drugs; Anesthetic agents are not known to ppt hemolysis Post-op: standard

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Acute hemolysis: early post op  (2-5 days) evidence of hemolysis may indicate G6PD; self limited as only older RBCs are affected

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Special: Avoid drugs that can result in methemoglobinemia (prilocaine, Lidocaine, bezocaine) because treatment with methylene blue is contraindicated

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Minimize aspiration risk

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maximize respiratory muscle strength (minimize / avoid NdMB)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain hemodynamic stability

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Conflicts: RSI without Sux/decreased NdMB vs hemodynamically stable induction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Guillain Barre Syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Acute idiopathic inflammatory demyelinating polyneuropathy characterized by ascending progressive muscle weakness and areflexia, usually associated with spontaneous remission.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of aspiration - weakness of pharyngeal muscles

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Respiratory failure - intercostal muscle weakness/post-op ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Autonomic instability - compensatory CV responses may be absent, exaggerated response to stimuli or hypovolemia, tachycardia, hypo/hypertension, arrythmias

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Altered response to NMB - Hyperkalemic response to succinylcholine - NdMB sensitivity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased risk of venous thromboembolism , raised ICP (rare)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Acute Medical therapy : IVIG / Plasmapharesis (Steroids not helpful!)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Onset of symptoms, respiratory compromise, cough, bulbar symptoms, cardiovascular instability, arrhythmias. Treatment. Functional capacity. AMPLE Hx. PE: Focused cardiorespiratory exam, neurologic exam.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
