Investigations: Usual investigations, PFTs / VC, ECG, CXR Optimization: Delay elective surgery, Neurology consult, Plex/IVIG, aspiration prophylaxis, DVT prophylaxis.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: GA, PNB, Neuraxial all plausible. Room Setup: CAS / PNS / consider invasive monitors,  vasopressors for hypotension, assistance for cricoids.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: hypotension, avoid stimulants on induction.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Consider RSI, avoid sux, judicious NDMRs, ensure reversal, direct acting agents for Arrythmias / DVT / PE / Respiratory embarrassment.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Special: M > F, bimodal distribution in young adults and elderly, 1:33,000, starts in legs, ascending flaccid paralysis, 5% mortality, children less severely affected. Rx: IVIG 0.4mg/kg x 5days, plasmapharesis, steroids not useful.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
HCM

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Myocardial hypertrophy resulting in a small and hyperdynamic left ventricle - risk of ischemia, sudden cardiac death and fixed or dynamic LVOT obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for dynamic outflow obstruction in 25%

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Precipitated by inc. contractility, dec. preload, and/or dec. afterload

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Tachyarrythmias

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypertrophy, diastolic disfunction and inc. MVO2 - myocardial ischemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mitral regurgitation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Associated medications - BBs, antiarrythmics, anticoagulants, diuretics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pacekmaker or AICD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid acute LV outflow tract obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Maintain full preload and adequate afterload to stent LVOT open while avoiding any inc. in myocardial contractility

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid tachycardia while maintaining strict NSR (diastolic dysfunction)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Be prepared to treat lethal arrhythmias and avoid precipitating arrhythmias

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Maintain myocardial oxygenation and monitor for ischemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimize oxygen delivery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Maintain adequate afterload

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Consider invasive monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Many pts are asymptomatic Hx of SOBOE (90%), angina (~30%) presyncope, syncope. Afib/flutter/SVT (25%), PVCs/VT/brady (20%), MR, Hx of CHF. Prior cardiac arrest, pacemaker settings.  Assess for risk of SCD and need for AICD (pts with prior cardiac arrest, sustained VT or 2 or more risk factors: family hx of SCD <45 yrs, Flat (failure to increase SBP by 25mmHG) or hypotensive (decrease SBP > 15mmHg) response to exercise in patients <40years, non-sustained VT during 48hr holter monitoring, LV wall thickness >30, resting peak instantaneous gradient >30mmHg. PE: Displaced apical beat, S4, Harsh SEM bw apex/LSB (worse with valsalva and standing) radiates to axillae. CHF, ↑ JVP, R sided S4 with R heart involvement.  Murmur of MR. Investigations: CBC/Lytes, ECG - arrhythmias, BBB, LVH (Deepest S in lead V1 or V2 + tallest R in V5 or V6 > 35 and or a R wave in lead aVL >12), LAD, q waves, -Giant t-wave syndrome‖ = sharply negative Twaves in V3-5 are typical of apical HCM. CXR may demonstrate LV/LA/RA enlargement. ECHO: asymmetric hypertrophy, SAM, gradient, systolic & diastolic dysfunction, MR, LA size, check for provocable LVOT obstruction, MIBI, angiography. consider septal alcohol ablation prior to elective procedure. If systolic dysfunction evaluate for transplantation. See hemod goals above. Deep plane of anesthesia prior to airway manipulation, consider

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Ensure adequate volume status. Cardiology consult, consider AICD/Pacemaker placement, BB / CCB (verapmil 75mcq/kg, may repeat 150mcq/kg in 15-30mins, max dose 20mg) for LVOT obs, consider anxiolytic for tachycardia. Diuretics for CHF, antiarrythmic therapy to restore NSR or cardioversion. Anesthetic Options: GA generally well tolerated.  Neuraxial techniques are acceptable and well tolerated if HD goals met - OB: GA, epidural, CSE with intrathecal opioid (spinal contraindicated), avoid oxytocin bolus Room Setup: Invasive lines, alpha agonists, BBs/CCBs, antiarrythmics, pacer, TEE/PAC in high risk pts. Intraoperative Mgt: phenyephrine infusion and volume preload. Avoid ketamine. Consider arrhythmias with CVP/PAC placement Post-op: Avoid tachy/pain on emergence, observe in HDU, maintain hemodynamic goals. Complications : Hypotension, acute LVOT obstruction, arrythmias

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hemophilia A (F VIII), B (IX), & vWD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
High risk of perioperative bleeding associated with specific factor deficiency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
F VIII - Hemophilia A (Classic) - sex linked recessive

<!-- PAGE=? -->
F IX - Hemophilia B (Christmas Disease) - sex linked recessive

<!-- PAGE=? -->
von Willebrand Disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Sequelae of bleeding in enclosed spaces: Joints, Intracranial, Pericardium, Thorax

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential contraindication to neuraxial anesthesia and analgesia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Labour Epidural in parturients ok if FVIII & vWF >50%

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Consultation with hematology for factor optimization, identification of inhibitors, difficult cross match

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Coexisting viral infections: HIV, HBV (less now with recombinant products)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimize factor activity and coagulation profile in perioperative period

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o DDAVP / Humate P / cryoprecipitate

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Techniques for minimizing perioperative blood/Factor loss.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Manage bleeding episode with appropriate Factor replacement.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Bleeding Hx - easy bruising, petechiae, mucosal bleeding, epistaxis, menorrhagia, family bleeding Hx, hx of cancer or collagen vascular disease. History of prolonged bleeding after Sx (dental work, tonsillectomy) PE: Bruises, petechiae, oral mucosa, lymph nodes, hepatosplenomegaly. Airway - hematoma MSK Joint deformity Investigations: CBC, INR, PTT, cross match.  Assay for activity level of factor, factor antibodies (anti-FVIII). Most sensitive test for vWD is ristocetin cofactor activity. Other Inv. as dictated by procedure and patient co-morbidity Optimization: Consult hematology.  Plan OR early in the week/day. Consider antifibrinolytics periop (3-5 days) Hemophilia: Assay factor levels 48h prior to OR and restore levels to >50% for major surgery (maintain 5-10 d), dental extraction (maintain >12hrs), delivery/pueperium (maintain 3-4 d). > 30% for minor surgery (maintain 2-4 d).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Rpt factor assay after administration and within 2h of OR to confirm factor activity.  Monitor level intra-op as dictated by clinical situation. No anti-platelet meds. Hemophilia A : Severe <2%, Mod 2-10%, mild >10%.  PTT, Normal INR. DDAVP (may  FVIII) , Recombinant F VIII (1U/kg  FVIII 2%) , Recombinant F VIIa for inhibitors, Cryo if nothing else available (the only fractionated blood product containing meaningful amounts of F VIII and vWF, FFP has ~.7-.9u/ml FVIII).  VIII T½ = ~12hrs in adults, ~6hrs in Peds Hemophilia B :  PTT. rFIX (1U/kg  FIX 1%, half is absorbed by collagen in the vasculature) , rFVIIa (for inhibitors), FFP if nothing else available (cryo does not contain FIX). FIX T½ = 8-24 hours. Pregnancy: Consider fetus affected in carriers and minimize trauma to fetus esp if male vWD Subtype 1 (70-80%), Nstructure, dec. quantity; Responds to DDAVP (3-5 fold inc. in vWF; dose = 0.3 mcg/kg (max 20 mcg/dose and rpt 24h).  Subtype 2a (20-30%) Abnormal structure, normal or dec. quantity; Requires F VIIIvWF concentrates (Humate P) in addition to DDAVP. DDAVP contraindicated in subtype 2b , as this promotes thrombocytopenia. Subtype 3 (rare) Little or no vWF. Bleeding pattern same as Hemophilia A. Require treatment with F VIII-vWF concentrates, platelets if thrombocytopenic. DDAVP no benefit. Emergency: 1st humate P (50iu/kg  consult heme), cryo, Plt concentrates; Pregnancy: Factor VIII, vWF, ristocetin cofactor early in pregnancy and at 34 weeks. During pregnancy, prophylactic tx if FVIII level <25%. During labour, maintain levels 50% of normal, if csec 80% normal. Post partum, follow levels and tx if <25% or significant hemorrhage. vWF: Type I or IIA, DDAVP 0.3ug/kg with labor q12h. Non responders, tx with humate P (40iu/kg). Regional: LEA OK if FVIII and vWF > 50%.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: surgery done in ctr capable of rapid Factor assays.  Neuraxial - requires 70-100% of Factor activity, reasonable platlets: vWD:  >50 % activity of F VIII/vWF

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: CAS, Large bore IV, Temp probe, blood warmer, rapid infuser, cell salvage, Arterial line for sampling, Factor (recombinant, human derived) available, X-match prior to OR - may be delays for antibody investigation Intraoperative Mgt: Careful positioning/laryngoscopy.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Mild Hemorrhage (early joint/muscle, epistaxis, hematuria, dental bleed) target 20-30% activity. Major Hemorrhage (advanced joint/muscle, hematoma neck/tongue, prophylaxis after severe trauma) target 40-50%.  Lifethreatening Hemorrhage (intracranial, surgical, GI bleed, major trauma bleed) target 50-100%.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
1. Multisystem disease:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CNS: Dementia, peripheral neuropathies, myopathys, visual loss, mass lesions with inc. ICP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Airway: upper a/w obstruction with Candida, possible difficult intubation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Resp: Pnuemonia, Lymphoma, Primary pHTN, pleural effusions

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CVS: Autonomic neuropathy, pancarditis (IE in IVDU), accelerated CAD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Renal: End stage nephropathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Heme - Anemia, coagulopathy (ITP), lymphopenia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
2. Immunocomprimised:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Opportunistic infections - Meningitis, encephalitis, pneumonia/TB, esophagitis, enteritis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Malignancy - Lymphoma, Karposi Sarcoma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications: Bone marrow suppression, renal failure, peripheral neuropathy, p450 activation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Chronic pain / Substance Abuse

<!-- PAGE=? -->
OB and HIV: dec perinatal transmission with AZT (25% - 8%), elective C/S, Regional OK (document peripheral neuropathy, coagulation, strict sterile technique, blood patch OK - d/w patient)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
HIV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx & Px: duration since Dx, Current treatment (prophylaxis), Screen for comorbid disease: oportunisitic infections (CNS - Dementia Resp - CD4 < 200 PCP, Cryptococcus, CMV), Vital incl temp, Focused resp (SpO2, cough, crackles), CVS (chest pain, rub, dec. exercise tolerance), peripheral neuropathy, GI disturbance (dysphagia, diarrhea)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Inv: CBC, E7, CD4, ECG, CXR, Consider PFTs, ABG, ECHO, MRI/CT Head

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Oprimization:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Adequate prophylaxis, treat infections

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Options:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
GA or regional OK

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Setup:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CAS monitors, strtct asepsis, otherwise as required by comorbidities and procedure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
As predictied by comorbidities

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Underlying etiology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Shift - acidosis, meds

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Impaired excretion - renal failure, ureteric obstruction, Addison's, lupus

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Excess intake or release - rhabdo, hemolysis, transfusions, burns, tumour lysis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Physiologic  sequelae  of  hyperkalemia:  weakness,  arrhythmias  which  may  progress  to  malignant arrhythmias

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Need for continuous monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevent/treat arrhythmias

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Reduce serum potassium levels

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Reduce total body potassium if elevated

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hyperkalemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Meds, Past Med Hx, allergies, fatigue, weakness, paresthesiae, palpitations, pain or history of trauma (rhabdo), recent transfusions.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Vitals, cardiorespiratory exam, neuro (decreased DTRs, weakness), evidence of renal failure (bruising, petechiae, edema, presence of fistulae), palpate compartments.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: 12 lead EKG, Lytes, BUN, Cr, Mg, Ca, Dig level (if on dig), ABG, urine myoglobin, urine R&M

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ECG changes: Early: Peaked Ts, QT shortening, ST depression

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Later: Increased PR, BBB, decreased P wave

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Late: Widening of QRS eventually to sine wave then VFib, Asystole

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Treatment: Calcium chloride 5-10cc  (stabilize myocardium), glucose/insulin 25-50g and 10 units (shifts intracellular), Lasix 1 mg/kg (increase K excretion), B agonism - ventolin 5-20 mg (shifts K intracellular), alkalinize - bicarb 1 amp or 3 amps in 1 L D5 (shifts K intracellular), kayexylate  15-30 g po or 30-60 g pr or calcium risonium (exchange resin to remove potassium from body - note kayexylate results in increased sodium which may not be desirable if CHF, renal failure or hypernatremia are part of clinical picture).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Failure to respond to above medical therapy or severe hyperkalemia (> 7 or >6 with physiologic derangement) should prompt consideration of urgent dialysis.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Meds which can cause hyperkalemia include: Amiloride, Angiotensin II inhibitors, ACE Inhibitors, Pentamidine, Spironolactone, Succinylcholine, Triamterene, Trimethoprim, NSAIDs, Heparin

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Management of hypercalcemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Monitor ECG and Ca concentrations perioperatively

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevent pathological fractures

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Airway vigilance

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hyperparathyroidism

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Underlying etiology (parathyroid tumour, PTH producing tumour, chronic hypocalcemia & hyperphosphatemia CRF, acute pancreatitis)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential difficult and dangerous airway secondary to mass effect and osteopenic bone

<!-- PAGE=? -->
pathologic fractures mandible and vertebral bodies, inc. aspiration risk

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Physiologic changes of HYPERcalcemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CNS: ↓LOC, hallucinations, psychosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CVS: HTN, hypovolemia, conduction blockade, long PR, Short QT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Resp:  potential respiratory muscle weakness with RLD, poor clearance of secretions

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Other: Renal failure - nephrolithiasis (70%); N/V, abdo pain, pancreatitis; weakness (titrate NdMB to effect); anemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations of cancer and associated syndromes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
MEN 1: hyperparathyroid, pancreatic islet cell tumors, pituitary hyperplasia or tumor

<!-- PAGE=? -->
MEN 2A: hyperparathyroid, medullary thyroid CA, pheochromocytoma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prevention of pathologic fractures during positioning

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op airway obstruction after parathyroidectomy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
hematoma, laryngospasm, hypocalcemia, RLN injury, tracheomalacia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Underlying etiology, symptoms of hypercalcemia; symptoms of neck mass (positional dyspnea, stridor) Px: Vitals; volume status, airway (mass effect), muscular atrophy; fractures/deformities Investigations : Ca, Lytes, Cr, PO4, Mg, albumin, PTH, ECG (long PR, QRS, short QT, arrhythmias), +/- CT neck

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Endocrine consult; Management of hypercalcemia - IV rehydration (2-6L) followed by Lasix(4080mg) after euvolemia  - goal of 3-5 L urine/day; If severe add - Bisphosphonate (etidronate 7.5mg/kg IV OD or 20mg/kg PO OD); Calcitonin 200 IU nasal spray/day; IV steroid (inhibit GI Ca absorption); Phosphate repletion; Mithramycin to antagonize PTH (prompt dec. in Ca) - results in thrombocytopenia, hepatotoxicity, nephrotoxicity;Hemodialysis if CRI/RF

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Options: No particular anesthetic technique is indicated

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Management: AFOI if difficult A/W or significant osteopenia; whatch for hypotensionwith induction; MAC may reduced with CNS symptoms; careful positioning; unpredictable response to NdMB - use a nerve stimulator; maintain normocarbia (acidosis results in inc. ionized Ca, alkalosis results in dec. ionized Ca & hypokalemia unopposed Ca)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Cardiac arrhythmias 2' to hypercalcemia - serial monitor Ca, Mg, PO4; A/W obstruction - B/L RLN injury, tracheomalacia, hematoma; Hypocalcemia - laryngospasm, arrhythmia, Sz; Hypomagnesemia, pneumothorax

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypoparathyroidism

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Etiology (thyroidectomy, parathyroidectomy, DiGeorge, hypomagnesemia, excess phosphate)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Physiologic changes of hypocalcemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CNS: decreased LOC, seizures

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Resp: laryngospasm , bronchospasm

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CVS: decreased contractility , dysrhythmias , hypotension

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 MSK: muscle spasms , altered response to NdMB (use PNS)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hyperventilation induced alkalosis causes ↓ serum Ca  (↑ Ca protein binding)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: : identify cause and look for symptoms of hypocalcemia (decreased LOC, confusion, delirium, seizures, perioral paresthesia, laryngospasm, bronchospasm, hypotension, syncope/presyncope, palpitations. Cramps, spasms, heterotopic ossification

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Px: Vitals (orthostatic), Resp - bronchospasm; CVS - CHF, hypotension, Muscle spasm - Chvostek's (masseter twitch with facial tap), Trousseau's (muscular contraction of the hand with BP cuff inflation)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CBC, Lytes, Ca, Mg, PO4; ECG - prolonged QT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Consult endocrine; replete serum Ca & Mg; dec. dietary PO4, PO4 binders early

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative management:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
No particular anesthetic technique is indicated

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Unexplained intraoperative hypotension should either prompt laboratory testing or empiric treatment for hypocalcemia in addition to your normal approach to hypotension

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypertension

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Most common periop comorbidity in surgical pts (~20-25%), and causes accel end-organ dysfnx (CAD/PVD/CVD/CKD) and increased periop morbidity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased perioperative morbidity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for end-organ dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o CAD +/-LV dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o CRF

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o PVD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o CVD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Labile perioperative hemodynamics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Exaggerated response to endogenous and exogenous catecholamines

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Relative intravascular volume depletion-hypotension on induction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Perioperative medication management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential secondary causes of hypertension

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Renal (CKD, renal artery stenosis), OSA (30%), Endocrine (pheochromocytoma, Cushing's, hyperaldo, hyper/hypothyroid, hyperparathyroid)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain periopertive BP within 20% normal

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 If SBP > 180, DBP > 110 - try and delay for w/o of secondary causes / optimization

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Document baseline, severity, duration, lability and control of HTN. Determine end-organ complications of severe HTN (CAD/CKD/CVD/CHF). Inquire about secondary casuse ( Pheo /Thyroid, Hyperaldosteronism, Cushings). Medical Rx and compliance. Co-morbid illnesses (DM/Smoking/OSA).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Vitals, BP both arms, postural. Carotids for bruits. LVH >> displaced apex, loud S2. CHF >> audible S4, basilar crackles, raised JVP. Renovascular bruits.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: Lytes if on diuretics or co-morbid CKD. Hypokalemia ? hyperaldosteronism. 12-lead ECG (associated LVH / ST changes, q waves).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Endocrinology/Cardiology consult if concerned about secondary causes of HTN. Consider cancelling elective surgery if evidence of end-organ dysfunction or SBP > 180/110. If untreated HTN consider IV/PO medications perioperatively (note POISE study results). Hold ACEi  ~ 48hrs for cases with anticipated major hemodynamic shifts/CPB. Consider holding diuretics for procedures associated with bowel prep/major fluid shifts. Continue all other antihypertensives and resume post-op.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: Any

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: 5 lead, consider invasive monitors, antihypertensives: BBs/NTG etc. Usual vasopressors Vasopressin for refractory hypotension with patients on ACEis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Any, observe intravascular depletion and sens to exog/endogenous catecholamines Minimize intubation time < 15s, generous opioids, anticpate lability, avoid ketamine. Maintain BP ~20% of baseline.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Monitor for ischemia, adequate analgesia, r/o bladder distention, continue antihypertensive ASAP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypertension: Emergency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Emergency situation which requires simultaneous diagnosis and treatment

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Inform the surgeon and ensure no surgical factors

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 My initial differential diagnosis includes:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypoxemia / hypercapnea

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Drugs: administered, illicit, errors and withdrawal

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Pain / light anesthesia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Patient factors including endocrine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 I would scan my monitors for HR, ECG, rhythm, CO2 tracing and temperature

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Provided I am adequate oxygenating and ventilating the patient, I would deepen the anesthetic and do a target physical examination:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Pupils (inc. ICP)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Diaphoresis and flushing (carcinoid, pheo, thyroid)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Rigidity (MH, serotonin syndrome)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Peripheral perfusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Bladder distention (autonomic dysreflexia)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hyperthermia (thyroid storm, MH, serotonin syndrome)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Scan machine, infusions and recent meds administered

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Drug error (bolus or infusions)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Awareness - TIVA disconnect, circuit disconnect

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o tourniquet

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DDx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypoxia / hypercapnea

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Drugs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Intentional or unintentional administration  vasopressors, cocaine, MAOI, stimulants

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Withdrawal  EtOH, BDZ, oipoids, clonidine,  -blockers

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pain / light anesthesia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 surgical site

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 remote (e.g. distended bladder, tourniquet)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Patient factors

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 pre-existing HTN

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 increased ICP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 autonomic hyperreflexia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Endocrine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 hyperthyroidism

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 pheochromocytoma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 carcinoid syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Seritonin Syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 malignant hyperthermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 NMS

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Obsetrical Hypertension

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 PIH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Cocaine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Goiter - Difficult airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
End-organ dysfunction of Hypermetabolic state

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CVS: tachycardia, high output CHF, atrial fibrillation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Resp: respiratory muscle weakness

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CNS: anxiety, hyperacitivity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 MSK: skeletal muscle weakness, fatigue, tremor

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Other: exophthalmos (graves); Electrolyte disturbances; Altered pharmacokinetics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Thyroidectomy - Postoperative complications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Tracheomalacia, Hematoma, RLN palsy, pneumothorax, Hypocalceima from hypoparathyroidism (tetany, laryngospasm)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Risk of AMM with retrosternal goiter - positional dyspnea

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Antithyroid drugs and their adverse effects

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Agranulocytosis, thrombocytopenia, aplastic anemia, Lupus-like syndrome, hepatitis, cholestatic jaundice,hypoglycemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of thyroid storm (see below)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hyperthyroidsim

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Render patient euthyroid before elective surgery - resting HR should be < 85

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid SNS stimulation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications - pancuronium, ephedrine, atropine, epinephrine, ketamine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Monitor for signs of thyroid storm (temperature, hemodynamics)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Diagnosis and management of thyroid storm

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Etiology - Graves' disease (thyroid stimulating autoantibodies), excess TH replacement, toxic nodular goiter, thyroiditis, TSH-secreting tumors (rare); Symptoms of hyperthyroidism - anxiety, emotional lability, increased appetite

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Thyroid Storm - usually presents 6 to 18hrs post-op - 72 hr duration; Arrhythmia: beta RLN; Hypoparathyroidism - Hypocalcemia (stridor, neuromuscular excitement)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
weakness, tremor, palpitations, heat intolerance, increased perspiration, and weight loss despite a normal or Px: Vital+ temp & postural (HTN, tachy, hyperthermia); A/W for BMV, intubation, surgical (masses); CNS hyperactivity, agitation, confusion, lid lag; CVS - arrhythmia, CHF (high output), volume status, shock; MSK proximal muscle weakness, tremor Inv: CBC, lytes, Cr, Calcium, TSH, free T4 & T3, ECG (sinus tachy, afib, prolonged QTc), CXR +/- CT chest (neck mass); ECHO Optimization: euthyroid prior to elective surgery; if emergent - esmolol infusion (100-300ug/kg/min), propranolol, PTU, steroids, sodium iodide; Endocrine consult; continue antithyroid meds; benzodiazepines for anxiety Options: local, regional, GA Room Setup: CAS +5 lead, temp, Art line, foley +/-CVC (volume status); TEE for LV dysfunction; protect protuberant eyes Anesthetic Management: avoid SNS  - Deep anesthesia prior to stimulus, avoid ketamine, pancuronium, ephedrine, hypercarbia; AFOI if neck mass (consider armoured ETT); judicious NdMB (weakness); monitor for thyroid storm; treat hypotension with direct acting agents (phenylephrine); ensure reversal prior to emergence Disposition: HDU/ICU if high risk for thyroid storm blockers, lidocaine, digoxin; CHF - digoxin; Airway obstruction (thyroidectomy): hematoma, tracheomalacia,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Thyroid Storm

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency situation with a high mortality

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Supportive measures: fluid resuscitation, Cooling

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Esmolol 0.1-0.3 mg/kg/min, Propranolol  10-40mg ng, 1 mg/min IV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Propylthiouracil 100 - 400 mg po/ng/pr q6h

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Potassium iodide 5 gtts po/ng q6h or Sodium iodide 0.25g IV q6h

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hydrocortisone 100-200 mg IV q8h

<!-- PAGE=? -->
End-organ dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o CNS: decreased LOC (may require A/W management), CVA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o CVS: high output CHF, A. fib, MI

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Resp: muscle weakness and hypercarbia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Metabolic: hypermetabolic state and electrolyte abnormalities

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Differential diagnosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o pheochromocytoma, MH, NMS / serotonin syndrome, sepsis, light anesthesia, cocaine toxicity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o rhabdo distinguishes MH from thyroid storm

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Restore intravascular volume, cool, invasive monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Excess Sympathetics - Esmolol, Propanolol

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Reduce peripheral conversion - PTU, Steroids

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Reduce release of thyroid hormone - Steroids, iodideSodium iodide:  0.25mg IV/PO/NG q6h

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Reduce synthesis of thyroid hormone (PTU, methimazole, steroids)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Precipitants of thyroid storm - surgery, sepsis, anesthesia, labour, I-131 therapy, DKA, withdrawal of antithyroid meds, trauma, PIH; DDx: MH (rhabdo - CK, plasma and urine myoglobin, elevated K), Sepsis (Blood C+S)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: hyperthermia, tachycardia, hypercarbia, CHF, dehydration, hyperglycemia, changes in LOC, shock and death

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Inv: CBC, lytes, Creatinine, TSH, fT4, T3, TSH, ECG, CXR, +/- echo

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Management: Rapid diagnosis; Inc. Monitoring; Supportive management - active cooling (Demerol for shivering, IV fluid replacement (art line, CVC), glucose and electrolyte replacement, oxygen, Steroids hydrocortisone 100mg IV q8h; PTU - 200-400mg PO/PR q6h; methimazole 20-25mg PO (60-100mg PR) q6h; Iodine one hour after PTU - Na Iodide 1gm IV, lugol's solution 4-8 gtts PO, PR q6h; B-blockers for SNS Esmolol 100-300ug/kg/min, propranolol 10-40mg ng (1mg/min IV); plasmapheresis; Digoxin IV for CHF amiodarone may make crisis worse (esp if given prior to PTU)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: ICU setting, most likely to occur 6-18 hr post-op

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Main DDx of Intra-op hypotension:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hypoxemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hypovolemia (Preload) - Hemorrhage, surgical obstruction to venous return, ischemic reperfusinon

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Cardiogenic - rate (vagal), rhythm, contractility, ischemia, valves

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Obstructive - PE, AFE, VAE, pHTN, PTX, tamponade

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Distributive - anaphylaxis, SIRS, neuraxial, neurogenic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Drugs - relative anesthetic overdose

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Less common etiologies:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Endocrine (Addisons, Myxedema, Carcinoid), Metabolic (hypoCa, hypoglycemia)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Emergency - simultaneous diagnosis and management - Inform the surgeon  and call for help

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Dec. anesthetic, hand ventilate with 100% O2 and temporize with vasopressors +/-fluid, inotrope

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Cycle BP and scan the monitors for HR, rhythm, ST segment, SaO2, EtCO2, PAP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Feel for a pulse: if no pulse  ACLS protocol.  If pulse present  targeted physical exam

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Reassess  DDx based on findings

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Targeted PE: Urticaria, flushing, angioedema, tracheal deviation, s/c emphysema, air entry, JVP, CVP, PCWP, peripheral perfusion, check surgical field for blood loss, IVC compression etc.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypotension

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DDx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-induction hypotension:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic :  relative overdose, relative hypovolemia, anaphylaxis, arrhythmia Patient :  cardiac compression due to mediastinal mass, PTX, tamponade

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Obstetrical Hypotension: hemorrhage, High/total spinal, AFE, PE, aortocaval compression, Cardiomyopathy Medications (oxytocin)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Neurosurgery Hypotension: Arrhythmia (posterior fossa or brainstem surgery), Hypovolemia (mannitol, lasix), Hemorrhage, VAE, Neurogenic (if SCI); Management : lower HOB, flood field, Bone wax Trauma Hypotension: Hemorrhage (Occult), Tension PTX, Tamponade, Fat embolus, Cardiac contusion, Pulmonary contusion, Neurogenic shock, Drug intoxication (cocaine), Rare: Anaphylaxis, arrhythmia, sepsis Post-pneumonectomy Hypotension: Surgical - Hemorrhage, Cardiac herniation, Tension PTX (stump disruption, BPF); Anesthetic - High TEA, Sedation; Patient -Arrhythmia (afib), MI, pHTN/RVF; Management: Operative side UP, physical exam: A/W, PTX, CVP, check chest tube for blockage, turn of TEA, sedation, CXR, ECG, CBC, ABG.  Cardiac herniation:  to OR, d/c PEEP, minimize Paw, turn off suction to CT, 1-2L of air into thorax, inotropes prn

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Laparoscopic Hypotension: Vagal response to peritoneal distension, Compression of IVC, Hemorrhage, VAE, Tension PTX, Hypercarbia-induced arrhythmia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Refractory Shock: Ingestion/toxidrome, Adrenal insufficiency, Hypocalcemia, Hypovolemia (severe)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypothyroidism

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Etiology of hypothyroidism and adequacy of treatment

<!-- PAGE=? -->
associated AI disease, previous radiation, surgery, hypothalamic / pituitary dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential difficult airway - Enlarged tongue +/- goiter from chronic thyroiditis (Hashimoto's)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Decreased gastric motility with risk of aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multisystem effects

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CNS : exaggerated effects of sedatives & NdMB

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CVS : hypodynamic circulation, ↓CO, CHF (diastolic and systolic), pericardial effusion, inc. QT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Resp : Potential for mass lesion, pleural effusions, impaired ventilatory response to hypoxemia &  hypercarbia, exaggerated ventilatory-depressant response to drugs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Metabolic : hypothermia, hyponatremia (SIADH), hypoglycemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Endocrine : adrenal suppression (cortical atrophy)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for myxedema coma → may develop in previously asymptomatic patients

<!-- PAGE=? -->
mortality >50%, precipitated by stress (surgery, infection, trauma, MI, CVA)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Exaggerated features of hypothyroidism

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Dec. LOC, inc. sensitivity to NdMB & sedatives, myocardial & respiratory depression

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 high risk for delayed emergence and need for post-op ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Treatment of myxedema coma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 IV T3 0.2mcg/kg q6h (onset 6-24 hrs) or T4 300-500 mcg IV load then 100mcg IV q24

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hydrocortisone 100mg IV then 25mg q6h (common association with adrenal suppression)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Risk of myocardial ischemia with IV T3/T4 supplementation in those with CAD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Inquire about etiology - autoimmune diseases, RAI, radiation, thyroidectomy; Determine cause. Look for symptoms of over or undertreatment (hyperthyroid = palps, anxiety, weight loss, heat intolerance, diarrhea; hypo = dry skin, brittle nails, brittle hair, cold intolerance, constipation, fatigue, depression, weight gain, edema). Evaluate for GERD, positional dyspnea or cough, SVC syndrome; heart failure symptoms. Px: Vitals (orthostatic) volume status. A/W - large tongue, hoarsness, goiter, radiation injury. Eyes for positioning. Resp - effusions, hypoventilation; CVS - hypovolemia, bradycardia, HTN, CHF. DTRs (reduced) Investigations: CBC, lytes (SIADH, gluc), TSH, free T3/T4, ABG if resp depression; ECG (low voltage, long PR, QRS, QT, VT torsades), CXR (effusions), ECHO (contractility, effusion) +/- CT (mediastinal mass) Optimization: Delay elective case if symptomatic; Consult Endo +/- Cardio (risk of MI with CAD); Aspiration prophylaxis; Avoid preoperative sedation; Supplemental O2 and ventilatory support as indicated; Drain symptomatic pleural effusions; Restore intravascular volume; Euthyroid prior to elective surgery - thyroxine PO titrated to achieve normal TSH over 6-8 weeks; Emergency Surgery - Preoperative thyroid and glucocorticoid replacement (levothyroxine 400-500 ug IV load then 50-200ug/day, T3 has more rapid onset - liothyronine 0.15 - 0.3 ug/kg IV q6h, Hydrocortisone 100 mg IV then 25 mg IV q6h) Options: Regional is acceptable option if CNS, ventilation, and cardiac status are appropriate Room Setup: CAS+5lead, temp; nerve stimulator; Art line; forced air warmer; PAC/TEE if indicated Management: anticipate hypotension - consider ketamine; judicious NdMB - full reversal; consider ephedrine for hypotension - need some B agonist given cardiac dysfxn, may be refractory to catecholamines; multimodal analgesia (limit opioids); high risk for delayed emergance Dependent on degree of cardiorespiratory compromise. Low threshold for ventilation &

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Postop disposition: HDU; monitor for fluid and electrolyte derangements

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Perioperative Hypoxemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Low FIO2 - machine, circuit

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Airway - obstruction, malpostioned ETT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypoventilation -  A/W, Bronchospasm, PTX , light anesthesia / pain, dec. LOC (ventilator drive)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
V/Q mismatch - pre-existing lung disease, pulm edema (CHF), atelectasis, aspiration , infection, Cardiac arrest (dec. pulmonary perfusion), Obstruction (PE, VAE, AFE, FE)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anatomic Shunts - Cardiac lesions (PFO, ASD, VSD, PDA)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Low SvO2 -Low CO , anemia, hemorrhage, high VO2, hemoglobinopathies

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Emergency - simultaneous diagnosis and management - Inform the surgeon and call for help

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Scan monitors: rate, rhythm, BP, EtCO2, SaO2, PIP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hand ventilate with 100% O2 - increase PEEP, use larger volumes (recruitment maneuvers)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Check position of ETT: pass suction catheter, FO bronchoscope (mucus plug, aspiration)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Examine patient - cyanosis, rash, pulse, tracheal position, chest movement, B/L air entry, wheeze

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Support / Monitor Circulation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Develop DDx and treat

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ABG (A-a gradient, Hemoglobin), CXR, ECG

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pediatric Hypoxemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Aspiration (esp. FB), Laryngospasm, Post-obstructive pulmonary edema, Shunting (undiagnosed CHD), Endobronchial intubation (especially if small)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Obstetrical Hypoxemia/Dyspnea

<!-- PAGE=? -->
AFE, PE, Aspiration, High spinal, Pulmonary edema (cardiomyopathy or valvulopathy, autotx), Anemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Trauma/Burns Hypoxemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Airway obstruction, Airway disruption, Aspiration, PTX (simple or tension), CO toxicity, Pulmonary contusion, Hemothorax, Tamponade, Fat embolism, ARDS, Eschar around chest

<!-- PAGE=? -->
OLV Hypoxemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Malpositioning of ETT/DLT/blocker, Shunt through non-ventilated lung (inhibition of HPV), Atelectesis, PTX, low CO with potential RV failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Management - 100% FiO2, confirm correct placement and lung isolation, PEEP demendant lung, CPAP operative side, Clamp PA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Massive Transfusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
TRALI, ABO incompatibility

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Artifact

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Poor peripheral perfusion, Hypothermia, Methemoglobinemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased Airway Pressure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Definition : an increase in PIP of more than 5 cm H2O; or a PIP greater than 40 cm H2O

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DDx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Machine - stuck expiratory, inspiratory, APL, O2 flush valve, kinked scavenger, failed check valve

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ETT - malpositioned, blocked (mucous, FB), kinked, cuff herniation, size

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Inc airway resistance

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 bronchospasm

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 light anesthesia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 anaphylaxis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 foreign body

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 mucous/secretions

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 URTI

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Decreased lung compliance

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 ALI / ARDS, aspiration / pulmonary edema

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 restrictive lung disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pleura PTX, hemothorax, pleural effusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Dec. chest wall compliance - kyphoscoliosis, muscle rigidity, MH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased abdominal pressures

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 abdo compartment syndrome, obesity, insufflations, retractors, trendelenberg

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Management:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Emergency which requires simultaneous diagnosis and management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Inc. FiO2 to 1.0, inform the surgeon and call for help

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Initial Differential Dx:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Machine - Disconnect - assess lung compliance with ambu bag, patency of circuit

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o ETT - Check placement with laryngoscope and pass suction catheter to ensure patency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 if marked obstruction: deflate cuff and recheck, extubate (consider exchange catheter), mask / LMA ventilate to increase SaO2 then reintubate, consider FOB examination if difficulties

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 If patient problem, initial management includes:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Deepen anesthetic with volatile (Sevo) or IV (e.g. Lido or Ketamine)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Ensure paralysis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o auscultate bilaterally for symmetry, breath sounds, wheezes, rales, crackles

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Asymmetry

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 endobronchial tube - examine and reposition ETT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 pneumothorax - assess BP, HR, palpate trachea, percuss chest

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Wheezing or silence: bronchospasm - deepen, ventolin, epinephrine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Crackles: pulmonary edema - PEEP, lasix, morphine, NTG...

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o If hypoxemic or ↓ BP, initiate epinephrine (can bolus or put 1 mg in 1000 mls and run as an infusion)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 exclude other causes:  MH, light anesthesia, inadequate muscle relaxation, opioids, surgical

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Principles of medical ethics:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Autonomy : right to self-determination

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Non-maleficence : Obligation to -do no harm‖ intentionally

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Beneficence : moral obligation to act for the benefit of others - do good‖

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Justice : obligation of fairness, entitlement to care & equity in its delivery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Fidelity : right to confidentiality

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Informed Consent:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Decision Making Capacity: :

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ability to make a particular decision at a specific time

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Voluntariness: Participate without coercion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Disclosure: The goal of disclosure is to provide information relevant to the decision-maker and the decision to be made (professional practice standard vs reasonable person standard vs subjective person standard (opera singer)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Recommendation: What the anaesthesiologist would recommend based on professional opinion. Understanding: Patient needs to understand the risks and benefits of the proposed procedure Decision: The patient should be encouraged to form a decision or be involved in the decision making process Autonomous authorization: To respect the paitents autonomy, the patient should give his/her consent for the procedure based on informed consent as an expression of the patients self determination

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ethics/ Informed Consent

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Approaches to pediatric consent

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Age

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Decision-Making Capacity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Technique *

<!-- PAGE=? -->
<6 years

<!-- PAGE=? -->
None

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Best interests standard

<!-- PAGE=? -->
6-12 years

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Developing

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Informed permission / Informed assent

<!-- PAGE=? -->
12-18 years

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mostly developed

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Informed assent / informed permission

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mature minor

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Developed, as legally determined by a judge

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Informed consent

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emancipated minor

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Developed, as determined by a situation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Informed consent

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Assent

<!-- PAGE=? -->
1. Helping the patient achieve a developmentally appropriate awareness of the nature of his or her condition

<!-- PAGE=? -->
2. Telling the patient what he or she can expect with tests and treatment

<!-- PAGE=? -->
3. Making a clinical assessment of the patient's understanding of the situation and the factors influencing how he or

<!-- PAGE=? -->
she is responding, including whether there is inappropriate pressure to accept testing or therapy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
4. Soliciting an expression of the patient's willingness to accept the proposed care

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Informed Consent (7) Components

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Decision Making Capacity: The ability to make a decision at a specific time which includes capacity to understand problems, proposed Rx, alternatives, options to refuse treatment, and forseeable consequences, and express a preference based on rational, internally consistent reasoning.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Voluntariness - Pt participates willingly w/o coercion or manipulation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Disclosure - To provide pt with info relevant to decision. (3) standards of disclosure: The professional practice standard, the reasonable (objective) person standard, and the subjective person standard (eg opera singer). Negligence related to informed consent is determined if -Materiality‖ assesses whether the info given met the std of care, -Causation‖ then assesses whether sharing the omitted info would have caused the pt to choose a different option

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Understanding - Patients need to understand the risks and benefits, distress does not seem to compromise the ability to recall risks, particularily amoung parturients. Recall and understanding are not correlated.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Recommendation - Anesthesiologists should offer an opinion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Decision - The Anesthesiologist should make substantial effort for to educate the patient prior to making a decision rather than to accept at face value the patients refusal to be educated. If the patient chooses a technique which the anesthesiologist believes to be inappropriate, they are not ethically obligated to provide care in non-emergent situations.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Autonomous authority - Obtaining informed consent is how we acknowledge the responsibility to respect a patient's right to self-determination.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Controversies:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergencies : Assume patient wants life-saving measures unless declared otherwise. Determine if intervention is reversible, if so, proceed.  If irreversible make all attempts to clarify patients wishes in advance.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Moral Objections : Anesthesiologist is not obligated to subjugate their morales, however they must make a reasonable effort to find a competent and willing replacement. They should perform care in life-or-death circumstances.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Confidentiality :  May disregard if a patient makes a credible threat to harm someone else.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pediatric informed assent : -Informed assent‖ acknowledges that although most pediatric patients cannot legally consent to medical care, pediatric patients should share in decision making to the extent their development permits. Help the patient understand a developmentally appropriate awareness of the nature of her condition, what he/she should expect with proposed Rx, assess patients understanding , and solicite an expression of the patient's willingness to accept the proposed procedure.  Generally < 6 years don't have decision making capacity > surrogate decision makers. 6-12 years DMC is developing, use informed assent, permission. 12-18 years, mostly developed DMC, Informed assent/permission. Mature Minor, developed as legally determined by judge -informed consent.‖ Emancipated minor, developed as determined by situation -informed consent‖

<!-- PAGE=? -->
IVRA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Indications: Anesthesia to entire extremity distal to tourniquet: limited to 60-90mins.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Contraindications: Usual + infection at site of needle insertion, coagulopathy (relative), pre-existing neuro deficits (relative), Raynaud's or Scleroderma, Sicke Cell due to tourniquet, open wounds, obesity (may exceed capabilities of tourniquet), partial heart block (tourniquet release may precip. complete HB) ie. RBBB/LBBB, bifasicular block).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Slow onset, may require 20 min, local anesthetic toxicity, inadequate block (better exsanguination = better block), hematoma (avoid multiple punctures), skin tears (minimize shear forces with Esmarch bandage, for fragile skin elevate arm for 3 mins prior to applying bandage + brachial artery compression.  Post op pain, ecchymosis, nerve injury related to ischemia, usually transient.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Technique: Standard CAS monitors , 20-22g IV, Esmarch bandage, double-cuff pneumatic tourniquet. Exsanguinate arm for 1-3 mins (elevate, then apply esmarch). Inflate tourniquet 100-150mmHg above SBP (at least 250mmHg). Remove Esmarch, confirm pallor and pulselessness.  Then inject local . anesthetic. Lidocaine 3mg/kg or 40 mL of 0.5%

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Bupivicaine contraindicated due to CVS  toxicity, Chloroprocaine contraindicated due to risk of thrombopheblitis.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Adjuvants: Guanethidine 10mg for 1 st  Rx, then 20mg for 2 nd  U/E, 40mg for L/W Reserpine 1-1.5mg (total) NSAIDs for improved analgesia 20-60mg Clonidine 1mcq/kg (not available in Canada)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Deflation: <20 mins = don't 20-40 mins = deflate for 10s, inflate for 1 min, deflate (delays onset but not peak serum levels) >40 min: deflate

<!-- PAGE=? -->
For longer cases and tourniquet pain inflate distal cuff (over anesthetized area) then deflate proximal cuff.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
For expected long cases, deflate after maximum time limit reached, allow limb to reperfuse x 5 mins, then repeat Bier Block with 50% original dose.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prehepatic:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hemolysis, Hematoma, Blood transfusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intrahepatic:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Drug induced : ETOH, Toxins

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Infectious: Hepatitis ABC

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Shocked Liver

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Sepsis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 TPN (acalculus choecystitis)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 congenital conjugation defects

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hypoxia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Posthepatic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Gallstone, mechanical obstruction or acalculus cholecystitis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Tests: CBC/Lytes/Haptoglobin/Coombs/Smear/LFTs/Bili/GGT/Alk-P/Hepatic U/S / Hepatitis Serology/ Toxicology Screen (EtoH/Tylenol)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations of fulminant hepatic failure: Considerations of maintaining hepatic perfusion pressure, correcting coagulopathy, avoiding toxins. Recognize increased risk of Post-op ventilation  and encephalopathy and ICU. Consider altered PK/PDs.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DDx Post-op Jaundice

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Jehovah's Witness

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Jehovah's Witnesses are an international religious organization that rejects much of modern mainstream Christianity in favour of what they believe is a restored form of first-century Christianity.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of perioperative morbidity and mortality secondary to massive blood loss and patient refusal of allogenic blood products (RBCs, WBCs, platelets, plasma)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Legal and ethical issues of consent specifically regarding JW minors and in emergency scenarios

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations of preoperative optimization of hematocrit (eg iron and Erythropoietin)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations of intra-operative blood conservation techniques including hypotensive techniques, antifibrinolytics, hemodilution, cell saver

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Specific obstetrical considerations

<!-- PAGE=? -->
In cases of mother vs. fetus , courts have ruled in favour of blood transfusions when fetus considered viable

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Consider (and discuss) hysterectomy for life-threatening hemorrhage

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Epidural blood patches are generally accepted (Watchtower)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maximize pre-operative HCT, minimize blood loss (antifibrinolytics, controlled hypotension, hemodilution), discuss cell salvage techniques (cell saver), factor VII!!

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Consider Regional Technique, tourniquets

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Document Refusal of Blood Products

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Conflicts: Parents vs. pediatric patients incapable of giving consent (courts have uniformly intervened to deny the ability to refuse transfusion therapy), Pediatric patients nearing the age of consent

<!-- PAGE=? -->
HX : Cardiopulmonary status, previous anemia, personal beliefs, cell-saver. Optimization: If elective, delay surgery until hematocrit/red cell mass is optimized with iron +/- erythropoietin (300U/kg SC x 3 injections/week for 3 - 4 weeks). D/C Anticoagulants. Heme Consult, blood utilization program. JW Hospital Liason. Legal counsel if dealing with minors. Consider pre-operative angiographic embolization. Venofer (IV iron sucrose 100mg iron) - Side effects include hypotension, GI symptoms, muscle cramps, headaches Intraoperative: Arterial line, minimize venipuncture, +- cell saver, controlled hypotension, regional, meticulous surgical technique, tourniquet, antifibrinolytics, hgb solutions if available, avoid coagulopathy Tranexamic acid reversibly binds plasminogen. S/E: hypotension, N/V, abd cramps, thromboembolic, retinal degeneration with prolonged use. E-aminocaproic acid reversibly binds plasminogen, 6-10x less potent than TXA. Side effects include hypotension, sinus bradycardia, GI symptoms, CNS symptoms, anaphylactic reactions (paraben hypersensitivity), agranulocytosis, and rhabdomyolysis (rare) Aprotinin Inhibits many serine proteases including; trypsin, chymotrysin, plasmin (inhibition of fibrinolysis) , and kallikrein (inhibition of factor XIIa - anaphylactic/toid reactions. Topical Collagen - causes platelet aggregation and initiates clotting cascade. POST-OP : Severe anemia > Consider sedation, ventilation, temperature control, iron supplementation, ICU.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hemodynamic Goals

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Maintain Rate, Rhythm, preload, and contractility

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Avoid extremes of afterload

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Avoid air bubbles

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Pregnancy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Slowly titrated epidural (dec. SVR - reversal of shunt - hypoxia)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Assisted 2 nd  stage - RV failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Avoid inc. pHTN - hypoxemia, hypercapnea, acidemia, hypothermia, pain

<!-- PAGE=? -->
L to R shunt

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Consideration primary lesion  ASD or VSD ,or PDA ( L -R  shunt )

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Consideration of eisenmenger  syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PTH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
RV dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Physiological interaction with pregnancy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 afterload suring labour can  L-R shunt and result in pHTN and RV failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
dec. SVR  exacerbate the severity  R-L shunt if preexisiting pHTN
