PPV and neuromuscular blockade

<!-- PAGE=? -->
May require emergency surgical airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals / Conflicts

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Identify the injury and evaluate extent

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid PPV and neuromuscular blockade until airway controlled distal to injury Identify associated injuries

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
: high index of suspicion for occult injury - airway, vascular, pulmonary, esophageal (esp with penetrating

<!-- PAGE=? -->
neck injury); AMPLE hx - mechanism of injuty

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Px : 25% of patients have no external evidence of injury - neck trauma, subcutaneous air leaks & emphysema, dyspnea, hoarseness or voice change, hemoptysis, stridor, dysphagia, cervical pain, flattening of thyroid cartilage, eccymosis in neck

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Inv: CXR - pneumothorax, pneumomediastinum, subcutaneous air; c-spines - paravertebral air; CT neck - quantify disruption, associated injuries; Laryngoscopy / Bronchoscopy / esophagoscopy are mandatory; CTA or angiography to assess for vascular injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Setup : If stable, transfer to OR; difficult airway equipment (FOB); equipment and personnel for immediate rigid bronch, tracheostomy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Airway management : if time, delineate injuries prior to airway instrumentation; consider AFOI (difficult topicalization); consider awake trach; if GA required - SV (inhalational, TIVA) vs. RSI (NO Cricoid or PPV); Confirmation of tracheal intubation - EtCO2, CXR, FOB

<!-- PAGE=? -->
LASERS (Light Amplification by Simulated Emission of Radiation)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Patient safety and potential complications : atmosphere contamination, perforation of a vessel or structure, embolism, inappropriate energy transfer.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Atmospheric  Contamination (mean size 0.31um) small enough to reach alveoli. Note most surgical masks filter particles down to 3um. Potential mutagenic/carcinogenic biproducts.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Tissue and Vessel Perfortion : Vessels > 5mm are not coagulable by laser, pneumothorax. With Nd:YAG laser perforation or bleeding may not be apparent until edema and necrosis become maximal several days post-op

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Embolism : Nd:YAG laser system associated with venous gas embolism due to the gas coolant

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Energy Tx to inappropriate locations (reflected or transmitted through air)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Operating room safety and appropriate precautions (eyewear, appropriate masks, window covers and warning signs)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prevention and possible emergency management of airway fires (low fiO2, avoidance N2O, specialized ETT, potential for jet ventilation, intermittent laser use).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Patient Safety: Eyes taped closed, cover with saline soaked gauze

<!-- PAGE=? -->
OR staff Safety: Laser specific lenses, wraparound goggles, all windows covered and warning signs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ease of ignition with Nd:Yag: PVC > Red Rubber > silicone

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ease of ignitition with CO2: PVC > Silicone > red rubber

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ETT Tube Fires: Incidence 0.5-1.5% - Any hardocarbon material (tissue/plastic/rubber) can ignite Puncturing cuff and O2 enriched gas increase chance of fire. 3 Preventative strategies: 1) Reduce flammability of ETT 2) Removal of flammable materials from A/W using metallic venture jet ventilation cannula 3) Reduction of O2 content of inhaled gas

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ease of ignition with Nd:Yag: PVC > Red Rubber > silicone

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ease of ignitition with CO2: PVC > Silicone > red rubber

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Options: Wrap ETT with reflective tape, protecting ETT cuff with laser resistant cuffs, saline filled cuffs with methylene blue for early detection, covering cuff with pledgets, Metal ETTs (Laser Flex), Jet Ventilation, intermittent Apnea. Reduce FiO2 < 0.4. Avoid volatiles as they can form toxic compounds in the presence of an airway fire (not inherently flammable).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Airway Fire Protocol: 1) Remove source immediately 2) OR staff notified, call code 3) Flamming material extinguished in bucket of water/saline (keep available) 3) Ventilation resumed with 100% O2 once extinguished by mask 4) Direct laryngoscopy/Rigid bronch/FOB to assess damage +/- saline lavage 5) Reintubation if any a/w damage 6) Tracheostomy if severe 7) Assess oropharynx for burns 8) CXR 9) Consider steroids?

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Lithium Toxicity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Toxicity occurs with serum levels > 2mEq/L, with signs of skeletal muscle weakness, ataxia, sediation, widening of QRS.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mulisystem effects of toxicity:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CNS: Sedation, decreased LOC, Seizures

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CVS: Wide QRS, AV block, hypotension

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Resp: potentiate NdMB

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Renal: Nephrogenic DI >> Fluid and electrolyte imbalance

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Treatment:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medical emergency requiring Hemodialysis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Diuresis - Loop or osmotic diuretics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Thiazide diuretics increase lithium resorption in proximal tubule

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid NSAIDS and ACEi's which decrease lithium excretion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Supportive management, correct fluid and electrolyte abn's of DI

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Liver Failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Underlying etiology and associated concerns

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Viral hepatitis, drugs (ETOH, Tylenol), Autoimmune, Hemochromatosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
End-organ Dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CNS - encephalopathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CVS - hyperdynamic (inc.CO, dec. SVR), cardiomyopathy, portal hypertension

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Resp  - chronic hypoxemia (V/Q mismatch, intrapulmonary AV shunts), RLD (ascities)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Renal -hepatorenal syndrome, CRF

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hem - anemia, coagulopathy (thrombocytopenia, dec. clotting factors), immunodeficiency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Endo - hypoglycemia, hyponatremia, lactic acidosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 GI - esophageal varices

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Altered pharmacology (inc Vd, dec. protein binding, dec. hepatic clearance)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
TBW excess with dec. effective circulating volume (dec. albumn)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Identify and optimize multi-organ dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Delay elective cases until optimized

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Correct hypovolemia, coagulopathy, acute hepatitis is a contraindication to surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Universal precautions

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: determine etiology & associated comorbidities (hemochromatosis - restrictive cariomyopathy, ETOH - dilated cariomyopathy); Identify end-organ dysfunction - encephalopathy, varices, hepatopulm/renal syndromes, dyspnea, ascites/SBP; Ongoing treatment and response to date. PE: Vitals, postural BP, GCS, temp, volume status. Cardiopulmonary exam assessing for high output heart failure, portopulmonary HTN, pleural effusions (supine vs upright sat can indicate hepatopulmonary syndrome), sigmata of chronic liver disease (caput, spider nevi, clubbing, asterixis, hepatosplenomeg), icterus Investigations: CBC (anemia, thrombocytopenia), lytes (hyponatremia), BUN, Cr (renal failure), coags, Ca, Mg, Cross Match, glucose, albumin, bili (Child-pugh), CXR (pleural effusions), ECG (pHTN), PFTs (restrictive), ECHO (PAP, EF, cardomyopathy Optimization: Consultation with GI/hepatologist - treat encephalopathy, evaluate for varices, Correct coagulopathies (vit K, FFP), electrolytes, anemia , volume deficit. Risks stratify with Child-pugh, Aspiration prophylaxis, Optimize nutritional status. If RLD is severe, then thoracentesis or paracentesis may be required. Anesthetic Options: local, GA, Regional - contraindicated with massive hemorrhage, inc. infect risk - if required, single shot (coagulopathy may recur) Room Setup: CAS + 5, temp, nerve stim, pre-induction A-Line, Blood warmer, large IV access with rapid infuser, CVP, PAC/TEE rarely (if varices banded for the latter), ICP monitoring can be discussed in setting of fulminant hepatic failure, PRBC, pressors and infusions Intraoperative Mgt: RSI vs. Hemodynamic instability, Anticipate altered pharmacokinetics - use propofol, fentanyl, remifentanil, cisatracurium. Follow glucose, colloid for volume, follow U/O Post-op: High dependency unit. Low threshold for postop ventilation Complications: Delayed emergence (encephalopathy, inc.ICP, drugs), ARF, Hemorrhage (surgical vs. medical, variceal bleed - octreotide 25-50 ug/kg/hr, vasopression, blakemore tube), Sepsis, transfusion reactions, ETOH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
withdrawal

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Urgent Case

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations of ESLD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Underlying etiology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Physiologic & metabolic derangement - encephalopathy, high output cardiac failure, pHTN, chronic hypoxia, coagulopathy, renal failure, varices

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of massive transfusion - Perioperative coagulopathy and management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hemodynamic instability

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Liver manipulation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o IVC clamping

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Post-reperfusion syndrome (acidosis,  cardiac output,  SVR,  BP)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of hypothermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Postoperative disposition (ICU)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimize end-organ dysfunction - volume resuscitate, correct coagulopathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Preparation for major blood loss

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Correct coagulopathy, Good IV access, cell-saver, fluid warmers, rapid infuser, Coordination with blood bank, consider antifibrinolytics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Preparation for 3 stages of liver transplantation and hemodynamic effects

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Dissection, Anhepatic, Reperfusion/neohepatic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Liver Transplant

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: determine etiology & associated comorbidities (hemochromatosis - restrictive cariomyopathy, ETOH dilated cariomyopathy); Identify end-organ dysfunction - encephalopathy, varices, hepatopulm/renal syndromes, dyspnea, ascites/SBP; Ongoing treatment and response to date. PE: Vitals, postural BP, GCS, temp, volume status. Cardiopulmonary exam assessing for high output heart failure, portopulmonary HTN, pleural effusions (supine vs upright sat can indicate hepatopulmonary syndrome), sigmata of chronic liver disease (caput, spider nevi, clubbing, asterixis, hepatosplenomeg), icterus Investigations: CBC, lytes (hyponatremia), BUN, Cr, coags, Ca, Mg, Cross Match, glucose, albumin, bili (Child-pugh), CXR (pleural effusions), ECG (pHTN), PFTs (restrictive), ECHO (PAP, EF, cardomyopathy) Optimization: Consultation with GI/hepatologist - treat encephalopathy, evaluate for varices, Correct coagulopathies (vit K, FFP), electrolytes, anemia , volume deficit. Risks stratify with Child-pugh, Aspiration prophylaxis, Optimize nutritional status. If RLD is severe, then thoracentesis or paracentesis may be required. Room Setup: CAS + 5, temp, nerve stim, pre-induction pre-induction A-Line, Blood warmer, 2-3 large IVs with rapid infuser, CVP, PAC/TEE rarely (if varices banded for the latter), ICP monitoring can be discussed in setting of fulminant hepatic failure, PRBC (10 units to start), pressors Cacium, and infusions Intraoperative Mgt: Induction: RSI/ETT. Maintenance: Balanced anesthesia. Maintain relaxation with Cis (or atracurium). Minimize crystallize. Albumin 5% or, less optimally, PS/VV for fluid resuscitation. Monitor lytes Stages: Dissection : Results in bleeding/hypovolemia - volume resuscitate and maintain renal perfusion Anhepatic: Clamping results in dec. preload, dec. CO, dec. renal perfusion, dec. citrate clearance (with associated citrate toxicity), fibrinolysis - volume load, vasopressors, consider veno-veno bypass Neohepatic/reperfusion: most unstable period, abrupt increased in K+, H+, dec. temperature, release of vasoactive substances. Postreperfusiion syndrome - hypotension, bradycardia, arrhythmia - preemptive bicarb, Calcium, hyperventilation, insulin/glucose, vasopressors, ?free radical scavengers (methylene blue) Post-op: Conservative management involves transferring to ICU ventilated and weaning over 6-8 hours.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prevent and recognize toxicity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Toxic doses, monitoring, mild signs and symptoms (Analgesia, Lightheadedness, Tinnitus, Numbness of tongue)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency management of CNS toxicity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
seizures, coma and respiratory arrest

<!-- PAGE=? -->
airway management and hyperventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency management of CVS toxicity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
arrhythmias, hypotension, and cardiac arrest

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ACLS, escalating doses of Epinephine, Vasopression

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intralipid therapy (1.5ml/kg may rpt q5 to max 3ml/kg followed by 0.25ml/kg/min)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Early consideration fo CPB

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevention of toxicity: aspiration, test doses, slow infusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid exacerbating factors: acidosis, hypercarbia, hypoxia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prompt administration of possible antidote: Intralipid 20%

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Local Anesthetic Toxicity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Presentation: initial sx of CNS toxicity - tinnitus, visual disturbance/diplopia, lightheadedness, metallic taste, circumoral numbness - Progression to myoclonus, grand mal seizures, coma & respiratory arrest Cardiotoxicity usually follows neurotoxicity; ~10% may present with arrhythmias, hypotension and CVS collapse rather than seizures - Arrhythmias include conduction delay, BBB, prolonged PR interval, complete heart block, sinus arrest, or asystole - ventricular ectopy, and malignant arrhythmias such as ventricular tachycardia, torsades de pointes, and ventricular fibrillation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Toxic doses: Chloroprocaine 12mg/kg, Cocaine 1.5-3mg/kg, Bupivicaine 2-3mg/kg, Lido 4.5-7mg/kg (w/ epi), Ropivicaine 3mg/kg

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Rates of Absorpstion: Arterial > venous > Tracheal > Intercostal > Caudal > Paracervical > Epidural > Brachial Plexus > Sciatic/Femoral > Subcutaneous > Topical

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prevention: Aspirate, give incremental doses, test doses with epinephrine (15mcg should increase HR by 10 bpm, SBP by 15mmHg, or lead to a 25% decrease in T-wave amplitude in lead II (peak in peds), wait 40-60 seconds, max BP response at 90 seconds. When using tissue depots, limit dose and use epinephrine Optimization: Benzo's raise seizure threshold, avoid hypoventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Management: Stop the injection / Maintain oxygenation and ventilation / avoid hypoxemia, hypercarbia, and acidosis - Thio, midaz, prop for Sz - Mild CVS depression (brady, hTN) ephedrine, atropine - Profound CVS depression and malignant dysrhythmias, ACLS, escalating epi, vasopressin, amio, intralipid - avoid Ca channel blockers

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Note: Intralipid may cause pulmonary vasoconstriction, pancreatitis.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Long QTc Syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hemodynamic compromise / collapse from rapid polymorphic VT (Torsade de Pointes) and sudden cardiac death

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimize QTc

<!-- PAGE=? -->
B-blockade, Lt stellate ganglion block

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications: Butyrophenones (Droperidol), Quinidine, TCAs, ketamine, Lidocaine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Electrolytes: Acute hypokalemia, hypoMg, hypoCa,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
SNS activation: hypothermia, hypoxia, hypercarbia, acidosis, stress, anxiety, auditory stim

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Valsalva

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Consider underlying etiology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Congential (catecholamine dependant) vs. acquired (pause dependant)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pacemaker / AICD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Recognize & optimize patients with prolonged QTc

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid prolongation of QTc

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o SNS stimulation, physical stress, anxiety, auditory stimuli

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o bradycardia in acquired long QT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Medications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Rapidly recognize and treat TdP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx and PE: FMHx of sudden death, associated congenital abnormalities, syncope, arrhythmias Investigations: Lytes (K, Ca, Mg) ; ECG (prolonged QTc ( F >480 msec, M>470 msec)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: EP study; B-blockade; Left SGB if refractory to medical therapy or ER surgery ; Correct Lytes (K + , Mg 2+ , Ca 2+ ) ; Continue antiarrhythmics; Cardioversion/defib pads on patient ; Anxiolysis Anesthetic Options: Local; GA; RA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: Resus drugs (phenyl and ephedrine) ; esmolol ; Mg 2+ ; ACLS drugs; DEFIB & CRASH CART Intraoperative Mgt: Propofol shortens Qtc; Deep prior to a/w instrumentation; TIVA optimal; Volatiles prolong QT but used safely; Avoid N2O and abrupt rise in Des (SNS +); Consider deep extubation; Avoid reversal atropine, glycol  & antiemetics  (droperidol & ondansetron) they all prolong QTc;

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Monitored bed; quiet atmosphere; Good pain control (Methadone prolongs QTc); consider Phenytoin in severe QTc prolongation (it shortens QTc)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Drugs: Prolongs QT: thiopental, ketamine, Iso, Sevo, Sux, pancuronium, Sufentanil, Neostigmine, edrophonium, atropine, glycopyyrolate, Epinephrine, Norepinephrine, class I & III antiarrythmics, haldol, droperidol, quetiapine, risperidone, SSRIs, Macrolide Abx, 5-HT agonists, cisapride

<!-- PAGE=? -->
No QT prolongation: Propofol, etomidate, methohexital, Halothane, vecuronium, atracurium, alfentanil, fentanyl, midazolam, phenylephrine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations of a vasculopath

<!-- PAGE=? -->
comorbidities: HTN, CAD, DM, renal insuff, CVA, COPD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
increased risk periop CV event (stroke, MI)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
inc HD monitoring/tight HD control

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Type of anesthetic and suitability - GA vs regional

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Etiology of occlusion/Urgency of surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Acute (emergency case, risks limb viability)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Chronic vascular atherosclerosis -high risk pt with time for optimization

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prevention and recognition of perioperative complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
MI, CHF, HTN

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mitigate stress response - adequate analgesia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Graft patency - IV hydration, avoid hypothermia, spinal anesthetic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Acute thrombosis and Graft dehiscence

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevention of periop complications - ischemia, CHF, CVA, renal insufficiency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Optimization of oxygenation, perfusion of end organs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Adequate intra-op, post-op analgesia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o HD control, volume status

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Promoting graft patency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Early recognition of postop graft thrombosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Adequate hydration, perfusion, warm limb to avoid vasoconstriction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Lower limb Revascularization

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx & Px: Indication for surgery - claudication, ischemic rest pain or ulceration, gangrene; Etiology  - acute arterial occlusion (embolic source? Afib, recent MI, prosthetic valves, aneurysm, paradoxical embous) vs. chronic vascular insufficiency/atherosclerosis; thorough assessment for comorbid disease; contraindications to regional

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Inv: CBC, lytes Cr, BUN, Type and screen, coags, ECG +/- echo, PFT, baseline ABG, CXR as appropriate

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: aspiration prophylaxis if emergent, diabetic,  if elective consider need for cardiology/resp workup/optimization

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Monitoring: 5 lead ECG with ST analysis, artline, +/- CVC, large IV,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Plan: consult w/ surgeon Re: length of case, expected blood loss, cell salvage, Spinal, Epidural, GA all reasonable, depends on procedure and pt comorbidity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intra-op considerations: Intraop IV Heparin (Delay heparin 1 h after needle, Remove catheter 2-4 h after last heparin dose and patient's coagulation status evaluated, Re-heparinize 1 h after catheter removal, Bloody/difficult tap may increase risk; no data to support mandatory delay, discuss with surgeon), Potential uncontrolled bleeding, HD swings - laryngoscopy, emergence, tunnelling for graft, Ischemic Reperfusion Syndrome (hypotension, hyperkalemia, acidosis, myoglobinuria - ATN

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Optimize hemodynamics to prevent myocardial ischemia , Ensure adequate analgesia , Monitor graft patency (Acute thrombosis - urgent take back, expect significant blood loss with thrombectomy, Graft dehiscence - massive bleeding, hypovolemic shock requiring resusc and urgent take back)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Indications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Relative vs. Absolute (see below)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Relative Contraindications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 High aspiration risk

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Severe hypoxemia (intolerant of brief periods of apnea)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Tracheal stenosis or obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Difficult airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Technique

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 DLT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Bronchial blocker

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Endobronchial ETT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Trauma (laryngeal, tracheal laceration)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Tube malposition

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Cuff herniation/obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Rapid and accurate placement of lung isolation device

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Common conflicts:  aspiration, difficult airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Lung Isolation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Absolute Indications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevention of contamination

<!-- PAGE=? -->
1.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Unilateral pulmonary hemorrhage    2. Unilateral infection (prevention of contamination)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Control of distribution of ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
1.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Giant unilateral bullae                       4. Bronchopleural/bronchocutaneous fistula

<!-- PAGE=? -->
2.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Tracheobronchial tree disruption       5. Surgical opening of major conducting airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Life-threatening hypoxemia d/t unilateral lung disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Unilateral bronchopulmonary lavage (alveolar proteinosis)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Relative Indications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Surgical Exposure (high priority):  thoracic aortic aneurysm, pneumonectomy, upper lobectomy, mediastinal exposure, thoracoscopy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Surgical Exposure (medium priority):  middle / lower lobectomy, esophageal resection, procedures on thoracic spine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post CPB status after removal of totally occluding chronic unilateral pulmonary emboli

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Significant hypoxemia from unilateral lung disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Predictors of low arterial oxygen saturation during OLV: 1)  Side of Surgery (right side has 10% more blood flow than left) 2) Poor  PaO2 on Two Lung Ventilation 3) Pre-operative percentage of predicted FEV1 (inverse correlation) 4) Supine position

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Management of hypoxemia on OLV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Manual ventilation, FiO2 1.0, notify surgeon

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Check position of DLT/blocker with FOB

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CPAP to non-dependent lung, PEEP to ventilated lung

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Insufflation of non-dependent lung with 1-2L/min oxygen

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intermittent 2 lung ventilation, Clamp operative lung PA to eliminate shunt

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Assessment of graft function

<!-- PAGE=? -->
rule out chronic rejection (BAL, biopsy) & active infection (immunosuppressed)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Assessment of non-transplanted lung function

<!-- PAGE=? -->
differential lung compliance

<!-- PAGE=? -->
potential for pHTN, cor pulmonale, and RVF

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Physiology of denervated lung

<!-- PAGE=? -->
impaired cough reflex and mucociliary function

<!-- PAGE=? -->
inc. risk of bronchoconstriction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Knowledge of anastomotic location, with placement of ETT under direct vision

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Immunosuppression and resulting end-organ dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations for the planned surgical procedure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals / Conflicts

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Minimize injury to allograft and native lung

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o meticulous aseptic technique

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o avoid instrumentation of lung

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o lung protective ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o avoid excessive intraoperative fluids

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o prompt recovery of resp function (early extubation)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Lung Transplant Recipient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
COMPLICATIONS OF LUNG TRANSPLANT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Primary Graft Failure (15-35%)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pneumonia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Acute Graft Rejection (50%)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Bronchial Stenosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Chronic Graft Rejection (aka Bronchiolitis obliterans)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
History and Physical

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 What surgery?

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Function of the allograft/SLTx vs DLTx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Evidence of bronchial narrowing, other disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Usual labs -esp  CBC, kidney function

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CXR - evidence of rejection or infection (but may be normal in presence of both)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Spirometry and ABG mandatory

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
postpone if evidence of infection;  stress steroids; prophylactic abx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic options:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
neuraxial/regional may be preferred if possible

<!-- PAGE=? -->
GA: careful placement of ETT  - avoid site of anastomosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
-Prone to infection, early extubation, judicious fluids, prone to bronchoconstr'n

<!-- PAGE=? -->
-If SLTx, consider different lung compliance in native vs transplanted lung

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
hypoxemia, trauma to native or transplanted lung

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Malignant Hyperthermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthesia induced-hypermetabolic state characterized by rigidity, rhabdomyolysis, hyperkalemic arrest, ARF, DIC and cerebral edema

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Rocognize susceptiple patients a provide a trigger free anesthetic (volatiles/Sux)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Early recognition, declaration of emergency and continuous therapy (dantrolene, cooling, ICU)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid triggers (volatiles and Sux) in MH susceptible patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Early recognition and Rx: D/C triggering agents, correct hypoxemia / hypercarbia by hyperventilating on 100% O2 at >10L min, reverse hypermetabolic state with dantrolene, correct metabolic acidosis with HCO3-, treat hyperkalemia, dysrhythmia control (avoid CCBs!), Cool patient until Core < 38 degrees.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Continue management after acute episode to prevent secondary complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Personal or FmHx of MH, intolerance to caffeine containing foods, previous testing, hx of unexplained fevers or cramps. 3 associated disorders: CCD (Central Core Disease), King-Denborough syndrome, Evans myopathy. Generally normal PE unless they have associated myopathy.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: Electrolytes, Crt, CK (70% of MH patients have elevated resting CK), urine for myoglobin, ECG may have ventricular dysrhythmias), Coags, ABG. Special: Caffeine-halothane contracture test = gold standard, sensitivity 98-100%, specificity of 73-93% . Genetic testing has low sens ~25%.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Dantrolene prophylaxis not recommended, avoid triggers consider arterial line. MH anesthetic machine or clean machine with 100% o2 at 10L/min for 10mins. Replace all disposable circuits, fresh gas outlet hoses, CO2 absorbers. Remove Sux. Use of expired gas analyzer can

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: CAS monitors, central temperature monitor, 5 lead ECG, urinary catheter, large bore IV, help demonstrate that all volatiles have been removed.  Dantrolene  (~36 ampules = 720mg) Intraoperative Mgt: N2O considered safe, TIVA, MH may present after surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: If uneventful anesthetic, pt can be discharged 4 hrs after surgery provided they are accompanied by a responsible adults who has been educated about MH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mgt of MH Crisis Initial Management: 1) Declare emergency 2) Notify Surgeon to finish ASAP 3) Call for MH Cart  4) D/C  volatiles and Sux 5) Hyperventilate with 100% O2 at >10L/min

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Dantrolene 2.5mg/kg IV q5-10mins push, may req 10-30mg/kg, cont until signs of MH resolved. Dissolve each bottle (20mg) in 60 cc sterile warm water. Each bottle has 20mg dantrolene + 0.3mg mannitol Supportive Rx: Establish IV Access, increase monitoring (temp/foley/art/CVC), Labs: ABG's, lactate, CK, SVO2, CBC, Lytes, urine myoglobin, sepsis workup, TSH, coags, volume resuscitation. Cool patient to target core temp of 38', ice packs to surface, gastric and urinary lavage, cold IV. HCO3 -   2-4MEQ/kg for urine alk and acidosis, Treat Hyperkalemia (OK to use calcium with caution)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Dysrhythmias: Lido 1-1.5mg/kg, Procainamide 3-15mg/kg, CCBs contraind, forced diuresis with Lasix/Mannitol

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Recrudesence in 25% in the first few hours, Dantrolene 1mg/kg q4-6hrs or 0.25mg/kg/h for atleast 36hrs. Measure CK q4-6hrs. Watch for DIC, renal failure. Refer patient and fm for testing!

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Marfan's Syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Connective tissue disorder affecting cardiovascular, skeletal and ocular systems. Particular relevance with associated valvular defects, thoracic aneurysms, kyphoscoliosis and emphysema.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Airway - TMJ laxity with risk of dislocation / Potential C-spine (C1/ C2) laxity/ instability

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Respiratory insufficiency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o RLD/ pHTN /cor pulmonale due to kyphoscoliosis, pectus carinatum/excavatum

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Emphysema / bullous lung disease - inc. risk of spontaneous pneumothorax

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Significant risk of CVS disease and perioperative complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Arrhythmias & conduction defects

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Aortic aneurysm and dissection (due to cystic medial necrosis) - minimize SNS

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o MI (due to dissection of coronary arterioles)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o MVP, MR, AR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Technical difficulties with positioning and neuraxial techniques .

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pregnancy:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Risk of 3 rd  trimester aortic dissection due to estrogen mediated inhibition of collagen/elastin deposition in aorta.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Screening TTE and pre-conception elective repair if aortic root > 4cm

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Beta bocker therapy during preg/labour and delivery - minimize sympathetic stimulation.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Difficult epidurals (kyphoscoliosis) > GA and C-section may allow optimal hemodynamic control

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Gestational HTN and risk of rupture, risk of pneumos with PPV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Focused history for CVS involvement, previous investigations, sx's of AI/MR. Hx of restrictive lung

<!-- PAGE=? -->
disease, spont pneumos, pHTN. Functional capacity. Neurologic sx's from cervical instability. Ocular sx's (lens

<!-- PAGE=? -->
displacement).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Focused cardiac exam. Murmers of AR (-blowing‖ diastolic mumur LSB), MR holosystolic mumur at apex.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Evidence of CHF. Skeletal abns: pectus, scoliosis, reduced elbow ext, pes planus, joint hypermobility, high

<!-- PAGE=? -->
palate with dental crowding. Resp: Increased WOB, hyperinflation.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: Usual BW, CXR: cardiomegaly, dilated vessels, bullous disease. 12lead: conduction abns / BBB.  Echo - for root dilatation, valves, EF, PAP. Conisder PFTs.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: cardiology / resp consult. Beta blockade, anxiolysis. Appropriate hemodynamic manipulation based on underlying lesions or ventricular dysfunction.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: GA/ Neuraxial (maybe difficult) / regional all appropriate if hemod. goals achieved. Consider avoiding PPV due to risk of pneumo if hx of emphysema or bullous disease.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: 5 lead +- invasive lines, +- TEE/PAC, Beta blockers, NTG/Nipride/Inotropes, + Chest tube kit (32-40F)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Avoid increases in SBP/catecholamine surges. Observe peak airway pressures. Ensure adequate analgesia on emergence and full NMB reversal.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: May require monitored setting based on underlying cardiorespiratory reserve. Observe for perioperative pneumothoraces, aortic dissection/rupture/tamponade/coronary artery dissection. Worsening MR / MVP.

Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: AMPLE; Dx, onset, progression, known location of bleed? Etiology (TB, Bronchiectasis, Neoplasia), recent procedure (iatrogenic), contraindications to surgery include inoperable pulmonary carcinoma, failure to localize site of hemorrhage, and presence of severe bilateral pulmonary disease Px: VS, Stable or unstable, airway for ease of intubation/DLT/obstruction, volume status, IV access, LOC Inv: CBC, lytes, Ur, Cr, PTT / INR, ABG & crossmatch, CXR, CT to localize, ECG (pHTN), baseline PFTs, rigid bronch (single most important technique to identify cause of active bleeding), FOB if not actively bleeding Optimization: Avoid sedation, bronchial artery embolization (contraindicated if collaterals to spine), Anesthetic Setup: Discuss plan with Surgeon, large bore IVs, Blood products immediately available, Vasopressors, High FiO2, suction, bleeding lung down (prevents contamination), early lung isolation (DLT, endobronchial SLT, blocker), Thoracic surgeon with rigid bronch, HFJV, fogarty catheter (place down bronch) Management of Anesthesia: bleeding lung dependant prior to isolation, then reverse after isolation; Acute airway obstruction or treatable cause - rigid bronchoscope (iced saline, vasoconstrictors, bronchial blocker, packing, Nd:YAG laser); not treatable with rigid bronch - rapid lung isolation (awake vs. asleep laryngoscopy; difficult topicalization; intubate in semi-fowlers; possible RSI with ketamine and SCh / rocuroium; endobronchial SLT vs. blocker vs. DLT) SLT maneuvers include - advance endobronchially - ETT goes down bleeding bronchus (attempt to reposition ETT into nonbleeding bronchus - try ventilating alongside endobronchial ETT by inserting an additional small ETT through glottis -consider placing Fogarty catheter down ETT and occluding bronchus, then withdrawing ETT into trachea); ETT goes down nonbleeding bronchus (suction ETT to remove residual blood, ventilate with 100%, if oxygenation continues to be a problem, prepare to insert DLT Can't ventilate / high airway pressures: (Massive airway clot, Tension pneumothorax, light

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: anesthesia), Aspiration, Hypoxemia, Hypotension, Cardiac arrest

Massive Transfusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Replacement  1blood/24 hrs (~10 units PRBCs in adult), or 50% blood vol/3 hrs, or 4 units/1 hour with ongoing losses, or 6 units in 1 bleeding episode with on going losses

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Early recognition of potential for massive transfusion and mobilization of resources

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Blood Bank, Lab, Hematopathology, Help for transfusion-related duties in OR/ER/LDR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Consider transfusion-sparing modalities - cell saver, antifibrinolytics, Factor VIIa

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Monitor hemoglobin (>70), platelets >50 (>100 with ICH), INR <1.5, PTT within 1.5 of lab's normal, fibrinogen >1, and replace appropriately. Octaplex to reverse Coumadin.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Monitor electrolytes including K + , Ca 2+  and Mg 2+

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid hypothermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Obstetric patient - etiology (fetal demise, AFE, placental abruption) may contribute to DIC

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Acute phase resuscitation Maintain hemodynamics - volume, crystalloids, pressors; Oxygenation - RBC transfusion; Hemostasis - factors, platelets, euthermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Maintenance phase resuscitation : time to base resuscitation on labs - standard lab tests have poor correlation with in vivo coagulopathy.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Bleeding Hx, previous transfusion, inherited coagulopathy, medications (ASA, coumadin, etc.).  Obstetric Risk factors: Placenta Previa, Prior C-section, Multiple gestation, Chorioamnionitis, Placental Abruption, Abnormal fetal presentation PE: Vitals + Temp. Surgical bleeding, medical bleeding with dec. clot formation (nose, gums, IV sites Investigations: CBC, INR, PTT, fibrinogen, Mg, Ca, Lytes, LFTs, Lactate, mixed venous Optimization: Prevention - Preop Fe  EPO, position to dec. venous engorgement, normothermia, controlled hypotension, antifibrinolytics, tourniquet, cautery. RBC conservation - ANH, Hypervolemic hemodilution. Cell salvage (obstetric concern of fetal debris/AFE causing anaphylactoid Rx - use after delivery of fetoplacental unit. Inform Blood Bank & Laboratory Anesthetic Options: GA for massive transfusion Room Setup: CAS+5lead, A-line, CVL, temp, large bore i.v.'s, rapid infusor, warmers, Foley, pressors/Inotropes Intraoperative Mgt: PRBC : Hct 0.70 in 250mL , FFP - all coagulation factors , dec FV and FVIII (15-30%) , Factors replaced if INR / PTT > 1.5x . Cryo - has fibrinogen, fibronectin, factor VIII, vWF and factor XIII (fibrinogen < 1.0 g/L), 1 unit FFP has 0.5g of Fibrinogen & 1u of cryo = 0.25g. Platelets For surgical hemostasis goal is PLT > 50 or > 100 for intracranial or neuraxial stuff. Recombinant Factor VIIa reduces the number of units transfused in cases of massive transfusion. Octaplex (prothrombin complex concentrate of F II, VII, IX, X) for rapid Coumadin reversal + VitK. ICU to monitor for tx compl, HD stability, coag abnormalites, electrolyte imbalance, acid-base status. Diluted

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: ETT & PPV cont until temp and HD goals are met and stabilized. Complications : Infx, Hemolytic transfusion rxn, Non-hemolytic ( Febrile , Delayed transfusion rxn , Anaphylactic ,TRALI / TACO, transfusion-associated Graft vs Host disease).  Hyperkalemia; hypocalcemia, Hypomagnesemia. Hypothermia , Coagulopathy : factors (< 30% activity) and plts with crystalloid, colloid and RBCs

Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize - biopsy peripheral tissue or mediastinoscopy under local, steroids, radiation, chemo,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain airway patency

<!-- PAGE=? -->

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Assisted expiration may be lifesaving in complete obstruction (pulmonary tamponade)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain hemodynamics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o careful positioning - lateral decubitus or prone if cardiovascular collapse

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o maintain preload (RV may be volume dependent)

<!-- PAGE=? -->

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Airway compression (positional dyspnea, cough, stridor, hoarseness), SVC Syndrome (H/A, upper body edema/plethora, cough, dyspnea), Right Heart Compression (positional syncope/dyspnea, hepatosplenomegaly). Comorbid Disease based on DDx (thyroid, thymoma, MG/ELS, lymphoma (esp adolescents), neuroblastoma in children) PE: Vitals (hypoxemia, postural hTN), H&N (edema/plethora, tracheal deviation, masses), CVS (syncope with valsalve, quite HS/JVD for pericardial effusion, pulsus paradoxus), RESP (WOB, stridor, supine dyspnea ) Investigations: Labs, CXR, CT scan (>50% tracheal comp ↑risk), +/-ECHO, PFTs not useful Optimization: Consider pre-operative steroids, chemo, radiation to decrease mass depending on diagnosis if too high risk (recognizing that this may impair definitive diagnosis), check for extrathoracic LN sites for biopsy especially if lymphoma, treat pulm infections, consider preop Airway / SVC stents Anesthetic Options: Always consider local/sedation first, otherwise GETA Room Setup: CAS + 5L ECG, arterial line, vasoactive drugs, lower extremity IV if SVC syndrome, consider having rigid bronch & CPB available. Intraoperative Mgt: If asympt with no radiologic evidence of heart/airway compression proceed with routine induction and maintenance.  If positional sympt/compression, consider awake FOI with positioning of ETT distal to obstrx with ENT/rigid bronch/CPB backup. Maintain SV during induction and carefully transition to PPV & muscle relaxation. Consider inhalational vs slow TIVA for uncooperative patients or kids. Post-op: Needs intensive monitoring in HDU to monitor for airway obs (mass or if resected, tracheomalacia) and airway edema. rigid bronch, CPB, consider dynamic hyperinflation), Cardiovascular collapse (reposition, SV, fluids, inotropes,

Special: Intraop emergencies - Acute airway compression or inability to ventilate (reposition, return to SV, CPB)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Metabolic Acidosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Underlying etiology (AG vs non-AG)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Other associated metabolic derangements

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Related multiorgan dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o malignant arrhythmias

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o impaired myocardial function

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o altered seizure threshold

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Altered pharmacology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Augments / prolongs NdMB

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Respiratory acidosis inhibits neostigmine reversal of NdMB

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Treatment of underlying etiology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Treat associated metabolic abnormalities

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Anticipate/manage physiologic sequelae of metabolic derangement

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Patient with severe metabolic acidosis with limited respiratory reserve

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o bicarb administration when minute ventilation is already near patient's maximum

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Identify etiology - Organ hypoperfusion and shock (Obtundation, dyspnea, angina, abdominal pain) Toxodrome (altered LOC, visual/balance disturbances, CNS irritability, N&V, palpitations, muscle weakness) PE: Vitals + temp, volume status, focused neuro (GCS, cranial nerves), peripheral perfusion (peripheral pulses), hyperventilation (fatigue may herald rapid deterioration), Kussmaul's breathing, abdominal exam Investigations: ABG, Lytes, BUN, Cr, Ca, Mg, Glucose. CBC. Urinalysis. osmolality. specific toxins. Optimization: Identify and treat cause prior to an anesthetic. Bicarb (1 mEq/kg) or Tris-Hydroxymethyl AminoMethane (1.1 x base deficit x body weight = cc required) if significant physiologic derangement. Dialysis for acidosis refractory to medical management or acidosis with significant physiologic derangement Anesthetic Options: GA. Regional likely not tolerated 2' to physiologic derrangement Room Setup: CAS + 5. Art line (for serial sampling), Warming blanket, Nerve stimulator (impact on NdMR) Intraoperative Mgt: Agents used for maintenance/induction dependent on etiology of acidosis. Anticipate exaggerated response to induction agents. Ventilation should aim for pH > 7.2 to optimize enzyme function. Post-op: Low threshold for high dependency unit. Causes of AG metabolic acidosis: MUDPILES CART = Methanol, Uremia, DKA, Paraldehyde/Phenformin, Iron/Isoniazid, Lactate, Ethyline glycol, Salicyclate, Cyanide, Arsenic, Rhabdomyolysis, Toluene Causes of Non-AG metabolic acidosis: GI losses, pancreatic fistulae, renal bicarb loss, renal dysfunction, hypoaldosteronism, hyperventilation, ingestion (ammonium chloride, acetazolamide, hyperalimentation, ketoacidosis while on insulin) Other key points: AG = Na - Cl-HCO3. Normal is 12 with range of 8-16. Adjustment of AG for hypoalbuminemia -> (Normal Albumin - Observed albumin) X 0.2 (some sources used 0.25 = Actual anion gap Osmolar gap = 2 X [Na] + glucose/18 + BUN/2.8

<!-- PAGE=? -->

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential difficult airway with risk of perioperative airway obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Shared airway with possible jet ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
barotrauma, TIVA, gas exchange

<!-- PAGE=? -->
need for vocal cord paralysis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Unprotected airway with risk of loss of airway and aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
debris, blood, gastric contents

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Laser complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Airway fire, ocular/cutaneous burns, VAE, air contamination

<!-- PAGE=? -->
High risk for perioperative myocardial ischemia / infaction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Safe induction and airway management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o AFOI, awake look, spont vent, ENT laryngoscopy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain adequate oxygenation and ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevention of barotrauma and Laser related complication

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Unobstructed, motionless surgical field

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: extent of lesion, location, and airway obstruction - hoarsness, dysphonia, stridor, dyspnea, dynamic obstruction; etiology - previous anesthetics; contraindications to jet ventilation (airway obstruction, restrictive lung disease - obese, ped, bullous lung disease, aspiration risk); coexisting diseases - CAD PE: careful airway exam, positional changes if airway obstruction, standard PE

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: imaging (CT), nasopharyngoscopy, CXR, PFTs, blood work and further tests dictated by comorbidities - -safe‖ small ETT with regular PPV, jet ventilation via suspension -ventilating laryngoscope‖, jet ventilation via bronchoscope (for sub-glottic masses), apneic technique with alternating ETT or BMV, high frequency PPV via a catheter

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: Laser precautions (goggles, masks, notice on doors, smoke evacuator, eye protection, saline bucket, Laser Shield ETT with Methylene blue for cuff); Jet ventilator - rigid bronch; TIVA; Standard monitors +/- art line

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: If difficult A/W - awake DL, AFOI, SV induction (inhalational vs. TIVA); if no A/W concerns - IV induction, Sux, TIVA; DL prior to handing patient over to surgeon; sux boluses (bradycardia). Limit FiO2, communication with surgeon is crutial

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op : head-up to decrease edema, Dex, monitor for PTX Complications: A/W obstruction - rigid bronch, cricothyroidotomy; Dec. chest excursion - suction, check for PTX, A/W fire: 4 E's = extract, eliminate, extinguish, evaluate - reintubate and observe; Barotrauma, VAE, hemorrhage, HTN / tachycardia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mitral Regurgitation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
MR can be acute or chronic and results in volume overload and decreased forward cardiac output. In acute MR, no compensatory hypertrophy and lack of compliance results in CHF / cardiogrnic shock.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased risk of perioperative cardiovascular complications including CHF and MI

<!-- PAGE=? -->
The pathological hemodynamic changes of mitral regurgitation:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Chronic -LA volume overload and decreased forward cardiac output / LV dysfunction / atrial arrhythmias due to LA dilatation / pulmonary hypertension and RV dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Acute - sudden LA and LV overload without compensatory hypertrophy leads to reduced forward cardiac output and simultaneous pulmonary congestion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 may require emergent surgical / anesthetic management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Associated co-morbidities including:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Other valvular pathology (MS, AR) / Endocarditis / Connective tissue disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Underlying Etiology: (1) Leaflets/commisures: Rheumatic, endocarditis, MVP (2) Tensor apparatus: rupture papillary muscle (ischemia), dysfunction (fibrosis), rupt. of chordea (3) LV cavity or annulus: LV enlargement (myocarditis/cardiomyopathy), calcified mitral ring, marfans

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medical therapy (ACEI, BB, digoxin, CCBs), anticoagulants for Afib

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Fast, full, and forward

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain forward flow: Adequate preload, high N HR~90bpm, NSR, slight reduction of afterload, maintain or increase contractility.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Onset, severity of disease. NYHA class (1=no limitation w/ ordinary activity, 2=mild limitation of activity, rest)  Sx's of CHF:orthopnea/PND. Comorbid illness: CAD, Mitral Stenosis, pHTN, afib , endocard. PE: Elevated JVP, edema, rales. Displaced LV apical impulse (chronic), holosystolic apical murmer radiating to axillae. S3 / S4. If associated MS, may have diastolic murmer. Findings of pHTN.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pregnancy and MR: ACEi contraindicated due to adverse effects, hydralazine ok.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
comfortable at rest or mild exertion, 3=marked limitation, comfortable only at rest, 4= confined to chair, sx's at Investigations: Usual BW, troponins, blood cultures (if endo), ECG : dysrhythmias, LVH +- RVH/strain, CXR : pulmonary vascularity and congestion, ECHO : EF, severity, LV + atrial size, thrombus. +- angiogram. Optimization: Cardiology consult, consider MVR/replacement>> Class 1 indications include : Acute sympt MR, NYHA II-IV sx's with N EF, Sympt or asympt with mild LV dysfx (EF 0.5-0.6) and dilatation / optimize CHF Anesthetic Options: GA, neuraxial (as long as hemodynamic goals met) early epidural in pregnancy Room Setup: 5 lead, Art, +/- TEE/PAC / +/- IABP/Perfusion services, Inotropes (milrinone/dobutamine), NTG/Nipride, AChs for brady, NO for pHTN. Intraoperative Mgt: Observe hemodynamic goals, consider mitral stenosis if rheumatic heart disease. Avoid hypercapnia/hypoxia and pain on emergence (increases PVR). May require inotropic support post MVR/replacement. Post-op: MVP : empty LV causes inc. MVP and acute MR / RV failure : Avoid precipitants of pHTN / SAM :inc. SVR, volume expansion and decreased contractility / Ischemia : CAD vs. hypotension / Arrhythmia : cardioversion vs. IV drugs / Hypotension : preload vs. afterload vs. contractility / Air embolism : keep lines free of air bubbles MR with NYHA 1-2 and N LVEF are low risk for mom and baby. NYHA III-IV sx's, MR with pHTN or LV dysfnx considered high risk. Maintain specific hemodynamic goals, early epidural, art line,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Identify severity of disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
mod. area 1-1.5cm2 (symptomatic), critical area <1cm2 (CHF, pHTN, RVF)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hemodynamic complications of Mitral Stenosis - CHF (inc. LA pressure with underfilled LV), atrial arrhythmias, pHTN with RVF, systemic embolization (TIA's/CVA's)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Percipitants of decompentation - inc. CO and dec. diastolic time

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pregnancy, thyrotoxicosis, sepsis, Afib, fever

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Co-existing disease: Associated valvular disease (Ao valve, TR), rheumatic fever

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications: anticoagulation, diuretics, BBs, digoxin

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pregnancy : moderate to severe MS usually inc NYHA status by 1 or 2 classes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Invasive monitoring +- PAC (for unexplained hypotension) / Judicious fluid management, BB for Tachycardia / Early titrated epidural / Avoid pushing (low forceps) / C-section of obstetric indications /Management of autotransfusion - intubation & PPV / oxytocin, methylergonovie, and hemabate (PF2-alpha) all inc. PVR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hemodynamic goals: Slow HR 60-80 bpm, Strict NSR, maintain preload and contractility, avoid drops in afterload.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid precipitants of pHTN: hypoxia/acidosis/hypothermia/pain/N2O

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mitral Stenosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Hx of dyspnea, CHF, PND, orthopnea, functional capacity, hemoptysis, arrhythmias, anticoagulation, risk of thrombosis.  Hx of pHTN (dyspnea, fatigue, angina), Hoarseness d/t compression of L recurrent LN, CNS sx's of stroke/TIA.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Irregular pulses, prominent S2 and a diastolic murmur, decreased pulse pressure, loud S1 (high closing pressure across MV) +- opening snap. Sx's of pHTN. Tacypnea, crackles, wheezes, hepatomegaly, pedal edema.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: ECG - Afib common, p mitrale, RVH, CXR: Enlarged LA, pulmonary edema. Echo: Thickened MV, MVA, gradient, presence of thrombus. ?head CT. INR, PTT if on anticoagulants, LFTs. Class I indications for valvotomy include: NYHA II-IV symptoms, asymptomatic patients with PAS > 50 mm Hg

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Cardiology consult, consider MVR or percutaneous valvulotmy prior to surgical procedures: at rest or 60mm Hg with exercise. Class I for MVR: NYHA III-IV when PMBV is not an option. Mod-Sev MR. Medical management: Beta blockers, digoxin, diuretics, anticoagulation.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: Narcotic based GA +- regional, controlled epidural, avoid spinal. Strict NSR, slow HR avoid exacerbation of pHTN.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: 5 lead ECG, A line, consider TEE>PAC, prepare for cardioversion, vasoactive meds.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Observe hemodynamic goals, control sympathetic outflow, avoid tachy/pain on emergernce. BB for tachycardia, early cardioversion, Consider NO if pHTN.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Monitored setting, observe for hypotension, MI, ischemia, CHF. If MVR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Note post CPB these patients often have depressed myocardial fnx despite N LVEF. Anticipate, augment preload, reduce SVR, inotropic support.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mucopolysaccharidosis (hurler's and hunter's)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential Difficult airway: Macroglossia, infiltration of tissues, short neck

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential unstable C-spine - AAI

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Developmental delay, growth retardation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
End-organ dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiomyopathy, valvular disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hepatic dysfunction, Neurologic dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hemorrhagic diathesis due to plt dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Perioperative risk of hypoglycemia (glycogen canot be hydrolyzed in hepatocytes)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Metabolic acidosis d/t inability to convert lactic acid to glycogen (avoid ringer's)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Perioperative monitoring of of serum glucose, minimization of fasting times when possible

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Pre-operative identification and optimization of cardiac system

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Safe establishment of airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid resp-depressants

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multiple Sclerosis Autoimmune, demyelinating CNS disease with multisystem effects

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Demyelination results in:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Increased risk of aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Respiratory failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Autonomic dysfunction - hemodynamic instability

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Altered response to neuromuscular blockers

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hyperkalemia with Succinylcholine if symptomatic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 May be sensitive to NdMR or resistant (b/c upregulation of NAchR)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for exacerbation of MS

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Surgical stress

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 neuraxial technique (spinal > epidural) - unknown why

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 hyperthermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Immunosuppressive medications (steroids, interferon, MTX)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevent exacerbations - Avoid hyperthermia and neuraxial anesthetics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Minimize aspiration risk - Aspiration prophylaxis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maximize respiratory muscle strength

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain hemodynamic stability

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Conflicts - RSI vs. Hemodynamic stability, Neuroaxial for labour or C/S

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Functional capacity, respiratory insufficiency, hemodynamic / autonomic instability, bulbar dysfunction. Course of disease, medical therapy.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Focussed cardiorespiratory exam, cough, resting tachycardia, neurologic exam.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Usual bloodwork, PFTs / ABG, CXR.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Delay elective surgery for symptomatic disease, consider neurology consultation, aspiration prophylaxis, stress dose steroids.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: Avoid spinal and high doses of LA, epidural is not associated with exacerbation. GA and PNB's Ok.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: CAS monitors, 5 lead ECG, PNS, consider arterial line, temp monitor (avoid hyperthermia), assistant for cricoids, vasopressors for hypotension.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Consider RSI vs hemodynamically stable induction. Judicious NDMR.  Ensure reversal. Avoid emotional stress / pain.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Monitoring for post-operative respiratory insufficiency and or neurologic dysfunction.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Special: Presents with ascending spastic pariesis (Legs>arms), optic neuritis, gait disturbances, limb parasethesias, L'hermette's sign F>M, non-smokers, Caucasians. Relapses in 3 rd  trimester with exacerbation 1-3 months post-delivery.Most common neuro-demyelinating disease 1:1000. Dx by IgG in CSF, MRI. Rx = Steroids = mainstay, Interferon B for RRMS, Glatiramer acetate = myelin mimic protein that blocks myelin destruction, Azathioprine: decreases rate of exacerbations but not course, others: MTX.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Minimize risk of aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Minimize risk of cardiopulmonary insufficiency / failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Trigger free Anesthesia - Avoid succinylcholine + volatile anesthetics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Conflicts: RSI (NdMB) vs titrated induction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Muscular Dystrophy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hereditary disease (x-linked recessive) of painless degeneration and atrophy of skeletal muscles with preserved innervation, often accompanied by developmental delay

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Aspiration Risk - dec. gut motility, laryngeal muscle weakness

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Coexisting disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Resp - Pre/post operative respiratory insufficiency, RLD (d/t scoliosis) - pHTN & RVF, OSA, recurrent pneumonia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiac - Cardiomyopathy (sensitivity to myocardial depression), MR (MVP), Arrhythmias

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Altered pharmacology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Susceptibility to Anesthetic-induced Myodystrophy (Sux/Volatiles)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hyperkalemia (rhabdomyolysis)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Sensitivity to NdMR (usual dose but prolonged action)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
+- Considerations of a pediatric patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Personal or FmHx of MH/Rhabdo, Cardiac - functional capacity, CHF, orthopnea, PND; Resp - home O2, recurrent lung infections, chronic aspiration, OSA, Bipap, noctural ventilation, hospitalizations PE: Vitals + BMI; Airway - Macroglossia, Resp - Adequate cough, kyphoscoliosis; Cardiac - CHF: crackles, JVP, S3, PHTN: loud P2, RV heave, TR, JVP; Assess for difficult IV access. Investigations: Usual bloodwork, Lytes to assess K, CXR (chronic aspiration) ECG (tachy, short PR, tall R in V1, and deep q's in limb leads), Echo (fxn & valves), PFTs (FVC <35% poor outcomes, >45% unlikely to req post-op ventilation), ABG, CK 30-300x N even in female carriers. Optimization: Delay elective Sx to optimize cardiopulmonary status (tx infection, optimize CHF) Avoid sedation (aspiration), aspiration prophylaxis, Consider cardiology consult (CHF, arrhythmias, pacemaker) Anesthetic Options: Trigger free anesthetic; consider local/regional technique (Muscle biopsy under local), GA - TIVA with low dose NdMB, possible post-op ventilation Room Setup: CAS +5 lead, temp, foley, invasive monitoring as needed, dantrolene in room, drugs to treat hyperkalemia, PNS for NdMB Intraoperative Mgt: Non-triggering RSI (NdMB, remi), avoid SUX/Volatiles, avoid myocardial depression with cardiomyopathy, ensure adequate reversal Post-op: Possible post-op ventilation , Adequate post-op monitoring for 24-48hrs - delayed Resp distress up to 36hrs, Telemetry for arrhythmia in 50 mg sterile water), rpt as needed, max 10mg/kg. 2-4 meq/kg HCO3-, Cool, management of hyperkalemia.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Special: Presents in boys 3-5 years, with gowers sign, proximal weakness. Wheelchair by 8-11years. Treatment of MH: Hyperventilate, change machines, circuit and CO2 absorber, Dantrolene 2.5mg/kg (20 mg Management of dysrythmias, avoid Ca+ blockers due to myocardial depression and hyperkalemia when used with Dantrolene. ABGs.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Myasthenia Gravis Autoimmune disorder- Ab against nAch-R à decrease in functional Ach-R at NMJ

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pseudobulbar dysfunction and increased risk for aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased risk of perioperative respiratory complications and post-op ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 risk factors: diagnosis > 6 yrs, daily pyridostigmine dose > 750mg/day, Hx of COPD, VC < 2.9L

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Association with thymoma and considerations of an anterior mediastinal mass, thyroiditis, RA, cardiac myocarditis, cardiomyopathies, afib, heart block

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Altered response to NMB - resistance to succinylcholine and increased sensitivity to NdMR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Perioperative management of medications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Steroids, anticholinesterases, immunosupressants

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of myasthenic or cholinergic crisis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize neuromuscular function

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevent or minimize complications: aspiration, respiratory failure, myasthenic crisis, cholinergic crisis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Minimize exacerbation of perioperative weakness.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Conflicts: RSI vs NMB, RSI vs cardiac involvement, RSI vs. ant. mediastinal mass

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Symptoms of muscle groups involved, bulbar dysfunction, respiratory embarrassment, exercise tolerance, stability of symptoms, medical treatment. Associated comorbidities, thyroid/cardiac, arrhythmias. Presence of mediastinal mass.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Focused cardiorespiratory exam, airway examination, dynamic symtoms due to AMM.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: Usual bloodwork, spirometry, Echo if suspect myocarditis / cardiomyopathy, CXR for AMM, if RA lateral neck films)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Postpone elective cases for symptomatic patients.  If acute myasthenic crisis, patient will need IVIG, plasmapheresis, and high dose steroids. Continue pyridostigmine perioperatively. ASPIRATION prophylaxis (sodium citrate, ranitidine, maxeran)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic options: Regional or local preferred.  Epidural for pregnant patient. GA.Discuss risk of POV.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: Assistant for RSI, Pns for NMB, Consider invasive monitoring for AMM / difficult A/W Intraoperative Mgt:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Stress dose steroids, IV induction with remi preferred. May need 2mg/kg Sux or 10% of NDMR dose.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Respiratory failure: Myasthenia crisis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cholinergic crisis: 2ry to excessive anticholinesterases (also bradycardic, salivation, miosis (SLUDGE) distinguish by giving edrophonium (Tensilon Test = 1 to 2 mg and titrate up 3mg, 5mg to max of 10mg) which improves symptoms if myasthenic crisis, worsens symptoms if cholinergic crisis)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Residual anesthetic drugs: ms relaxants

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypothermia; Hypokalemia; antiarrythmics; Mg; antibiotics; psychotropics;

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Special: Dx: Tensilon(Edrophonium), RMG, RIA against Ab RX: Pyridostigmine, IVIG / Plasmapharesis for Myasthenic crisis, Steroids/ Immunosuppressants. Surgery (Thymectomy improves 85%). Rule of 1/3's in pregnancy (get better/same/worse)
