<!-- PAGE=? -->
Myasthenic Syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Association with Small Cell Cancer

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Sensitive to Succinylcholine and Non depolarizing relaxants

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Respiratory weakness/RLD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of Aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications: Anticholinesterases don't work well, IVIG, Plasmapharesis, 3-4di-aminopyridine.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Myotonic Dystrophy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Myotonia is the delayed relaxation of skeletal muscle after voluntary contraction, electrical stimulation or mechanical stimulation. As disease progresses, weakness and atrophy become more prominent and loss of DTReflexes (distal muscles before proximal!!!)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of aspiration secondary to bulbar weakness

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Respiratory insuficiency , restrictive lung disease and PHTN , central sleep apnea

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiovascular involvement and conduction abnormalities : 1 st  degree heart block, atrial and ventricular arrhythmias , cardiomyopathy and MVP (20%)but rarely sx.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Endocrine abnormalities: DM, hypothyroid, hypogonadism, addison's

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Sensitive to CNS and respiratory depressants, Avoid Sux - Hyperkalemia, Association with MH -trigger free

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of Myotonic Crisis with cautery, mechanical stimulation, succinylcholine and cholinesterase inhibitors, post operative shivering. (Rx: Lido 0.5% infiltration, mb stabilizers, phenytoin)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid aspiration and triggers of myotonic crisis, and post-operative shivering

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Treat Myotonia if it interferes with ventilation, be prepared for post-op ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Conflict: RSI with avoidance of Succinylcholine or cholinesterase inhibitor vs cardiac induction for cardiac co-morbidities

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid long acting opioids due to risk of central sleep apnea

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Functional history. Elucidate respiratory sx's, central sleep apnea, restrictive disease. Elucidate cardiac

<!-- PAGE=? -->
involvement, symptomatic heart disease or evidence of cardiomyopathy/rhythem disturbance. Inquire about

<!-- PAGE=? -->
endocrine disease. Bulbar symptoms, dysphagia. AMPLE hx.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Chest excursion, ability to cough, myotonic hand grip (unable to release), Cardiac examination for MVP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
(systolic apical click +/- late systolic murmur), arrhythmias, RVH (loud P2), failure. Developmental delay,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
frontal balding, expressionless facial weakness, dysarthria, SCM wasting.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Usual BW / ECG / +-ECHO / +- Spirometry / tSH / Electrolytes / CK = N to slight high

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Aspiration prophylaxis, avoid sediation (CSA) / CPAP / Keep Warm / ?Stress dose steroids

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CAS / 5lead ECG / TEMP / Lido 0.5% / Mexilitine  / Pheyntoin and Procainamide 18mg/kg over

<!-- PAGE=? -->
20 - 30 mins IV / Quinine 300-600 mg IV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic options:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Theoretical risk of MH > trigger free preferred. Avoid Sux, Regional / Neuraxial for pain

<!-- PAGE=? -->
preferred. Avoid long acting opioids for CSA.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid myocardial depression. Judicious use of NDMRs to avoid reversal agents.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Although Neostigmine is usually ok.  IV or propofol may precipitate contracture >> EMLA / lido.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications / treatment of a Myotonic Crisis:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
muscle inflitration with dilute 0.5% lidocaine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
phenytoin 18 mg/kg IV over 20-30 mins

<!-- PAGE=? -->
procainamide 18 mg/kg IV over 20-30 mins

<!-- PAGE=? -->
quinine 300 - 600 mg IV, phenytoin, mexiletine and tocainide depress Na+ influx, decreasing spread of

<!-- PAGE=? -->
action potentials.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
postoperative cardiopulmonary complications common

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations of Prematurity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased risk of aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Bowel obstruction, dilated bowel loops, pneumatosis intestinalis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Full stomach

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Associated multisystem derangements

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypoxia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Sepsis / Hypovolemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o DIC, thrombocytopenia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Metabolic acidosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Associated conditions

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Birth asphyxia, hypotension, RDS, PDA, recurrent apnea, intestinal ischemia, UV cannulation, systemic infections, early feedings

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize multisystem abnormalities of prematurity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevent aspiration (consider RSI)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Conflict with sepsis/hypovolemia and hymodynamic stability

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Anticipate and optimize fluid / electrolyte / glucose derangements

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Ensure good IV access (or central line above the diaphragm)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Ensure continuous temperature monitoring and maintain normothermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Correction of coagulopathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
NEC

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Obstetrical hx, PCA/prematurity and complications of prematurity (BPD, RDS, PDA, IVH, ROP), NEC hx: abdominal distension, vomiting, bloody or mucoid diarrhea, occult blood loss in stool, lethargy, irritability PE: Vitals, wt (volume loss), focus on volume assessment (IV access, u/o); Resp - intubated, WOB, FiO2; CVS - perfusion, cap refill, murmurs; abdominal exam CBC (anemia, thrombocytopenia), lytes/Cr (hypovolemia), glucose, coagulation profile, G & S,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: ABG, ECHO if indicated, AXR (pneumatosis, intestinalis, dilated loops, free air)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Unless intestinal necrosis/perforation, initial management in medical - decompress stomach, NPO, Abx, Fluid/TPN; Volume resuscitation - Crystalloid, blood, FFP, Plts; good IV access +/- CVP Anesthetic Options: GA - caution d/t hypovolemia/sepsis, RSI for aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: Warm room/warming devices, resuscitation drugs (epi) drawn up, extra personel, neonatal circuit

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Monitors: CAS, +/- artline, temp probe, foley Intraoperative Mgt: muscle relaxant/opioid +/- ketamine, Volatiles may be poorly tolerated,  avoid N2O (destends bowel), FiO2 to maintain Sats ~90%

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: NICU, post-op ventilation, +/- inotropes Complications: hypothermia, hypovolemic shock, metabolic acidosis, coagulopathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Special: Operative indictions - Absolute:  pneumoperitoneum, gangrene; Relative:  clinical deterioration, portal vein gas, erythema abdo wall, fixed abd mass, persistently dilated loop.  Non-indications are severe GI hemorrhage, abd tenderness, intestinal obstruction, gasless abd with ascites

<!-- PAGE=? -->
3.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Neuraxial Opiod Monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Identify risk factors for respiratory depression

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Sleep apnea

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Advanced age

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Co-existing disease (diabetes, obesity, unstable medical condition)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 High dose opioid, repeated neuraxial doses, concomitant enteral or parenteral opioids and sedatives

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Select appropriate opioid and dose

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Lipophilic vs hydrophilic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Select appropriate monitoring and disposition for the patient (based on patient factors, opiate choice and neuraxial technique)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 All patients should be monitored for adequacy of VENTILATION, OXYGENATION and LEVEL OF CONSCIOUSNESS after receiving neuraxial opioids

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Single shot of hydrophobic (ie fentanyl or sufentanil) = continuous for 20min then q1h x 2h

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Single shot of hydrophilic (morphine) = q1h x 12 hr, then q2h x 12 hrs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Continuous infusion: continuous x 20min then q1h x 12 hrs, q2h x 12 hrs, q4h until infusion stopped

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Sustained/Extended release epidural morphine: q1h x 12hrs, then q2h x12hrs, then q4h after 48hrs Intensify monitoring in the presence of risk factors - Continuous pulse oximetry

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx : OSA Sx's, concomitant Opiod/CNS depressant use (benzo, EtOH)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pathophysiology:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Neuraxial opioids mechanisms of respiratory depression:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Vascular uptake by epidural/subarachnoid venous plexuses & circulation to brainstem resp center

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Arachnoid penetration and movement into the spinal cord

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Rostral spread via the aqueous CSF to the brain stem or via direct perimedulary vasc channels

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
BUN/Creat for renal insufficiency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Drug Effects: Lipohilicity ( fentanyl) rapid onset of effect & dec. duration of action. In single doses of 10-30ug, has rapid onset (10-20min) and short duration (4-6hrs) with minimal cephalad spread, making it least likely to cause delayed respiratory depression. May cause early (0-1hr) respiratory depression. Hydrophilicity (i.e. morphine) inc. duration of action and dec. onset time. Slow onset (30-60min), dose related duration (13-33hrs) and potential for both early and delayed respiratory depression .  Delayed depression is primarily assoc with hydrophilic opioids because of cephalad spread and typically occurs within 12hrs post-injection (up to 24hrs, with a peak at 6hrs ).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Treatment:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Supplemental Oxygen available, administered if dec. LOC or resp depression, routine use may inc. the duration of apneic episodes and hinder diagnosis of hypotension.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Reversal Agents available, IV access mandatory, administered if respiratory depression develops, ABC approach, infusion will likely be required (2-10mg/24hrs).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
NIPPV may be considered to improve ventilator status.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Neurofibramatosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Definition: multi-system, AD disorder effecting neural crest cells during development causing a tendency to form multiple soft tumours (neurofibromas) in the skin and CNS

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential difficult airway: pharyngeal tumor, laryngeal stenosis, limitation of c-spine ROM

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential restrictive lung disease (kyphoscoliosis 30% or pulmonary fibrosis from parenchymal infiltration of tumor)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiovascular involvement: essential hypertension , Pheochromocytoma 1% incidence, renal artery stenosis, may have idiopathic hypertrophic cardiomyopathy , dysrhythmias

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Altered response to NB's: Sensitive to Sux , unpredictable response to NdMR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential contraindication to neuraxial technique due to spread of tumor, and potential raised ICP from intracranial tumours, seizures.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Background:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Three subtypes: NFI, NF2, Segmental, hallmark café au lait spots >1.5cms, > 6

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Autosomal dominant but 50% are new mutations. Often worsens in pregnancy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 NF1: Classic, multisystem neurofibromatosis. 1:3000 early dx, increases severity with age

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 NF2: More localized dx(Café spots and neurofibromas ↓ common). Bilateral acoustic neuromas. Also have abn growth of other cell types, ie schwannomas, meningiomas, gliomas, cataracts.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Segmental: Mosaic form of disorders with neurofibromas in some areas and other areas unaffected.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Airway issues, hoarseness, previous hx of difficult intubation. Respiratory sx's, functional capacity, history of restrictive lung disease, cor pulmonale. Cardiac involvement: HTN, pheo, RAS, RV outflow obstruction. Hx of headaches, seizures, raised ICP, visual symptoms. Endo- pituitary involvement, pancreatic tumors, thyroid tumors.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Airway exam (hoarseness, dysphonia, stridor), focused cardiopulmonary exam, kyphoscoliosis, fine crackles, clubbing, BP(HTN/perspiration), neurological exam for ICP, visual defects, papilledema decreased LOC + neuro exam for regional technique

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: Usual BW +- imaging related to symptoms, MRI if planning regional technique. CXR in severe kyphoscoliois, consider PFTs or ABG.  24-hour urine collection for creatinine, total catecholamines, vanillylmandelic acid, and metanephrines.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Consider endocrine consult, MRI if planning regional technique, BP control, respiratory consult if restrictive lung disease?

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: GA preferred or MRI prior to regional / neuraxial technique.  May avoid LMA from laryngeal obstruction by tumor. Consider raised ICP.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: Entirely dependent on manifestations of disease, consider difficult airway equipment, antihypertensives, alpha blockade (phentolamine). PNS for unpredictable response to NMB. Post-op: Seizures, residual NMBs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Neuroleptic Malignant Syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potentially life-threatening emergency with high mortality (4-20%)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Altered LOC: Coma which may mandate airway managment

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Autonomic instability: tachycardia, hypertension, cardiac dysrhythmias (most likely cause of death)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypermetabolic State: fever, rhabdomyolysis, DIC, volume depletion, renal failure and acidosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Tachypnea and potential respiratory insufficiency from hypoventilation/rigidity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DDx:  MH, infection, drug toxicity/withdrawal, Serotonin Syndrome, heat stroke, status epilepticus, malignant catatonia, thyrotoxicosis, pheochromocytoma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Underlying psychiatric condition

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Resuscitation and ICU monitoring following trigger

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Stop offending agents (?Sux, antidopinergics), supportive treatment, cooling, treat acidosis and electrolyte abnormalities, hemodynamic support

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Pharmacologic: bromcriptine, dantrolene, benzodiazepines

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o ECT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Rule out high risk conditions on differential diagnosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Trigger free‖ anesthetic in patients with history of NMS (controversial)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: AMPLE + recent neuroleptic drugs started or increase dosage, psych hx, most common drugs: agonsists; Symptoms - Mental status changes (confusion, stupor, delirium) motor rigidity, akinesia, bradykinesia, dystonia, mutism, dysarthria , involuntary mov'ts.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
haloperidol, phenothiazines, butyrophenones, thioxanthines.  Withdrawal of anti-Parkinson meds (dopamine PE: Vitals (orthostatic, temp): autonomic dysfxn, CVS: tachy, diaphoresis, arrhythmias; MSK: rigidity that resolves with NdMB (unlike MH); Resp failure (WOB, cyanosis, hypercarbia), CNS: altered LOC, hyperthermia Investigations: CBC (+/- incr'd WBC), ABG (Met acidosis), CK (rhabdo - correlates with disease severity), coags (risk of DIC), incr'd LFTs, electrolyte abN (hypo PO4, Ca, Mg; hyper Na, K), pan-culture to r/o sepsis, tox screen, renal function, myoglobinuria.  ECG, CXR (aspiration, infection), CT Head Optimization: Delay elective surgery. D/C any offending meds (Haldol, loxapine, maxeran, perphenazine, droperidol), rehydrate , maintain U/O (rhabdo), cool, r/o Ddx, ICU consult, +/- intubation for dLOC, Bromocryptine (2.5-20mg PO TID), muscle relaxants, dantrolene (reduced rigidity and heat production), ECT. Room Setup: Trigger-free anesthetic to be conservative, inotropes available, avoid the above mentioned drugs (most anti-emetics), CAS + invasive monitors, temp probe, Sux controversial if these pts need ECT. Crash cart available. Intraoperative Mgt: As above:  trigger free.  Use NdMBs to aid rigidity. Post-op: Likely need ICU post-op. Complications: hyper/hypotension, hyperthermia, hypermetabolic, volume deplete, renal failure, MH,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Special: thromboembolism, residual catatonia.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Parturient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of aspiration, difficult airway, rapid desaturation, aortocaval compression, 2 patients

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Maintenance uteroplacental perfusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid hypoxemia, hypotension, acidosis and hyperventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
FHR and uterus monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of preterm labour

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Obstetrical consulatation, tocolytics, Steroids if viable and < 37 wks

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Surgical considerations of a gravid uterus

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Approriate timing related to gestational age

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Exposure to potential teratogenic drugs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Ensure obstetrical involvement and FHR monitoring when possible

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid Teratogens

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain uteroplacental perfusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o maintain oxygenation,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o maternal MAP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o prevent acidosis, normocapnea

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Non-obstetrical surgery for the Parturient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Gestational age, Obstetrical history, underlying medical condition, adverse pregnancy associated features (PIH/HELLP/hyperemesis/Gestational Diabetes), CVS status, Preterm labor.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Volume status, CVS exam, detailed airway examination, uteriene tone/contractions. Investigations: Review fetal U/S, usual bloodwork, +- PIH bloodwork +- Echo depending on CVS exam Optimization: Delay elective surgery, essential surgery in early 2 nd  trimester, aspiration prophylaxis, consider steroids for fetal lung maturation (Betamethasone 6mg q 24hrs x 2days for infants < 37wks), consider tocolytic therapy (Nifedipine/tertbutaline (s/e's tachy, hypokalemia, hyperglycemia)/MgSo4/Indomethacin (high risk of ductus closure). OBS consult! Room Setup: Airway adjuncts, fetal heart rate monitor after 20-24 wks/vaginal probe/consider arterial line for CO2 insufflation. Left uterine displacement, calf compressors, temperature. Avoid laparoscopic procedures after end of 2 nd  trimester Intraoperative Mgt: GA or regional acceptable, avoid N2O (controversial). Maintain oxygenxation, uteroplacental perfusion, avoid hypocarbia (aim 30-35mmHg) and acidosis Specific Procedures: Laparoscopy - open trochar placement, low insufflations pressures 8-12mmHg;  ECT - OB Consult, intubate beyond 1st trimester (aspiration prophylaxis for all), monitor FHR, Not a risk factor for SA; Trauma - Early fetal U/S and FHR, All diagnostic modalities required (primacy of mother), C/S (stable mother, a viable fetus in distress, traumatic uterine rupture, unsalvageable mother with viable fetus, If fetus is pre-viable or dead, optimize mother (i.e. do not go for c-section, vaginal delivery can be performed later) Post-op: Moniter FHR and uteriene contractions, Risk of DVT Complications: Most serious fetal risk associated with surgery is due to intrauterine asphyxia: Maintain maternal oxygenation, oxygen tension and carrying capacity, uteroplacental perfusion. The most common causes of maternal hypotension: deep GA, sympathectomy with high spinal or epidural, aortocaval compression, hemorrhage, and hypovolemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Obesity: BMI >30, Morbid Obesity: BMI>40 kg/m2

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Physiologic Changes of Obesity:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Airway - potential difficult BMV / Intubation / Cricothyroidotomy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Respiratory Restrictive lung defect (dec. FRC/ERV/VC), assoc. OSA , risk of post-op hypoxemia / ventilation. Potential pHTN related to OSA.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CVS - Increased demand with limited reserve, incr. blood volume, CO, LVH, wall stress

<!-- PAGE=? -->
GI - Increased risk of aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Heme Hypercoagulability (2x risk of DVT)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Co-morbid disease: OSA, Obesity hypoventilation, HTN, IHD, CAD, CHF, Type 2 DM,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Altered Pharmacokinetics and Pharmacodynamics:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased LBW, altered drug dosing, increased pseudocholinesterase

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Sensitivity to opioids

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Reduced LA requirements 20-30% for NA techniques

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential technical difficulties: (positioning, monitoring, IV access)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Evaluate and optimize the physiologic  impact of obesity: OSA, pHTN, DM, CAD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Safely secure airway, avoiding aspiration and long acting agents: minimize post-op resp complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid thrombotic complications and peripheral nerve injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Consider regional technique, post op pain management vs resp depression

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Hx of difficult airway, OSA, CPAP, HTN, DM, hypothyroid, CAD, CHF, functional capacity, pHTN, Stroke, Renal failure, GeRD, Meds. PE: Detailed A/W exam for ease of laryngoscopy and BMV, CVS:  BP, Cardiomegaly: displaced PMI, CHF S3/S4, basilar crackles. pHTN: JVD, R parasternal heave, loud P2, Murmur of TR, hepatomegaly, edema). Resp: Focus on restrictive dysfx (rapid RR, shallow resps, ruddy color,  OSA (ruddy color, thick neck). Gastro - hepatic dysfunction (hepatomegaly, ascites, spider angiomas, jaundice).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: CBC: Polycythemia, Lytes, Cr, BUN, glc - if Htn, DM or on diuretics LFTs, PT, PTT if hepatic dysfunction. ABG if hypoxemia. ECG: Typically shows low voltage, LVH, strain: LA abnormalities. If pHTN: RVH, RBBB, P Pulmonale. Echo / Consider PFTs if severe (not cost effective in asympt obese patients nor utility in optimizing the postoperative mgt. Polysomnograph: 10 sec or more cessation of flow (apnea) (5/hr) or 50% reduction in flow or decrease in sat >4% 15/hr (hypopnea) is diagnostic of OSA. Apnea/Hypopnea index >30 = severe Optimization: Aspiration prophylaxis, avoid pre-op sedation, antisialagogue for AFI, DVT prophylaxis (SC heparin / compression stockings), Optimize co-existing diseases. CPAP. Room Setup: Difficult A/W equipment, glucometer, remainder depends on co-morbid disease. OR tables designed for 120-140kg patients. Position and pad carefully. Intraoperative Mgt: Local/Regional/GA. Avoid long acting agents. Do not use LMA's in morbid obesity. Difficult spinal/epidural , use 20-30% less dose due to increased spread. Doses based on lean body weight esp. NMDs. Use PPV / PEEP, extubate awake. Post-op: Resp insufficiency, consider OSA protocol, overnight oximetery, semi - recumbent positioning,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CPAP / BiPAP.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Obstetrical Hemorrhage

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency Situation with high materal and fetal morbidity & Mortality

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o requiring immediate resuscitation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Etiology & Risk factors

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o APH: Abruption, placenta previa, uterine rupture, vasa previa, other

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o PPH: Tone, tissue, thrombin, trauma, turnout Antepartum

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hemorrhagic Shock

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for DIC & massive transfusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pregnant Patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic goals:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Intrauterine Resuscitation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Optimize uteroplacental perfusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain adequate circulating blood volume and coagulation factors

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Facilitate safe and timely delivery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Clear lines of communications regarding ongoing HD & coagulation status

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Mobilize resources early

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Need for oxytocin in a increasingly hypovolemic patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Risk of preterm delivery vs risk of delaying delivery in compromised mother

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Regional in hypovolemic patient? (ie hypovolemic, unstable patient with difficult airway)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Bleeding patient with contraindications to many uterotonics (eg Pulm HTN, severe asthma…)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Differentials: APH - placenta previa(Multipara, Uterine scar, Risk of placenta accrete); Abruption (HTN, cocaine use, trauma, PROM); Uterine rupture (Uterine scarring, Tumultuous or prolonged labor, Trauma, iatrogenic); Vasa Previa (Severe fetal distress)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PPH - Uterine atony (Uterine overdistension, Augmented labour, Retained placenta, Operative delivery); Retained product; Genital trauma; Placenta accrete; Uterine inversion; Coagulaopathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
History: AMPLE, OBHx, fetal distress, ongoing blood loss, maternal compromise, coagulopathy P/E: Vitals, A/W, classification of stage of shock

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CBC, G&S, DIC screen, repeat…US

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Intrauterine resuscitation, Large bore IV access,  Volume resuscitation (blood), Aspiration prohylaxis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic options: Directed by - Fetal distress, Airway, Coagulopathy, Hypovolemia GA/RSI unless airway difficult. Regional contraindicated related to volume status / coagulaopathy / prolonged procedure. FOB if difficult airway. Consider TIVA Setup: CAS monitors, temp, Artline, +/- CVP, rapid transfuser, Emergency drugs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Specific management of OB hemorrhage:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Volume, blood components, uterotonics (oxy, hemabate 250 mcg IM/IU, misoprostol 600-800 pr/po/pb, ergot 0.25 mg by slow IV infusion, vasopressin 20 U in 100 cc injected diffusely into uterus), surgical measures (B-Lynch, vascular clamping/ligation, emergency hysterectomy, packing, massage), interventional radiology, Factor VII

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Postop disposition: Following massive transfusion a critical care bed is appropriate or at least a monitored bed with invasive monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Identify patients at risk

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Anticipate potential for failed intubation/ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid long-acting opioids, sedatives or other respiratory depressants

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o NSAIDs, acetamenophen, regional/local techniques to minimize pain (i.e. opioid sparing techniques)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Monitoring to decrease morbidity associated with apnea post-operatively

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Obstructive Sleep Apnea

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential difficult intubation/BMV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased incidence of peri-operative pulmonary complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased susceptibility to obstruction with sedatives/respiratory depressants

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 need for post-op monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiopulmonary alterations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypoxia, hypercarbia, polycythemia, systemic/pHTN, RV dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Co-morbid diseases including:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Obesity (60-90%), diabetes, CAD, HTN and congenital syndromes in children

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx : snoring, daytime somnolence, apneic periods during sleep, morning H/A, functional reserve, BiPAP, Home O2, congenital syndrome, history of difficult intubation/ventilation. Hx of Etoh, hypothyroid, sleep meds. Risk Factors: Male, middle aged, BMI > 30, Alcohol (evening), drug induced sleep, down's syndrome, acromegaly

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE : Room air sat, BMI > 30, neck circumference >17‖ M (16‖ F), A/W for ease of intubation/BMV, signs of CHF (JVP, S3/S4), signs of RVF (JVD, right sided S3/S4, systolic murmur of TR, hepatomegaly, signs of PHN [loud P2])

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations : CBC (polycythemia), ABG (baseline PaCO2, PaO2), +/- Echo (cor pulmonale), TSH, GH if acromegaly. Overnight oximetry (at home>15/hr desats > 4%). Gold standard is polysomnography (5 or more apneic events per hour or 15 or more hypopneic events per hour during a 7 hr sleep study. Apnea Hypopnea index: Mild AHI 6-20, Moderate 20-40, Severe = >40.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization

<!-- PAGE=? -->
: Weight loss, CPAP pre-op, smoking cessation, CAD/HTN optimization

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup

<!-- PAGE=? -->
: Difficult airway cart, art line for repeat ABGs, CPAP in PAR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt

<!-- PAGE=? -->
: Local>Regional>Neuraxial (opioids-free), GA - ETT > LMA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid long acting resp.depressants, adjuvant analgesia (local, NSAIDS)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op :  CPAP, step-down unit, continuous sat monitoring until sats >90% sleeping. At VGH it's a minimum of 3H in PAR. Consider 24H of monitoring if patient demonstrates apneic episudes <90% or severe preexisting OSA (AHI > 30) or requiring complicated pain management. Patient d/c'd to ward should continue intensive monitoring (RR/SS Q1H x 48h, then Q4h).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Surgical Emergency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Further expulsion of eye contents risks blindness

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Full stomach/risk of aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Trauma & other associated injuries

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations for Eye Surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Shared airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Immobile patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Oculocardiac reflex

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Smooth emergence with minimal coughing

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Minimize risk of aspiration (prophylaxis, RSI)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Minimize increases in IOP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Avoid coughing, straining and hypertensive response to laryngoscopy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Avoid hypercarbia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Use deep anesthesia, barbituates

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Consider avoiding succinylcholine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Open Eye

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Mechanism of injury, associated trauma, last meal (full stomach), PMHx (may be elderly)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Airway examination

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
As directed by Hx & PE

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: For pediatric patient for which an inhalational induction is necessary, may consider delaying until fasted but generally cannot delay; aspiration prophylaxis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
GETA  only option

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CAS monitors, atropine available (OC reflex)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Deep anesthesia and muscle relaxation needed to prevent coughing or movement.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Extubate awake with minimal coughing or straining (balance risk of aspiration with smooth emergence)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pacemakers

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Indication for implantation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PM - SSS, AV block

<!-- PAGE=? -->
AICD - VT, Vfib, cardiomyopathy EF < 35%

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Minimize risk of and prepare for potential for pacemaker / AICD interference & failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Magnet

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pacer clinic interrogation periop

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Disable antitachycardia functions

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Alternate pacing strategies

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Sympathomimetics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Transvenous pacemaker or pacing PAC

<!-- PAGE=? -->
External defib device

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Co-existing disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Associated CAD / Cardiomyopathy EF<35%

<!-- PAGE=? -->
HTN / CRF / DM

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Issues:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Identify & optimize underlying cardiac status

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anticipate and prevent failure or interference

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid inappropriate inhibition or triggering of pacemaker by electrocautery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid inadvertent activation of AICD leading to life-threatening rhythm

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prevent damage to device

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Indication for pacemaker, pacemaker dependency, last interrogation, type of pace maker, response to magnet, symptoms of pacemaker malfunctioning (CHF/Syncope etc), ICD frequency. Coexisting illnesses, cardiac disease. Type of OR, cautery being used, location of surgery.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Pulse, Location of generator, Rhythm, CHF >> Investigations: Lytes/EKG/CXR for type of pacemaker, lead location.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Underlying disease, pre-op interrogation if elective, disable ICD/tachyarrythmia sensing , reprogram to demand mode, call manufacturer.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: 5 lead ECG (disable ‗artifact filter', consider artline for hemodynamic capture,  Magnet (avoid in ICD unless necessary >> can disable permanently), Pacing pads (AP positioning, away from generator), Defibrillator, chronotropic meds (Atropine, Isoproterenol (2-10mcq/min), Epinephrine, Dopamine), consider telemetric programmer present if interference expected/hemodynamic instability.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative: Bipolar, short bursts, avoid generator between cautery and ground. (with magnet 60% go to 60-100bpm asynch, 25% go to asynch at program rate, 15% brief 60-100 beats pacing event, some may produce no change)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Reprogramming and interrogation by pacemaker clinic prior to discharge to ward Special: Pacemaker Mediated Tachycardia (PMT): Dual Chamber pacemaker w/ magnet defaults to demand mode >> retrograde p waves which are then -tracked‖ after magnet removal. Tx: Reapply and remove magnet.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 1 - Chamber Paced 2- Sensed 3- Response (T/I/D/0)  4- Rate Modulation 5 - Arrhythmia Treatment (Paced / Shocked / Dual)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 AICD: I = Shock Chamber, II = Antitachycardia pacing chamber A/V/D, III = Tachycardia detection E/H Electrogram vs Hemodynamic, IV = Antibradycardia pacing chamber A/V/D

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pain

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency situation requiring immediate management and Dx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Classification of the pain

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 nociceptive

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 neuropathic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 malignant or non-malignant

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Develop DDx whiling ruling out a medical or surgical emergency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Compartment syndrome, nerve compression & ischemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Metastases, infection, inflammation, fracture, visceral (GI, vascular, renal)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Develop a comprehensive management plan

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 biopsychosocial assessment  (depression, suicide)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 multidisciplinary resources

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Specific Management Strategies  Multimodal approach

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Biological - Disease-specific treatment, Physical (Exercise, stretching, heat, massage), Pharmocologic (symptom-related): PO, IV, SC, epidural, intrathecal, regional blocks, Neurostimulation (TENS, SCS), Neurodestructive (Chemical, thermal, surgical)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Psychological/Social

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Red Flags - thoracic pain, fever, weight loss, bladder/bowel dysfunction, history Ca, gait problems, saddle anesthesia, age <20 or >55

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Yellow Flags - negative attitude that back pain is harmful or severely disabling, fear-avoidance behavior, expectation that passive rather than active treatments is beneficial, depression, low morale, social withdrawl, social or financial problems, litigation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Differential Diagnosis for Lower Back Pain:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mechanical:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Discs: annular tears, internal disc disruption or herniation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Sciatica (either referred mechanical or nerve root compression)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 ligaments, periosteum

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 spondlysis, spondylolisthesis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 spinal stenosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Non-mechanical: Spinal

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Neoplasia: metastatic (breast, prostate,  lymphoma; primary spinal cord; retroperitoneal tumours

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Infection: osteomyelitis; septic discitis; paraspinal or epidural abscess; HZ

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Inflammatory arthritis: AS, IBD; Reiters syndrome; Psoriatic Spondylitis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Trauma (fracture)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Visceral

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Pelvic organs: prostates; endometriosis; PID

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Renal: nephrolithiassis; pyelonephritis; perinephric abscess

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Vascular: AAA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 GI: pancreatitis; cholycystitis; perforated bowel

<!-- PAGE=? -->
WHO Relief Ladder/Algorithim for Cancer Pain

<!-- PAGE=? -->
3-step -ladder‖ for cancer pain relief

<!-- PAGE=? -->
correct drug, correct dose, at the correct time  80-90% effective

<!-- PAGE=? -->
If pain occurs  prompt oral administration of drugs in following order:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Nonopioids (NSAIDs and Acetominophen) +/- adjuvants

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mild opioids (ie. Codeine, oxycodone) +/- adjuvants

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Strong opioids (ie. Morphine, hydromorphone) +/- adjuvants

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Adjuvants also used to calm fears and anxiety. To maintain freedom from pain:  give regularly (q3-6h) and not -prn‖ Surgical intervention on appropriate nerves may provide further pain relief if drugs are not wholly effective

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Considerations for Phantom Limb Pain:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Common chronic neuropathic, non-malignant pain - distinct from stump pain

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Difficult to treat, warranting multidisciplinary involvement including physio, heat, and psychiatry

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multi-modal analgesia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
aggressive pre-op pain management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
avoidance of aggravating factors, including cold, stress, stump irritation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
liberal use of regional anesthesia, anti-neuropathic agents, simple analgeics, opioids

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Parkinson's Disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Central dopamine deficiency leading to rigidity, tremors and late dementia.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential difficult airway due to cervical TMJ rigidity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased risk of aspiration secondary to bulbar dysfunction, gastropareisis, esoph dysfnx.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Autonomic instability , NE depletion (med), increased risk of hypotension on induction + regional

<!-- PAGE=? -->
restrictive lung disease secondary to chest wall rigidity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased risk of perioperative A/W obstruction, Resp. failure, exacerbation of Neurologic symptoms (maxeran droperidol, nozinan) , and delerium

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Interactions with medical therapy : continue current therapy,  MAOi's (type B) and Demerol (seizures rigidity and hypertension), Levodopa (can deplete NE stores).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Elderly patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Safely manage patient's airway: RSI vs. hemodynamic lability, difficult airway.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Continue anti-parkinson medications perioperatively, avoid anti-dopaminergic meds

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maximize respiratory function

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Onset and severity of disease, medications, previous anesthetic history.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Particular attention to airway, orthostatic symptoms, neuro exam (pill-rolling tremor, rigidity etc), volume status.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: Nothing specific

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Continue anti-parkinson medications (L-dopa only oral, absorbed prox SB) >> NG for long surgery, immediately post-op. Aspiration prophylaxis.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: Appropriate airway equipment, direct acting agents for hypotension, consider arterial line

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Volatiles or TIVA, be aware of narcotic induced rigidity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Increased risk for hypoventilation, respiratory compromise, and post op delirium >> use atypical antipsychotics if necessary (Olanzapine/Quetiapine/Risperadone), worsening parkinson's >> restart meds ASAP.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Physiologic changes:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Altered airway anatomy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
higher risk of laryngospasm

<!-- PAGE=? -->
rapid desaturation on induction or apnea

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Dec. Cardiovascular Reserve

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 increased vagal tone

<!-- PAGE=? -->
altered pharmacokinetics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 higher MAC, higher TBW

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Limited or no cooperation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Need to communicate with and manage parents

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pediatric Patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Inc. risk of aspiration, Limited time for optimization and investigation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Airway compromise

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Potential for catastrophic loss of the airway, hypoxemia, respiratory acidosis, cardiac arrest, negative pressure pulmonary edema

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mobilization of resources and collaboration with other specialties: ENT, ICU, ER

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pediatric patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pediatric Stridor

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DDx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Congenital (generally chronic symptoms) - Nose (Choanal atresia, Septum deformities, Turbinate hypertrophy), Pharynx (Craniofacial anomalies - Crouzon's, Pierre-Robin, Apert's syndromes; Tongue - macroglossia and glossoptosis), Larynx (Laryngomalacia, webs, cysts, hemangioma, stenosis), Trachea (stenosis, vascular rings & slings, tracheomalacia)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Infections - epiglottitis, tracheitis, peritonisillar and retropharyngeal abscess, croup (parainfluenza), RSV, Influenza A and B, Mycoplasma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Tumors - Enphalocele, Teratoma, Lymphoma, Granuloma, Fibroma, Papilloma, Neuroblastoma, Hemangioma, Rhabdomyosarcoma, Cystic hygroma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Trauma - RLN palsy (post PDA repair, thyroid surgery), Post extubation (Croup/ edema, Vocal cord injury or paralysis, Subglottic stenosis), Caustic injury, Inhalational injury, Facial trauma or burn

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Allergic - Anaphylaxis, hereditary angioneurotic edema

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Miscellaneous - Hypocalcemia, Foreign bodies (airway or esophageal), Spasmodic croup, Exercise, GERD, Juvenile RA with cricoarytenoid involvement

<!-- PAGE=? -->
HISTORY AND PHYSICAL MAY BE ABBREVIATED DUE TO URGENCY

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: AMPLE; onset of symptoms (acute, subacute vs chronic); circumstances (related to feeding); associated symptoms (constitutional, drooling, dysphagia, vocal changes/muffling, hoarseness); previous episodes (chronic or recurrent episodes - congenital, tumor or vocal cord dysfunction); OSA (suggests pharyngeal cause: tonsils or adenoids); PMHx - intubation, PDA/necl Sx, immunization Hx Px: VS; general (Toxemia, Fever, Hypotension, tachycardia) weight; A/W exam (size of tongue and mandible, craniofacial anatomy, neck edema); Respiratory (WOB/ accessory muscle use, nasal flaring, retraction, Cyanosis, Clubbing: underlying CHD or bronchiectasis, stridor may be heard in inspiration, expiration or during the entire respiratory cycle); Hemangiomas, café au lait spots; Anaphylaxis: rash, hypotension Inv: CBC: leukocytosis, BldCx; Imaging: unstable: skip radiology and evaluate their airway in the OR with ENT; accompany to radiology suite with A/W equipment; Neck radiographs - generally nonspecific; CXR Mediastinal masses, Vascular rings, R aortic arch, FB; Airway fluoroscopy; CT scan; nasopharyngoscopy Options: Compromised airways should be evaluated and secured with direct visualization in the OR with ENT present under spontaneous ventilation; FB: SV with rigid bronch Anesthetic Setup: difficult A/W cart, ENT surgeon, skilled help, Rigid bronch, cricothyroidotomy (age > 6) Monitors: CAS, consider transcutaneous CO2 monitoring for rigid bronch Drugs: Succinylcholine, Atropine, vasoactive agents if suspicion of severe sepsis, TIVA vs Inhalational Management: Moribund: awake DL; Stable child: SV GA, IH - 4% ET sevo, TIVA - Propofol infusion at 200 u/k/m, Remi 0.1 u/k/m; DL when unresponsive (may take ~10min); ETT placed (use 0.5-1.0 size smaller); Topicalize A/W prior to rigid bronch (lido 3mg/kg) Typically 1-4yrs, max in 4hr, resolution in 24h; DDx; humidified oxygen; Neb epi 0.5

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergence: PICU, FB removal: consider intubating and extubating awake (aspiration & laryngospasm risk) Post extubation Stridor: ml/kg -watch for rebound; Dex: 4-8mg IV; Emotional support; Heliox; Admission

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pharyngeal Abscess

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Urgent/Emergent Procedure with Risk of Aspiration and acute A/W obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Difficult airway management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Distorted Anatomy, trismus, difficult topicalization

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of abscess rupture and lung soilage

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Shared airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Life Threatening Complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
AW obstruction, abscess rupture & aspiration, sepsis/toxic shock syndrome, mediastinitis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk Factors / Co-morbidites

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pediatric, DM, IVDU. HIV, ETOH, ENT malignancy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Efficiently + Safely secure airway recognizing evolving obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Consider preoperative abcess needle drainage

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Prevent abscess rupture and lung soilage

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Fluid resuscitation and appropriate Abx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o uncooperative patient (peds) vs. difficult airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o full stomach vs. potential inhalational induction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o deep plane of anesthesia vs. potential hypotention from sepsis/ dehydration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o awake FOB does not visualize ETT passing abscess (potential for rupture by ETT)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Abcess time course, associated symptoms (drooling, dysphagia, stridor, dysphonia, hoarseness); presence of sepsis; establish risk fx/comorbidies - DM, IVDU, HIV, underlying head & neck malignancy, alcoholism

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Vitals (respiratory distress, sepsis); detailed airway examination (mouth opening/trismus - pterygoid muscle spasm, edema, submandibular edema, tracheal deviation, Torticollis / dec neck ROM, Horner's syndrome & cranial nerve palsies); resp exam for infection/empyema; CVS exam for hypovolemia/sepsis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: Limited impact on management; CBC, Blood Cx, CXR, neck xray, CT head & neck

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Aspiration prophylaxis, Antisialogogue, fluid resuscitation, antibiotics, needle aspiration and decompression by surgeon

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: SV induction (peds); awake FOI (may be difficult to topicalize); tracheostomy under local (maybe difficult anatomy); blind techniques not recommended.  Use slow, gentle technique to minimize risk of abcess rupture.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: Difficult airway cart, skilled assistants, ENT surgeon present Intraoperative Mgt: Discuss plan with surgeon (shared airway); dexamethasone to decrease edema Post-op: Consider postop ventilation/ICU or extubation over tube exchanger depending on severity, continue abx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Airway obstruction, aspiration of abcess contents, laryngospasm, sepsis, post-obstructive pulmonary edema, abcess spread (meninges, lung, epidural space, etc), vascular injury/hemorrhage

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pheochromocytoma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prevention and Management of hemodynamic instability:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Preoperative optimization, Avoidance of SNS stimulation, histamine release, & unopposed alpha

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Intra-operative monitoring and management of HTN, tachycardia, arrhythmias

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Relative intravascular volume depletion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
End-organ dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypertrophic or dilated cardiomyopathy, IHD, CVA, Hyperglycemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Associated endocrinopathies:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hyperparathyroid (MEN2a)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Medullary thyroid CA (MEN 2a & 2b)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Neurofibromatosis (Von Recklinghausen's)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o von Hippel-Lindau disease (cerebellar hemangiobastoma, RCC)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-operative complications :

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o HTN or hypotension, Hypoglycemia, Adrenal insufficiency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevent, recognize and be prepared to treat pheochromocytoma crisis:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Adequate pre-op optimization - Alpha blockade; Volume resuscitation; Anxiolysis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Tight hemodynamic control

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid SNS surges (anxiolysis, deep induction, Epidural)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid histamine releasing drugs(catecholamine release from tumor)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Triad of diaphoresis, H/A, tachycardia in HTN pt; flushing; orthostatic hypotension; end-organ dysfx (CHF; IHD), endocrinopathies; 5Ps - Pressure (HTN); Perspiration; Pallor; Pain (H/A; CP); Palpitations (associated with tremor, wt loss, fever) PE: Vitals (including posturals), CHF Signs; volume status; caution with abd exam Investigations: CBC (polycythemia), Lytes, BUN, Cr, Glucose (hyperglycemia), Ca ++  (Men 2), CXR, ECG (LVH, ischemia, prolonged QTc, abmornal R waves, ECHO (hypertrophic or dilated cardiomyopathy), MIBI (CAD), PET/CT to localized non-adrenal masses Optimization: Endo consult; 10-14 days required; correct hypovolemia; Phenoxybenzamine 10-20 mg po bid or Prazosin 1 mg tid or qid until Hct drops by 5%, no BP>165/90 in hospital x 48hrs (1hr continuous in PACU), orthostatic hypotension (not below 80/45), ECG normalization, <1 PVC q5min (Roizen criteria). B-Block for tumours that secrete epi, or reflex tachycardia (after effective alpha blockade); Steroid replacement for bilateral adrenalectomies, CCB & Mg for refractory HTN; Preg - <24 weeks remove, >24 treat - epidural, C/S Anesthetic Options: GETA +/- Epidural; no data that RA is better than GA Room Setup: CAS + 5 Lead; Aline; Foley; CVP; (PAC, TEE); Temp; Glucometer; ER Drugs (use rapid acting titratable  meds, particularly during high risk times like intubation (remi, lido), tumour manipulation (phentolamine, NTP) and ligation of venous drainage (fluid, phenylephrine) Intraoperative Mgmt: communicate with surgeon throughout; Deep plane of anesthesia prior to stimulation (lido, remi); avoid (ketamine, ephedrine, pancuronium, histamine releasing agents, desflurane); Preremoval: HTN, Tachycardia, arrhythmia (Phentolamine 1-5mg IV, SNP 1-2ug/kg IV bolus, NTG, labetalol, lido, Mg); Postremoval hTN (fluids, phenyl, dopamine, decr anesthetic) Postoperative: HDU; Monitor HDs and glucose may still be HTN post-op (cleared over 7-10days) Complications: Hypertension ; Hypotension ; Hypoglycemia ; Adrenal insufficiency (if bilateral)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pneumonectomy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Postresection pulmonary function (suitability for procedure)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Mechanics (ppoFEV1>40%) / Lung Function (ppoDLCO>40%) / Cardiopulmonary interaction (ppoVO2 max>15ml/kg/min)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Perioperative respiratory and cardiac complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypoxemia, hypercapnea, atelectasis, pneumonia, ALI, respiratory failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o pHTN with RV failure, Ischemia, Arrythmias (afib)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Co-morbid disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Malignacy 4 Ms (Mass, Metastases, Metabolic derangement, Medications), Smoker, COPD, CAD, PVD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations of OLV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o DLETT placement / Physiologic changes - hypoxia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Postoperative pain and monitoring for complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Respiratory failure, Arrhythmia, BPF, Herniation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize respiratory function pre-operatively

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize oxygenation during OLV and plan for immediate extubation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize respiratory mechanics post-operatively

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o pain mgmt, fluid mgmt

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Minimize modifiable complication risks

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 hypothermia, arrhythmias, ischemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: assess RF for difficult EBT; RESP: dyspnea, exercise tolerance, cough, wheeze, positional aw aggravation; pneumonia; CVS: functional status, RV dysfunction; Hx of underlying resp dz; Malingancy  4 M's PE: VS; Distress; AW; RESP (COPD, tracheal compression); CVS (CAD, arrhythmias, pHTN, SVC syndrome) Investigations: CBC, coags, lytes, iCa, ABG, X-match; CXR, ECG, CT, +/- ECHO; PFTs, V/Q scan Slinger's 3 legged Stool : Resp Mechanics (ppoFEV1 < 40%)  Gas exchange (ppoDLCO < 40%) Cardiopulmonary interaction (ppoVO2max <15ml/kg/min) Other factors: RV/TLC ratio > 50%; < 2 flights stairs; 6 min walk < 2000ft; Exercise SpO2 <4%;  ppoVo2 max < 10 ml/kg/min may be an absolute contraindication to pulmonary resection Optimization: Smoking cessation; COPD optimization; CAD optimization; +/- antiarrhythmia prophylaxis Anesthetic Options: GA +/- TEA; lung isolation  R or L DLT; Bronchial blocker; Mainstem Bronchus intubation with single lumen tube or 2 single lumen tubes Room Setup: Drugs (inotropes, vasopressors & antiarrhythmics); CAS monitors, 5 lead ECG, pre A-line; CVP; +/TEE & PAC; Difficult AW cart; FOB; different size DLT & bronchial blocker; DLT size based on tracheal width (mm)  18 = 41; 16 = 39; 15 = 37, 14 = 35 Intraoperative Mgt : Volatiles inhibit HPV (halothane worst), consider TIVA; epidural LA / narcotics; maintain 2 lung ventilation as long as possible; avoid N2O; FiO2 0.5-1.0, VT 5-8ml/kg, PEEP dependant Lung, permissive hypercapnia; may need intermittent 2-lung ventilation, intermittent recruitment maneuvers, CPAP or O2 insufflation to nondependent lung; minimize peri-op IV fluids; Extubate early to  risk of barotrauma / pulmonary infection; for ppoFEV1 >40%, normal extubation criteria; for ppoFEV1 <30% + poor exercise tolerance, staged weaning from mechanical ventilation is best. Post-op: HDU/PAR; Pain control; supplemental O2 Complications: Hypoxia with OLV; ↑ a/w pressures; herniated heart; ruptured bronchus; RLN injury, RV overload; torsion of lobe on operative side; post-pneumonectomy ALI. Special  Predictors of Hypoxemia during OLV: Side (R>L); Hypoxemia on 2 lung ventilation; Supine; Normal

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PFT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Popliteal Nerve Block L4-S3

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Note: US techniques use high frequency 10-15MHz probe.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Indications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anatomy:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ankle and foot surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Sciatic nerve at the level of popliteal fossa, superficial and lateral to popl. Art.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Common peroneal gives off sup. and deep peroneal nerves and lateral sural nerve. Tibial gives of medial and lateral plantar nerves and medial sural nerve.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Contraindications: Post-op neurological monitoring, risk of post-op compartment syndrome, previous politeal artery bypass (relative)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risks:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Infection, hematoma, nerve injury, LA toxicity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Approach:  Intertindinous (Classic): Prone, Landmarks: poplit. Crease, tendons of semitendinous and semimembrinous medially and biceps femoris laterally. Insert 10cm 22g needle 7cm above the crease, and 1 cm lateral to the midway point bw the tendons. Goal 0.2-0.5mA, 0.7mA if peripheral neuropathy!. Aim: Plantar flexion or inversion indicative of tibial nerve stimulation whichi s more reliable than CP (dorsiflexion and eversion).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Lateral: Supine, landmarks are popliteal crease, vastus lateralis (superior) and biceps femoris (inferior). With palpating hand on biceps femoris muscle, insert needle (10cm) perpendicular to skin at point marked 7cm above popliteal crease, midway between tendons. Contact Femur, then withdraw to skin and redirect 30 degrees inferiorly.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
35-40mL LA, slow onset 10-25mins

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Saphenous NB: for tourniquet, or supplement popliteal block

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Inject 7-10ml LA subcutaneously from the Tibial Tuberosity, medially.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Tibial

<!-- PAGE=? -->
tuberosity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Line of

<!-- PAGE=? -->
injection

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medial

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Lateral
