<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of Porphyric Crisis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoidance of pharmacologic and physiologic triggers

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Neurologic dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Autonomic Hypertension, Tachycardia , Abd pain, Vomiting, diarrhea, orthostatic hypotension

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cranial - Bulbar dysfunction ( Aspiration Risk )

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Peripheral Respiratory weakness , peripheral neuropathies, quadraplegia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anxiety, confusion, hysteria, seizures , coma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CRF with severe volume depletion and electrolyte abnormalities Hypokalemia, hyponatremia (SIADH), hypomagnesemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Adequate optimization

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid prolonged fast (dehydration), correct anemia, manage pain/anxiety

<!-- PAGE=? -->
2.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid triggers:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Barbiturates, etomidate, steroids, diazepam,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Fasting, progesterone, estrogen, infection, anemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Smoking, ETOH, marijuana, ecstasy, amphetamines, cocaine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Be prepared to treat an acute crisis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Fluids, glucose, hematin, cimetidine, somatostatin, plasmaphereis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Manage Sz with midazolam/propofol - avoid diazepam, STP, phenytoin

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Porphyria

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Determine type of porphyria (acute/inducible), family history, known triggers, current symptoms - focus on CNS (Sz, confunsion, neuropathy), bulbar dysfunction, tachycardia, palpitations, CHF, respiratory failure. PE: Vitals + posturals, volume status, GCS, neuro exam, CVS (HTN / hypotension, tachycardia, CHF) Investigations : CBC, lytes, BUN, Cr, Glucose, LFTs (if any suspicion of hepatic dysfunction), Mg, Calcium, Coags, ECG (LVH), CXR, +/-PFTs, ABGs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Hematology consult, Correct anemia, avoid prolonged fast (IV glucose), aspiration prophylaxis, Correct metabolic abnormalities and volume status, Anxiolysis with midazolam

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: CAS + 5, art line, aggressive multimodal (regional only if you have a good preop neuro exam) Anesthetic options: Local, Regional (Preop neuro exam, resp function, bupivicaine), or GA (trigger free) Intraoperative management: Management dictated by extent of cardiorespiratory dysfunction. Generally Propofol, Succ, Roc, Narcoric, Volatile, Neostigmine/glycopyrrolate

<!-- PAGE=? -->
: IV glucose load, fluid bolus (D10NS), Beta-blocker (if hypertensive/tachycardic), Hematin (3-4 mg/kg), octreotide, plasmapheresis (may reduce pain), midazolam/propofol for Sz, Manage

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Acute Porphyria crisis electrolyte disturbances

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Unsafe Drugs : barbiturates, etomidate, NSAIDs (diclofenac, ketorolac), ACE-I, CCB, Diazepam, Steroids (estrogen, progresterone…), Cephalosporins, Phenytoin, ergotamine Disbuted: Lidocaine, Maxeran (stemetil OK), other NSAIDs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Posterior Fossa Surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of inc. ICP / obstructive hydrocephalus

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intra -op Complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Injury to vital brainstem structures (CNs IV-XII, CVS/Resp centers)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o VAE and paradoxical air embolism

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hemodynamic instability during brainstem manipulation (arrhythmias, hypotension)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hemorrhage

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypothermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Neurophysiologic monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraop considerations

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o sitting position

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Shared airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Prolonged surgical time

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain CPP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Vigilant monitoring of hemodynamics for early signs brainstem injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Provide brain relaxation to facilitate surgical exposure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevent and manage complications related to positioning (VAE, hemodynamic instability, tension pneumocephalus, macroglossia, quadriplegia, peripheral nerve injury)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Establish preoperative neurologic dysfunction - inc. ICP (a.m. headache, N/V), cranial nerve deficits (a/w obstruction, aspiration). Contraindications to sitting position - absolute (Ventriculoatrial shunt; RAP>PCWP; PFO; Cerebral ischemia when upright & awake) & relative (extremes of age; uncontrolled HTN; COPD) PE: Vitals including GCS, postural BP; Cardiopulmonary for instability & aspiration; Neurological exam for  ICP, Cranial Nerve, cerebellar & bulbar dysfunction.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: CBC, Lytes, BUN, Creat, X-match, Osmolality (Mannitol) . Imaging - ECHO to screen PFO; CT head for mass effects/  ICP/herniation/obstructive hydrocephalus.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: pre-op dexamethasone for tumor edema, ICP management, volume loading to mitigate positioning hemodynamics, Aspiration prophylaxis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: GETA - balanced technique with volatile or TIVA if neurophysiological monitoring (BAER, EMG facial nerve)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: CAS with 5 lead (dysrhythmias with brainstem compression), temp probe, Art line transducer on arm (appreciate that Cerebral circulation is above in sitting position), CVP/Bunegin multi-orifice catheter 2 cm below SVC/RA junction (confirmed with TEE/CXR), Precordial Doppler (3 rd -6 th  Right sternal ICS).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Vasopressors/vasodilators (post-op HTN), mannitol, atropine +/-TCP for bradycardia (if in brainstem) Intraoperative Mgt : Sitting position: SCD's/ G-suit minimize venous pooling, two finger breadths between sternum and chin to  potential for macroglossia and cervical cord ischemia, avoid excessive hip flexion (sciatic/ peroneal nerve injury), confirm ETT position with neck flexion;

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: possible ventilation d/t A/W edema, CN dysfunction, Cardiopulmonary dysfunction, dec. LOC; HDU to monitor for CVS, resp, neurologic deterioration - inc. ICP, dysrhythmia, central apnea, aspiration Complications: VAE, brain stem dysfunction (ECG changes are sensitive), tension pneumocephalus (CSF replaced with air - H/A, Sz, confusion, dec. LOC - CT, burr hole), quadriplegia (ischemia d/t cervical flexion)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pregnancy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Difficult airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Airway edema of pregnancy exaggerated

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications and organ dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ICH, seizures, cerebral edema

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Conpensated hypovolemia, LV dysfunction, HTN crisis, HD instability and shock

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Noncardiogenic pulmonary edema (dec. oncotic pressure)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Renal dysfunction, Thrombocytopenia, coagulopathy, infrequently DIC

<!-- PAGE=? -->
HELLP syndrome (Hemolysis, Elevated Liver enzymes, Low Platelets)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations of antihypertensive / anticonvulsant therapy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of fetal distress and need for operative delivery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Decreased UPP, IUGR, abruptio placentae, premature labor and delivery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Control maternal HD - prevent HTN crisis  & ICH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevent & manage eclampsia - MgSO4

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize intravascular volume & avoid pulmonary edema

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize end organ perfusion and oxygen delivery, including UPP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DDx: Pain, Cushing's, hypoxia/hypercarbia,cocaine, withdrawal, NMS, serotonin syndrome, essential hypertension, pheo, thryotoxicosis, carcinoid

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Preeclampsia and HELLP Syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Rule out other causes, evaluate for end organ dysfunction (evaluation of CNS, cardioresp, coagulation, GI, renal all important); Risk factors - Chronic HTN, primip, Previous Hx, multiples, Age, Race, Obesity PE: airway airway airway; VS, volume status, heart failure, bruising Investigations: serial CBCs, G&S, lytes, BUN, Cr, Uric Acid, U/A for protein, LFTs, CXR, 12 lead, ECHO Optimization: Asp. prophylaxis, close communication with OB & NICU, early IV access/bloodwork, serial CBCs, early labour epidural, MgSO4 for Sz prophylaxis (6 g IV bolus over 15 minutes, then 1 - 2 g/hr / monitor for toxicity / resp depression, dec. reflexes / antedote - CaGluc 1 amp, potentiates NMB), antihypertensive therapy (Labetalol 5 mg IVP, doubling q5min max 300 mg, Hydralazine 5 - 10 mg IV q10 minutes, NTG 50 100  g IVP, nitroprusside, Nifedipine, Esmolol 1.5 mg/kg to blunt  BP associated with laryngoscopy); platelets (count <50), steroids? Room Setup: CAS +5 lead +/-art line +/-CVP for CHF, IV x2; difficult A/W cart; Consider blood warmer, immediate access to PRBC, FFP, Plts; Draw up additional induction agent +/- remi, esmolol; Peds and OB Intraoperative Mgt: Regional if no contraindications (coags, thrombocytopenia, inc. ICP) - volume load with colloid prior to regional (no fluid with GA - aim for 80ml/kg), tight hemodynamic control; GA requires deep induction - Thio 4mg/kg, lido 1.5mg/kg, remi 1-2u/kg (or +/- esmolol 1.5mg/kg), sux 1.5mg/kg; treat hypotension. If bleeding secondary to uterine atony, TIVA is reasonable Post-op: HDU for 24-48 hrs post-op (hypertension may peak post partum) Complications: DIC, PPH, pulmonary edema, Seizures, ICH, ARF Classifications: Chronic HTN: before 20wks; Preeclampsia:  HTN > 20 wks SBP>140 or DBP >90 AND proteinuria of >0.3g/24h; Severe preeclampsia:  SBP>160 or DBP>110; proteinuria >5g/24h or >3+; CNS dysfunction: blurred vision, altered mental status, severe headache; Liver capsule distension: RUQ or epigastric pain; ↑ transaminases of 2X normal; Thrombocytopnenia < 100,000; Oliguria < 500 mls in 24 hours; IUGR; Pulmonary edema or cyanosis; CVA; Eclampsia:  above plus seizures

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Altered airway anatomy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Impaired temperature and glucose regulation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Other physiologic derangements of prematurity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Resp - RDS, BPD, rapid desat, post-op apnea, persistent pHTN

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o CVS - HR/preload dependant CO, Transitional circulation/PDA, bradycadia, CHD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o CNS - IVH, seizures, ROP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o GI - GERD, NEC

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Heme - Anemia, thrombocytopenia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Altered pharmacology - inc. Vd, opioid sensitivity, dec. clearance, protein binding, metabolism, dec. MAC

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Difficult IV access and monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ensure optimization of multisystem derangements including respiratory, cardiovascular, hepatic, renal, hematological

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anticipate fluid / electrolyte / glucose derangements and optimize preoperatively

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ensure continuous temperature monitoring and maintain normothermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prematurity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Uncuffed ETT size 2.5 for < 1000g or 28 weeks 3.0 for 1000-2000g or 28-34 weeks 3.5 for 2000-3000g or 34-38 weeks 3.5-4.0 for larger / older neonates

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: PCA, Obstetrical hx, PMHx since birth and assess for complications (IVH, retinopathy, PPHTN/PDA, CHD, RDS/BPD, hx apnea, GERD, NEC, hypoglycemia, anemia, thrombocytopenia, etc), meds

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Vitals, weight, ins/outs, IV access, ventilator parameters, CVS (cap refill, fontanel, perfusion, murmurs, CHF), RESP (WOB, retractions, wheeze, crackles)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CBC, lytes, Cr, coags, bili, glucose, ABG, CXR, AXR, head U/S, ECHO

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Optimize volume status (esp if CHF), glucose, acidosis, coagulopathy, transfuse (Hb>100 if cardioresp disease), NPO (2hrs clear fluid, 4hrs breast milk), pretreat with atropine/glycopyrrolate, Vit K (1mg)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: GA - muscle relaxant + opioid may be tolerated best.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: Warm room/forced air warmer, consider NICU ventilator, epinephrine/resusc drugs drawn up to exact doses, pre & post-ductal SpO2, appropriately sized ETT (leak at 20cm H2O , circuit Intraoperative Mgt: Depends on case, avoid SNS stim (risk of IVH), muscle relaxant/narcotic vs. desflurane/remifentanil for rapid emergence; be aware of impaired metabolism/excretion of drugs, FiO2 to maintain SaO2 88-92%

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: PTX, hypoglycemia, paradoxical air embolism Post-op: Apnea monitoring if PCA < 50-60 wks (risk fx: prematurity, PCA, HCT <30%, hx apnea, chronic respiratory disease e.g. BPD, neurological disease)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pulmonary Hypertension

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mean PAP > 25mmHg at rest or 30mmHG during exercise

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for acute perioperative RV dysfunction and hemodynamic collapse

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimize pulmonary pressures and right heart function

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Avoid hypoxia, hypercarbia, acidosis, hypothermia, sympathetic stimulation (pain), high/low lung volumes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Cautious fluid administration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Maintain RV perfusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Associated Conditions

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o COPD, obesity, OSA, CHD, valvular disease (MR), CHF, CTD, HIV, recurrent thromboembolic disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medication

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Anticoagulation / CCBs / Vasodilators (e.g. sildenafil) / Prostacyclin analogs (e.g. Epoprostenol/Flolan) / Endothelin antagonists (e.g. Bosantan) / Diuretics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Need for invasive monitoring, optimized analgesia & post op disposition

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Ensure patient is OPTIMIZED - Resp, Cardio, alternatives to OR (medical management etc.)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid increases in PVR (minimize pain, sympathetic stimulation, hypoxia, hypercarbia, acidosis, optimize airway pressures  Conflict with hypoxia/hypercarbia vs. PPV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize RV function (careful fluid administration, maintain RV perfusion (afterload)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Be mindful of ventricular interdependence

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Fatique, functional capacity, ischemia, RHF, presyncope/syncope, orthopnea/PND, cyanosis, hemoptysis. Underlying etiology, medications, investigations/ECHO.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: pHTN: large A wave, Loud P2, RV heave, TR (high pitched pansystolic mumur @ 4 th  intercostal space in the parasternal region), dec. CO, S3/S4, JVD, hepatomegaly, ascites, dependent edema Investigations: CBC (polycythemia), elect, coags if on AC's, ABG, ECG - RVH R/S ratio in V1 and V2 of 1 and S waves >than 3mm in V5 or V6, P pulmonale > 2.5mm II/III/AVF. CXR - globular heart, prom.or engorged pulm. vasculature, chronic lung dx. ECHO-TR/PAP, EF, cardiac size, fnx. VQ scan if thromboembolic disease, PFTs, R sided angio= gold standard, can trial nitric oxide and assess resp. Optimization: Resp consult: Rx resp infections, Rx bronchospasm (bronchodilators, mucolytics, steroids), Inotropes for RVF (dobut/milrin) consider neb 5mg. Ensure optimal preload. Rx: pHTN, heparinize pt if indicated, cont pHTN meds. Must cont. PGI2 infusion (short half-life)3-5 mins, can get rebound htn. Start or cont. chronic therapy for pHTN: Nifedipine 30-240mg PO OD, Diltiazem 120-900mg PO OD, Epoprostenol (PGI2) 2-150ng/kg/min IV or inhaled (60mcg aerosolized?), Sildenafil 50mg PO BID, Bosentan (a dual endothelin receptor antagonist) 125mg bid - S/E: anemia/fluid retention. Home O2, phlebotomy if HCT >50% Anesthetic Opt: Regional preferred (sympathectomy), avoid ketamine ( ↑ PVR), IV anesthetics are safe Room Setup: Pulm vasodilators: NO, NTG, Nirpride, Hydral, Inhaled NO (SE: inhibit plt agg, - inotrope, methHgb), CCB: Nifedipine/Diltiazem, PGE1, prostacycline (PGI2), Adenosine, Ach, Inotropes: Dobutamine (0.1-10mcg/kg/min)/Milrinone/Vasopressin if needing inc. SVR w/o PVR increase. CAS/Invasive lines/PAC/TEE (note PAC risks arrythm/rupture)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Risk of hTN/CVS collapse, avoid ketamine, hyperventilate, ↑ or ↓ TV w/PEEP ↑ PVR. Any tech. is ok, as long as hemodynamic goals me, consider TIVA. Post-op: HDU, consider RVAD for RHF or ECMO if awaiting Tx.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medical, not surgical, emergency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
High risk for aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Metabolic derangement

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypochloremic metabolic Alkalosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hyponatremia & hypokalemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Severe dehydration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of post-operative apnea

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Persistent metabolic alkalosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations of neonate/infant

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimize fluid and acid-base deficits prior to anesthesia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
(Na + >130; K + >3.0; Cl - >90; HCO3<27; U/O 1 cc/kg/hr; normal HR/BP/RR)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prevent aspiration - OG suction prior to induction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ensure adequate postoperative monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Conflict being difficult a/w and RSI

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pyloric Stenosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Initial Goal is to determine the degree of dehydration: <5% - 50cc/kg 5-10% - 100cc/kg >10% - 150cc/kg Hx: 1st born M; 2 nd  - 6 th  wk; projectile nonbilious vomiting (Hx), feeds; Vol. status (tears, diapers, lethargy) PE: VS; Wt; MM; Ant fontanelle; Sunken eyes; Cap refill; Skin Turgor; Activity (lethergy; olive sign Investigations: CBC, electrolytes, BUN, Cr, glucose, ABG, bilirubin unconjugated, U/A; Classic abn: hCl, hNa; hK metabolic alkalosis; HypoK (2' hyperaldosteronism); If severe volume depletion, can have metabolic acidosis (metabolic abn less common now because of earlier presentation); US to confirm Dx.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: May take 12 to 72 Hrs to correct volume and metabolic abn: IV; Use NS in 20 cc/kg boluses to replace deficit and titrate to clinical criteria outlined above and U/O of 1 cc/kg/hr

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Maintenance of D5NS + KCl 20-40 mEq/L at 1 to 1.5x maintenance requirement of 4 cc/kg/hr

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prevention of aspiration: 14F NG suctioned with child in various positions (does not ensure empty stomach); Pre-operative acetaminophen 20-30 mg/kg rectally.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: Generally, GA vs neuraxial anesthesia (SAB: 0.8 mg/kg of bupiv 0.5% vs Caudal: Large doses of 1.6 mL/kg (4 mg/kg) of 0.25% bupivicaine)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: Routine + ER meds (atropine, Sux); CAS + T° probe; Neonatal setup (neonatal circuit, warm room, warming blanket and lights).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: RSI (P 4-6; Sux 2; or Remi 2-4); Continue Maintenance IV; Maintain on Volatile or TIVA; Avoid hyperventilation (worsens resp alkalosis); LA to wound.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Monitored bed for apneas for 12-24 hrs  (inc. risk with metabolic alkalosis); Analgesia: Caudal; Tylenol; Local anesthetic infiltration by surgeon; Postop narcotics are not required

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Fluid, electrolyte & metabolic imbalance uncorrected; Aspiration; Apnea postoperatively

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Restrictive Lung Disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased risk of perioperative respiratory failure, pneumonia, PTX

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Cancel elective procedures if there is an acute + reversible processes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o higher risk if VC < 15 ml/kg, FVC<50% or 500cc, or pCO2>45

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential difficult BMV and rapid desaturation dec. compliance, lower SaO2, dec. FRC

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Respiratory physiologic changes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypoxemia (V/Q mismatch)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Decreased compliance - Inc. Pk Pressures barotrauma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o pHTN and RV dysfunction / cor pulmonale-AVOID INC PVR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Etiology / Co-morbid disease states

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o CTD/ autoimmune disease, IPF, ARDS, Obesity, Neuromuscular, kyphoscoliosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o steroids , immunosuppressives, bleomycin , amiodarone, oxygen

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o May be very sensitive to CNS depressants (opioids)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 degree depends on etiology / inc. dead space ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Preoperative optimization of pulmonary function

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Either minimally invasive (LA or regional) or maximally supportive (slow wean)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Lung protective ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Low VT, inc. RR, inverse ratio, pressure control, PEEP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid precipitants of pHTN

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimal postoperative pain management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 encourage postoperative mobilization

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Etiology of RLD; Severity of RLD and treatments; Dyspnea, exercise tolerance, recent infections, hemoptysis, cough, meds (bleomycin),  (home O2); Smoking; CVS: Angina, CHF, orthopnea, PND; Supine symptoms (mediastinal mass)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: AW; SVC syndrome (facial swelling) ; ↑ WOB ; cyanosis (SpO2<80%, PaO2 <50mmHg), clubbing AE: crackles (fine vs coarse) wheezing ; pHTN - Loud, fixed, widely split S2, palpable P2 ; RVH - RV heave, S4 ; RV failure - JVD, S3, hepatomegaly, ascites, dependent edema; skeletal abnormalities, obesity, abdominal distension causing restrictive lung pattern

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: CBC, lytes, CXR, ABG, EKG (RAE, RVH), PFT (dec VC, TLC, normal FEV1/FVC), consider echo

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Resp consult, treat infection, drain pleural effusion and ascites, diuretics if fluid overloaded, NG to decompress distended abdomen

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
pHTN drug, spirometry, difficult A/W cart b/c risk of difficult BMV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Minimize drugs that depress ventilation; Consider epidural; Avoid N2O (PTX); May need stress dose steroids; PCV - keep PAP < 30 mmHg, inverse ratio, permissive hypercapnea

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Risk of Postoperative pulmonary complications /ventilation; Incentive spirometry; Early ambulation Special: FiO2 to goal O2 sat = 88-92% if history of bleomycin

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Rheumatoid Arthritis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for difficult airway (AAI, limited neck ROM, unstable C-spine )

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multisystem disease including cardiac, pulmonary, renal, hematologic involvement

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o CVS: pancarditis, AI, pericardial effusions, conduction system defects

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Resp: RLD, interstitial fibrosis, pHTN, pleural effusions, nodules

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Renal: CRF

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Chronic anemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Co-existing Diseases

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o SLE, amyloid, IHD, cancer, DM, osteoporosis, PUD, infections

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Corticosteroids, Immunosuppressives: cyclosporine, cyclophosphamide, MTX, NSAIDs, Chronic pain meds

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Technical difficulties with access. patient positioning, & fragile skin

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Assume unstable c-spine unless radiographic evidence to the contrary

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Difficult AW should be anticipated

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Careful positioning and documentation of pre-existing neurologic symptoms

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Multimodal analgesia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Duration of illness (RFs for AA subluxation include male gender, severe arthropathy and longstanding dysphagia, dysphonia, diplopia, neck/arm pain, dizziness, U/E numbness); functional capacity, dyspnea, cough, chest pain;  joints/systems involved; meds/side effects, bruising/bleeding, fatigue; peripheral neuropathies

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Dictated by degree of cardiorespiratory compromise; Ventilation may be required d/t RLD Complications: neurologic deficits, post intubation edema or cricoarytenoid dislocation (stridor) Other manifestations of disease renal dysfunction secondary to vasculitis/GN/infiltrative disorders, pleural effusions, interstitial fibrosis, pulmonary nodules, pulmonary hypertension, heart failure (may be ischemic or infiltrative), pericarditis, pericardial effusions, coronary arteritis, heart block, aortitis, airway involvement (with involvement of cricoarytenoids ), and many other multisystem manifestations disease, neck symptoms, rheum factor positive), A/W - cricoarytenoid arthritis, evidence of AAI (occipital H/A, PE: A/W, neck ROM, mobility of A/W structures, CVS exam (LV dysfunction, effusions, pHTN, valvular Dz); Resp (pulmonary fibrosis, effusions) Neurologic dysfunction; restricted mobility; access options. Investigations: CBC, Lytes, BUN, Cr, Coags, ECG , CXR (if significant pulmonary involvement), ABG +/PFTs, Cspine Flex/Ex views (atlanto-dental interval > 3-4mm is abnormal), MRI of Cspine; ECHO Optimization: Consider Spine consult, ENT for cricoarytenoid arthritis (awake trach) stress dose steroids, Iron +/-EPO pre-op, blood conservation Anesthetic Options: GA or regional may be used. Awake FOB is recommended but any technique that minimizes neck flexion may be appropriate; LMA may be difficult. Neuraxial OK (relative sparing of TL spine). Intraoperative Mgt: AFOB, smaller ETT; Exaggerated hemodynamic responses; Careful positioning; eye drops (Sicca); Aggressive multimodal analgesia. Extubate awake, warm, comfortable, reversed. : Peripheral neuropathies, anemia, thrombocytopenia, bruising/bleeding,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Shared  / unprotected airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
need for good communication with surgeon

<!-- PAGE=? -->
risk of aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anticipated complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
A/W obstruction (supra or infraglottic), injury, or edema

<!-- PAGE=? -->
pneumothorax

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations of jet ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Barotrauma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pulmonary tamponade

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Comorbidities

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Underlying condition - acute/chronic pulmonary problems, cancer - 4M's

<!-- PAGE=? -->
cardiac disease, smoker, EtOH, elderly

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Need for deep plain of anesthesia/muscle relaxation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Good pre-oxygenation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Excellent muscle relaxation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain adequate oxygenation and ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 SV with insufflation vs. paralysis and jet ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Depends on ease of A/W access, intraluminal vs. extraluminal compression

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Rigid Bronchoscopy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Standard history with focus on respiratory, airway concerns, functional capacity; Eaton-lamber assoc'd with lung ca; Positional dyspnea; EtOHism assoc'd with H&N cancers

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Standard cardiopulm exam.  Careful airway exam assessing for upper a/w obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: CBC, ABGs, CXR +/- CT chest, PFTs (don't necessarily need all these test but see if available in chart)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Preop respiratory function (inhalers/nebs is appropriate), +/- antisialogogue

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: Standard monitors, prepare for TIVA, have ETT and appropriate A/W equipment ready, jet ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Good pre-oxygenation, TIVA, SV for FB removal / difficult A/W access, muscle relaxation (sux vs. NdMB), good communication with surgeon, timed ventilation with procedure.  Hyperventilate in preparation for periods of apnea.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Emergence may be stormy with coughing up of secretions or blood.  Usually post-op pain is minimal so only use short-acting opioids during the case.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential complications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypoxemia, Hypercapnia, hemorrhage, Tacheobronchial injury, airway obstruction (bronchospasm, bleeding, tissue, FB), aspiration, dental damage, pneumothorax

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency case

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o unprotected airway/decreased GCS

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o unsecured aneurysm with risk of rupture

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased ICP with the need to maintain CPP while minimizing transmural pressure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Maintain high/normal MAP to prevent critical reductions in CBF

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Avoid / manage inc. ICP (avoiding transmural pressure)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Identify and manage Complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Surgical: Rebleeding, vasospasm, hydrocephalus, seizures

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Medical:  LV dysfunction, neurogenic pulmonary edema, SIADH, cerebral salt wasting

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Fascilitate surgical exposure - Brain relaxation after dural is open

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize O2 delivery & CPP while avoiding intracranial transmural pressure (HTN, rapid dec. in ICP)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o With inc. ICP, conflict between minimizing transmural pressure  (deep induction) and maintaining CPP (hemodynamic support)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid secondary injury - hyperglycemia, hyponatremia, hyperthermia, elevated HOB

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevention of rebleeding (early surgical management) & vasospasm (nimodipine, pravastatin)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Facilitate rapid postoperative neurological assessment

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Grade I - Asymptomatic or minimal headache/ slight nuchal rigidity; Grade II - Mod - severe headache, nuchal rigidity, cranial nerve palsies but not other deficits; Grade III - Drowsiness, mild confusion or mild focal deficit; Grade IV - Stupor, mod-severe hemiparesis, possible early decerebrate rigidity, vegetative; disturbances; Grade V - Deep coma, decerebrate rigidity, moribund appearance

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cerebral Aneurysm & SAH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Focused. Evidence of cardiopulmonary compromise. Timeline of events (rebleed most common in the first 6-12 h). Mechanism (suspicion of aspiration, possible C-spine injury), H&H scale, co-existing aneurysms, co-morbidities that might alter targets for CPP or otherwise complicate management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Vitals including temp, GCS, A/W for ease of intubation, continuous monitoring (arrhythmias), assess extent of inc. ICP, Cardiopulmonary assessment looking for evidence of ventricular dysfunction (S3, S4), pulmonary edema, or suspected aspiration. Focused neuro exam.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: CBC, Lytes (hypoNa), BUN, Cr, glucose, G&S, ABG, ECG (ST changes, canon T waves, prolonged QT, U waves), trops if suspected ischemic changes, CXR, ECHO if suspicious for LV dysfunction Optimization: Aspiration prophylaxis, Goal CPP is 60mmHg (ischemia <50, ARDS >70), euvolemic, minimize inc. ICP (caution droping ICP if unptotected aneurysms) Nimodipine, Pravastatin

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: CAS + 5 lead, Art (don't delay if severe inc. ICP) CVP (triple H therapy - volume status, vasoactive agents), Temp, glucometer, foley, ICP control (mannitol, lasix), titratable vasoactive agents (? Ups, downs, adenosine). Consider STP for burst suppression if rupture, Lumbar drain may be considered. Possible neurophysiologic monitoring (SSEP/EEG)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Imperative to prevent rupture or rebleed during induction. Minimize transmural pressure during stimulating parts of procedure (lido/prop/remi for intubation) TIVA for maintanence (brain relaxation), consider inc. MAP by 15% during temporary clipping, Crisp emergence - avoid coughing

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Hypertension +/- bradycardia = rebleed/rupture - therapeutic hypotension (dec. bleeding to allow surgical exposure and control of aneurysm) burst suppression (cerebral ischemia due to clips- reduce CMR), inc. MAP once aneurysm controlled, hydrocephalus, herniation, vasospasm

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: BP control (labetolol, hydralazine, ACE-I), ICU post-op, triple-H therapy (hypertensive, hypervolemic, hemodilution - may result in pulm edema and myocardial ischemia), Dx for delayed awakening = anesthetic, ictal/post-ictal, bleeding, ischemia, metabolic (hypercarbia, hyponatremia, hypoglycemia). CT early.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Sarcoidosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Systemic granulomatous disorder that involves many tissues but has a predilication for intrathoracic lymph nodes and lungs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multisystem granulamotous disease:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CNS: Ocular sarcoidosis may produce uveitis, unilateral facial palsy.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CVS: Conduction defects, dysrhythmias

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Resp: Endobroncial sarcoid, laryngeal sarcoidosis/stenosis, pulmonary fibrosis, pHTN and cor-pulmonale.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Metabolic derrangement: Hypercalcemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Corticosteroids are administered to suppress the manifestation of sarcoid and to treat hypercalcemia - Stress dose steroids.

SBE Prophylaxis

Reglmens for a Dental Procedure

<!-- PAGE=? -->

<!-- PAGE=? -->
"Or other first - or second-generation oral cephalosporin in equivalent adult or pediatric dcsage

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ampicillin

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Sciatic Nerve Block L4-S3

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Indications: For any L limb procedure (may req. saph supplementation), for entire LL with femoral NM Particularily for below knee procedures or for post op pain management. Contraindications: Usual + infection at the site.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Distribution of Anesthesia: Post. Thigh, hamstrings and biceps muscles, complete anesthesia below knee except medial strip of skin (saphenous).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Nerve injury (predisposition for ischemia) avoid tourniquet and epinephrine, hematoma, vascular puncture. LA toxicity, cardiac arrest 0.01%.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Technique: Standard CAS Monitors, 25-27G, 10-15cm Stimuplex, Sciatic nerve passes from pelvis through the sacrosciatic foramen below piriformis.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Classic approach of Labat: Pt is lateral with operative side up, knee flexed 90 degrees. Line connecting PSIS to greater trochanter, a perpendicular line is then drawn bisecting this line and extending 5 cm caudad. Another line is drawn from the greater trochanter to sacral hiatus. (Note Winnie approach is 1cm below SH). Insert need to a depth of 5-8 cm (gluteus muscle twitches disappear). Hamstring twitches, dorsiflexion or plantar flexin are acceptale. At 0.2-0.4mA use 20-30ml of LA.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anterior Approach Classic: Inguinal ligament divided into 3 parts. Transtrochanteric line parallel to Inguinal ligament (Start at greater trochanter and draw parallel to IL). Then draw a line perpendicular to both the inguinal ligament and the TT line at the point where the medial third of the ligament meets the middle third. Use a 15cm long insulated needle and start at 1.5-2mA. Advance need perpendicularly. If the femur is contact, reinsert slightly medially and advance 4-5cm deeper. May rotate the leg internally to help. Or start 1-2 cm medial and aim lateral.  - hamstrings not acceptable with ant. approach

<!-- PAGE=? -->
When using tourniquet epinephrine should not be used due to risk of ischemia!

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anterior approach of Raj: Line drawn bw greater trochanter and ischial tuberosity Site of introduction of needle is Midway bw these two points.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ra'ch

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Scleroderma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Difficult airway (microstomia, ↓ neck mobility, bleeding from nasal & oral telangiectasiae) and high risk of aspiration (esophageal dysmotility with ↓ LES tone)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multi-organ Dysfunction (d/t fibrosis):

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o CVS: pancarditis, LV failure, pericardial fluid, conduction disease, HTN, ischemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Resp: RLD (pulmonary fibrosis), pHTN, cor pulmonale and RVF

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Renal failure & -renal crisis‖: accelerated HTN, ARF, hemolytic anemia; ensure ACEi

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypothyroidism

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Peripheral vasoconstriction with hypovolemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Avoid hypothermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Difficult vascular access / positioning / monitoring (dermal thickening, calcification, contractures)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Myopathy (sensitivity to NMBs)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications: immunosuppressives, steroids, vasodilators (ACEi), pulmonary vasodilators

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Anticipate difficult airway and prevent aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Difficult airway vs aspiration risk

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o RSI in patient with limited reserve

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid increases in PVR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Difficult ventilation (RLD) vs. need to avoid inc. PVR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevention of hemodynamic instability with volume resuscitation and titrated anesthetic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevention of vasoconstriction episodes by avoiding hypothermia and other precipitants

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Possible CI to radial art line in patient with significant cardioresp disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Functional capacity. Symptoms of reflux, swallowing problems, biventricular failure (edema, coagulopathies, RUQ pain, PND, orthopnea...), arrhythmias (syncope, palpitations...); Dyspnea, no-productive cough neuropathy; Prior anesthetic history with focus on airway (nose bleeds), access. Medications including steroids last 6 months, cyclosporine (renal tox), cycophosphamide (lung/renal tox) PE: Vitals, with postural BP, volumestatus; Airway, access, extent of contractures, reynaud's, cardiorespiratory exam (looking for evidence again of restrictive lung disease, CHF, pHTN and cor pulmonale - peripheral edema, hepatomegaly, ↑ JVP, +ve HJR, HSM, loud P2, RV heave, pericarditis - rubs, pulsus paradoxus) Investigations: CBC, Lytes, Bun, Cr, LFTs, Coags (malabsorption), ABG, CXR (falure), ECG (conduction Dz, RVF, pHTN, pericarditis), PFTs, ECHO Optimization: Consult Rheum, Resp (possibly pHTN specialist), Cardio, Nephro. Trial pulmonary vasodilators. Treat reversible pulmonary disease (eg pulmonary edema, infection…). Aspiration prophylaxis Anesthetic Options: Regional preferred if possible - epi free local, avoid respiratory muscle block, assess coagulation. If GA then RSI vs FOB, avoid nasal d/t bleeding, difficult surgical A/W Room Setup: Dependent on extent of organ dysfunction. CAS monitors + 5 lead. Consideration of pre-induction A line despite risks. CVP, PAC, TEE depending on extent of pHTN, RV dysfunction; Pulmonary vasodilators and wide selective of resuscitative drugs should be available (including vasopressors and inotropes). If inhaled nitric oxide or Flolan are considered then specialized equipment will be required. Difficult airway cart. Consider ICU ventilator; Warm room (21'C) & fluid Intraoperative Mgt: Need to identify goals (avoid inc. pHTN); Volume resuscitate; caution with NdMB; Aggressive multimodal analgesia (may be sensitive to CNS and resp depressants). May require post-op vent. Post-op: Determined by cardiopulmonary involvement - HDU Complications: Difficult A/W, hypoxemia, Hemodynamic collapse on induction (hypovolemia, cardiac dysfunction)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Scoliosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Etiology: idiopathic vs. non-idiopathic (neuromuscular Dz, congenital abnormalities)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Restrictive Lung Disease:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
pHTN with cor pulmonale; postop resp failure; prolonged ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cardiovascular abnormalities:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CHD; cardiac conditions associated with NM disease etc

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Surgical Consideration:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
blood loss; hypothermia; AW edema; Prone/Lat; OLV if Thoracic approach

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Spinal cord integrety: wake-up test / SSEP / MEP's

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op pain control - clonidine, gabapentin, ketamine, opioids

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid exacerbations of pHTN (hypoxemia, hypercarbia, acidosis, hypothermia, light anesthesia & pain)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Balance perfusion pressure to spinal cord vs. need for mild hypotension to minimize blood loss

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Manage anesthetic agents to allow adequate monitoring of spinal cord integrity (SSEPs / MEPs)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Vigilance for life threatening complications of VAE or major vascular injury (aortic, vena caval or iliac vessel)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize for postoperative wean from ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Scoliosis hx (extent of disease, etiology): functional capacity, recurrent infections; CHD, NM disease, CTD, preexisting CNS deficits; Nutritional status; Surgical Plan - Approach & monitoring to be employed PE: Vitals, airway, CV/Resp exam , RVH & cor pulmonale (increased JVP, peripheral edema, hepatomegaly, +HJR, RV heave, loud P2, wide split S2, unexpected murmurs, cyanosis, clubbing), Neuro deficits, scoliosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: CBC, G&S, Coags, ABGs if RLD, CXR for chronic lung disease, spinal xray, ECG, +/- echo if applicable, PFTs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Preop Hgb optimization, Respiratory health optimal, Preop Clonidine (3ug/kg) and Gabapentin (10mg/kg)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: CAS monitors, 5 lead ECG, a-line, good IV access, fluid warmers, forced air warmer, emergency drugs, TIVA infusions, TXA, SLETT vs DLETT, monitor for VAE (Doppler, TEE) Intraoperative Mgt: Induction with hemodynamic goals in mind, short-acting NdMBs, Maintenance MEPs  no muscle relaxation, SSEP  TIVA or low-dose volatile, prepared for prone or lateral position, TXA (100mg/kg bolus and 10mg/kg/hr) adequate analgesia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Possible ICU, post-op vent - depends on pre-op cardiorespiratory reserve, intra-op events, length of procedure, adequacy of analegesia, temperature, a/w edema, etc.: pulmonary function is expected to worsen in first 7-10 days

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Special: Complications: intra-op blood loss, neuro deficit (stop surgery, ensure adequate oxygenation/ventilation, raise BP to above preop, check Hg, r/o surgical causes), VAE, vascular injury, post-op resp failure (RF: VC <40%)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Seizures

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Paroxysmal discharges from abnormally excited neuronal foci, which can be generally classified as: PARTIAL (simple vs. complex) or GENERALIZED (convulsive vs non-convulsive)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Underlying etiology of Seizure : Drugs, Infetion, Metabolic, Structural - Raised ICP, Trauma: (hypoglycemia/hyponatremia/hypocalcemia/hypomagnesemia), Withdrawl

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Perioperative mangagement of medications / interactions:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Continue anti-epileptic medications peri-op

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 NdMB resistance due to enzyme inducers (phenytoin, carbemazepine, phenobarbitol), p450 upregulation.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of perioperative seizures : Avoid medications that exacerbate/precipitate seizure (Methohexital, ketamine, Cis/atratcurium, enflurane, demerol)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of Aspiration with Seizure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain a physiological pharmacologic and metabolic milieu to minimize risk of perioperative risk of seizure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: AMPLE, seizure history, etiology, type, Hz, duration, medications / doses / side effects, recent serum levels.  Etiology: DIMS PE: Vitals, gingival hyperplasia (dilantin), airway exam, LOC if recent seizure, neuro exam, signs of liver failure, bruising etc, evidence of aspiration pneumonia. Investigations: Usual b/w, toxicology screen, glucose, tsh, consider antiepileptic serum levels, CT-head, CXR for aspiration. Optimization: Neurology consult for uncontrolled or new onset seizures, ensure patient continues antiepileptic medications perioperatively. Correct metabolic derangements. Consider benzodiazepine premedication. Anesthetic options: Regional or GA, possibly lower seizure threshold with LA toxicity, avoid ketamine , cisatracurium/atracurium/enflurane/meperdine etc. Avoid regional in post-ictal. Room Setup: Usual setup Intraoperative Mgt: Ideally Propofol or STP induction, consider benzo, may require higher doses of NMDR due to increased metabolism. Emergence = highest time for seizure. Complications: Seizure Management: ABC, 100% O2, BM ventilation, Vitals, Rapid glucometer, lorazepam 0.1mg/kg or midazolam in 0.5-1mg doses, STP 25-50mg, Propofol 25-50mg doses. If sz does not break >> GA doses, Phenytoin 20mg/kg IV load slowly, Phenobarb 20mg/kg IV, intubate, treat underlying cause. Consider ICP management!! Hyperventilate, Mannitol/Decadron/elevate HOB, Phenobarb - Agranulocytosis, Hepatic Toxicity, SJS. Phenytoin - Gingival hyperplasia, ataxia,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Special: anemia, angranul, SJS, hepatotoxicity. Carbamazepine - Neutropenia, agranulocytosis, hepatotoxicity. Clonazepam- Thrombocytopenia, Valproic Acid - Agranulocytosis, hepatotoxicity, pancreatitis.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DDx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hypoxemia / Hypercapnia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Drugs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Infections

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Encephalitis, Meningitis, abscess, Sepsis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Metabolic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypoxia / hypercarbia, Hypo/hyperglycemia , myxedema coma, adrenal insufficiency, Electrolytes (hypo/hypernatremia, hypercalcemia), Toxins (Uremia, hepatic encephalopathy)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Structural

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o TBI, CVA, ICH, Tumor

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Pyrexia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Obstetrical Seizure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Eclampsia, Drug withdrawal/intoxication (cocaine), ICH (hypertension), Epilepsy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pediatric Seizure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Febrile/meningitis/infection, Ingestion, Hypoxemia, Epilepsy, TBI (trauma/abuse), Metabolic (DKA, hypoglycemia)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Seizure during Regional

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hypoxia/hypercapnia, LA toxicity (intravascular injection), High spinal, Epilepsy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Seizures: Emergency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Emergency Situation - Prevent injury, call for help and inform surgeon

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Scan monitors for HR, Rhythm, EtCO2, SaO2, and cycle BP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hand ventilate with 100% O2 - DO NOT hyperventilate→ ↓ seizure threshold

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Anticonvulsants

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Propofol 20-30mg (Thiopental 25-50mg) titrated to effect

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Midazolam 0.5mg titrated to effect

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 If no resolution and difficult ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o NdMR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Higher doses of sedatives

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Anticonvulsants

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Phenytoin 10mg/kg IV load -  slowly

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Phenobarbital 1-2mg/kg

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Investigate etiology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Blood glucose, Electrolytes, Toxicology screen

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Focused neurological exam

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Infection, trauma, ↑ ICP, drug reaction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Consult Neurology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Pregnancy - MgSO4 6 g IV bolus over 15 minutes, then 1 - 2 g/hr

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 ↑ ICP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Maintain low normal pCO2, Mannitol 1g/kg bolus, Dexamethasone 10-20mg bolus, Lasix 10-20mg bolus, HOB > 30°

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Septic Shock

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Critically ill patient with high mortality

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Distributive shock with severe relative hypovolemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Early goal directed therapy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Potential for cardiovascular collapse on induction of anesthesia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Need for critical care monitoring/ICU post-operatively

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multi-organ failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 ARDS, ARF, DIC

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Systemic Infection

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Early treatment with antibiotics, source control

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Early goal-directed therapy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Early Abx - meropenum / Vanco

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Fluid resuscitation and inotropes/vasopressors titrated to MAP > 65, CVP > 8-12 & SvO2 > 70

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Peds - fluid titrated as 20ml/kg, monitor cap refill, BP less useful monitor, dopamine is 1 st  line

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Parturient - FHR as resuscitative end point

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Urgent source control

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Parturient Conflicts - HD instability vs. fetal distress/Stat GA, neuroaxial vs. bacteremia/HD instability

<!-- PAGE=? -->
SIRS: Two or more of the following Temp <36, >38; HR > 90; RR > 20; WBC >12, <4, or 10% bands Hx&Px: Comfirm Dx - distributive vs. cardiogenic vs. hypovolemic; R/O other etiology - Pancreatitis, anaphylaxis, drug ingestions, transfusion Rx, myxedema coma, adrenal crisis; Source of Sepsis - CNS (GCS, pupils, focal findings, meningismus), Resp (WOB, Sputum, auscultation), CVS (murmurs, CVLs, endocarditis Septic emboli), Abd (jaundice, acute tenderness, ischemic gut), GU (flank pain, dec U/O, positive U/A, foley) Derm (cellulitis, abscess), Pregnancy (Chorioamnionitis, PROM) ; Identify end-organ dysfunction - LOC, resp failure, decreased peripheral perfusion, ARF; Vitals with postural & temp; assess volume status; IV access Inv: CBC + diff, plt, lytes, Ur, Cr, Glu; INR/PTT; Bld cultures; group & screen; ABG, lactate, LFTs, amylase; CXR; sputum; ECG; +/-ECHO (TTE vs TEE) Optimization: Consult ICU; Goal directed therapy - Monitored bed, Addequate IV access, Arterial Line, CVC (IJ or SC); O2 +/- ETT with PPV (dec. WOB / VO2); fluid to keep CVP 8-12; Vasopressers to keep MAP > 65; SvO2 >70% - PRBC to Hct >30%, Dobutamine 2.5ug/kg/min; Early Abx (Meropenum 1gm IV q8h, Vanco 1g IV q12h); Surgery for source control (minimal delay); Consider Steroids if refractory shock; APC if APACHE >24 (stop 2 hrs preoperatively, re-start 12 hrs post); Glycemic control; Early entral feeding; DVT & stress ulcer prophylaxis GA; neuroaxial relatively contraindicated (infection, unfavorable hemodynamics, altered coagulation)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Options: Setup: CAS 5 lead +temp, A-line, CVC; adequate IV access; inotropes, infusions; bld products

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Management: Aspiration risk; avoid Sux with prolonged immobility / intra-abdominal sepsis; HD stable induction (titrated, ketamine, minimize propofol, avoid etomidate); lung protective vent (Vt 6 mls, Ppl <30, permissive hypercapnia, PEEP titrated to PaO2 >60), Remember goals of resuscitation Disposition: leave intubated; transport to ICU

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Serotonin Syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
A potentially life-threatening adverse drug reaction with typical symptoms including agitation, delirium, autonomic hyperactivity, hyperreflexia, clonus, and hyperthermia.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multisystem effects of serotonin excess:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CNS: seizure, altered LOC; CVS: Tachycardia and HTN, autonomic instability, arrhythmia; MSK: rigidity, rhabdomyolysis, hyperkalemia and renal failure; Hyperthermia; DIC

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid drugs that will precipitate Serotonin Syndrome in patients taking MAO inhibitors

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Demerol, Fentanyl, Ondansetron, Metoclopramide, SSRI's & TCA's

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Management strategies:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Cyproheptadine (5-HT antagonist), Benzodiazepines for rigidity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hemodynamic support - may be altered and exaggerated responses to indirect acting sympathomimetics (avoid ephedrine and dopamine)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Psychiatric Patient - Co-operation, Informed consent / Substitute Decision Maker

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Stop offending medications and provide supportive care

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Aggressive cooling, antipyretics, NdMBs or benzodiazepines for rigidity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o 5-HT receptor antagonists (b-blockers, cyproheptadine)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid drugs which may exacerbate serotonin syndrome: meperdine, ?fentanyl ?ondansetron/maxeran

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Rule out high risk conditions on differential diagnosis (MH, NMS, thyrotoxicosis)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Detailed hx to reveal concomitant use of psychotropic meds, new meds, neuroleptics (need to r/o NMS). Symptoms: confusion, agitation, sz's, coma, mydriasis (miosis in NMS), shivering, flushing, hyperthermia, muscle rigidity, myoclonus, hyperreflexia, autonomic instability, GI symptoms (rare in NMS); rarely rhabdo

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: Vitals (orthostatic, temp) volume status, autonomic instability, CNS changes, muscle tone, reflexes, myoclonus, resp compromise/failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: Goal to narrow DDx - CBC, lytes, Creatinine, CK, Coags, pan-culture, tox screen, ECG, +/CXR, AXR to r/o secretory tumours.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Psych and ICU consult, delay elective surgery, discontinue serotonergic meds, activ'd charcoal if recent ingestion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Supportive Care: ABCs, intubation if appropriate; antipyretics, cooling, sedation, paralysis for hyperthermia; benzos for myoclonus, rigidity & agitation, consider phenytoin; NdMBs if benzos ineffective for rigidity; Bblockers (propranolol, esmolol) for 5-HT antagonism, HTN - sedation +/- SNP, hTN - volume +/- NE, phenyl, epi; cyproheptadine for severe symptoms - 12mg NG load then 2mg q2h until symptoms resolve

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup :  Standard CAS + a-line, CVP.  Avoid meperidine, dextromethorphan, tramadol, ?fentanyl, ?ondasetron, maxeran.  Have vasopressors, vasodilators available.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: Likely ICU setting.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
SIADH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hyponatremia, elevated urine osmolality, excessive urine sodium excretion, and decreased serum osmolality

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Etiology or Co-existing disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Tumor - lung, pancreas, prostate, lymphoma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CNS - trauma, SAH, tumor, infection

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pulmonary (infection, CF), Drugs (opiatesm oxytocin, chlorpropamide, vincristine), Pain, idiopathic, iatrogenic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hyponatremia and volume status - potential for volume overload

<!-- PAGE=? -->
cerebral edema, seizures, coma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications associated with treatment

<!-- PAGE=? -->
central pontine myelinolysis from overly rapid correction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DI from demeclocylcine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DDx of hyponatremia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypovolemic - CSWS, Diuretics, Addison's, nephritis, RTA, Metabolic Alkalosis, vomiting, diarrhea, burns, pancreatits, trauma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Euvolemic - adrenal insufficiency, hypothyroidism, Drugs, SIADH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypervolemic - ARF, CRF, nephrotic syndrome, CHF, cirrhosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain hemodynamic stability, fluid and electrolyte balance

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Correct underlying reversible etiologies (infection, tumour, medications, iatrogenic)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid overcorrection or overly rapid correction resulting in CPM

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: surgical history (NueroSx), symptoms of hyponatremia/cerebral edema (lethargy, weakness, confusion, altered reflexes, Seizures, coma), urinary frequency & amount

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: vitals, Volume status (possible overload), Resp for edema, Neuro - areflexia, dec.LOC, pseudobalbar palsy, asterixis, muscle weakness

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: Lytes, BUN, creatinine, and glc. Look for low osmolality (<280 mOsm/kg), elevated UNa (>20 mmol/L) & Uosm >100 mOsm/L; CXR for edema, CT head - edema, hemorrhage

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Correct symptomatic hyponatremia until asymptomatic, usually 120mmol/L, rate of 1-2mEq/L/h (3% NaCl 1-2ml/kg/hr); asymptomatic 0.5mEq/L/h; with true volume depletion, serum Na will inc. ~ 1mEq/L per liter of 0.9% NaCl infused - once ADH is turned off, serum Na may rapidly correct, may need DDAVP to slow correction; Inc in  Serum Na = (infusate [Na] - serum Na) / (TBW+1), Na deficit = TBW x (140-[Na]); eliminate precipitating cause, free water restriction is mainstay of SIADH treatment (500-1000ml/d), Demeclocycline (300-600mg/d) to induce reversible nephrogenic DI, sufficient to decrease TBW by 0.5-1.0 L/day

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: All feasible - assess Neurologic status

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CAS + 5 lead, Art line for serum Na levels, CVP for volume, foley

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Avoid drugs known to lower seizure threshold, avoid hypotonic fluids, minimize stress response - ADH secretion, avoid drugs that induce ADH release - morphine, barbiturates, Beta agonists Post-op: Monitor urine output, serum Na, Fluid restriction 500-1000 mL/d, differentiate SIADH from cerebral salt wasting in the neurosurgical population (CSWS is associated with volume depletion, SIADH is eu/hypervolemic)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Central pontine myelinolysis - S/S = quadriplegia, seizures, coma, and death; RF include ETOH, liver Dz, malnutrition, hypoK, burns, premenopausal women, severe chronic hyponatremia, onset may be delayed 1-2 days after correction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Chronic hemolytic anemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
chronic transfusion (Hct>30%), difficult Cx match , risk of hemolytic transfusion reactions from allo-immunization

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multisystem disease with end-organ dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CNS Stroke

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pulomnary - acute chest syndrome, recurrent pneumonia, possible RLD from pulm infarct -pHTN and RVF

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CVS - LVH from chronic anemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Other CRF , Splenic infarct (may be asplenic and immunocomp), Iron overload

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for peri-operative exacerbations of vaso-occlusive crises

<!-- PAGE=? -->
acute pain crisis, acute chest syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Chronic pain and opioid tolerance

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Pre-operative optimization (consult hematology, consider hydroxyurea (increases [HbF]), consider prophylactic blood transfusion)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid precipitants of crisis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypoxia; Hypovolemia, Hyperviscosity, dehydration, Acidosis, Hypothermia, Infection, stasis, EtOH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Ensure good perioperative pain control

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Sickle Cell Disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx : Exacerbations/Triggers (hospitalizations, frequency); extent of end-organ damage (primarily pain, CVA, CHF, pHTN, RVF, RLD, hypoxemia, bronchospasm, CRF, priapism, cholelithiasis, liver infarcts, hemolytic or aplastic anemia, splenic infacts, hemosiderosis, chronic infection) ; predictors of post-operative complications - Inc. age, complications (lung disease), hospitalization, abnormal CXR, African haplotype, pregnancy, infection, type of Sx (Chole=D&C=C/S or Hyster > AbdSx > myringotomy > HipSx) PE: Vitals with RA SaO2 ; wheeze, crackles; Vol status, LVF, pHTN/RVF; neuro deficits; Investigations: CBC, Lytes, Ur, Cr, Coags, Hb electrophoresis, CXR +/-ABG, ECG +/- ECHO, +/- CT head Optimization: Heme Consult; Hydroxyurea (inc. HbF); Euvolemia; Bld Tx for high risk procedures (Hg>100); Avoid resp depressants; Cancel elective (acute crisis); Delay urgent (to optimize Hb > 100) Anesthetic Options: GA; RA ok; TEA beneficial for pain mgmt; Tourniquet use Ok Room Setup: CAS + 5 lead; T probe; Invasive monitoring Intraoperative Mgt: Standard; Follow above mentioned Goals Complications: Acute vaso-occlusive crisis - PAIN (ppt by cold, dehydration, stress, menses, EtOH, OSA; pain is typical feature, associated with fever, swelling, N&V; Rx: tylenol, NSAIDS, PCA opiods, hydration, temp management); Acute chest syndrome (2' to vaso-oclusion, infaction, pneumonia; new lobar infiltrate, fever, inc. WOB, chest pain 2-3 days postop; Rx: as per pneumonia: pulm toilet, mobilization, analgesia, incentive spirometry, physio, Ventolin, steroids, Abx, Bld Tx); Aplastic crisis ; Splenic Sequestration (rapid RBC trapping & fall of Hct, and hypovolemia/shock, LUQ pain; Rx: volume and pRBC, delayed splenectomy); RUQ Syndrome (hepatic ischemia, fever, jaundice, liver failure; Rx: fluids, analgesic, Bld Tx) Cholecystectomy - most common procedure, high risk, laparoscopy is OK Obstetrics - inc. risk of SA, prematurity, previa, abruption, PP infection: inc. pain crisis in 3 rd  tri - no effect on UBF/fetus, Maternal mortality ~1%, Fetal mortality as high as 20%, keep Hg > 80 for Vag & 100 for C/S.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Spinal Stenosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Geriatric patients (potential for multiple co-morbid illnesses and altered pharmacology and physiology)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Chronic pain with potential concomitant behavioural and psychiatric limitations and drug tolerance

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Need for multimodal approach for pain management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Surgical consideration for spine surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prone position

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Blood loss and conservation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Fluid shift

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post op pain

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential neurological monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Lack of good evidence around standards for diagnostic, pharmacological and surgical modalities

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Careful surgical candidates selection

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize co-morbid illness

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Obtain thorough history and physical and exclude other potential DDx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Ao aneurysm, vascular claudication, PMR, pyelo, herniated disc, osteoporosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Key distinguishing feature is intermittent neurogenic cauldication

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Induced by standing or walking with erect posture

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Document pre-op neurological deficits

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Multimodal pain management - activity modification, passive ROM, PT, gabapentin, NSAIDs, opioids, epidural steroids, surgical decompression

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Indications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 May help some patients with back and leg pain (first line is still ice, NSAIDs, rest  exercise)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Reserved for patients with symptoms of radiculopathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Pain that persists more than 4-6 weeks, sciatica and spinal stenosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Epidural steroid injection should be reserved for patients with symptoms of radiculopathy (disc herniation or spinal stenosis with evidence of nerve root impingement)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Radicular symptoms may be secondary to nerve root inflammation and edema, release of arachadonic acid metabolites, neuropeptides such as substance P, VIP, and CGRP released from the nucleus pulposus through the annulus.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Contraindications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Ongoing use of anticoagulant medications, local infection, discitis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prominent motor deficit or paresis suggestive of severe root or cauda equine compression (bowel & bladder dysfunction)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Failure of previous injections

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Imaging studies demonstrating severe spinal stenosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Technique:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Epidural steroid injections have been traditionally given through either a caudal or interlaminar route; transforaminal route effective if experienced

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Volume used varies:  5-10ml recommended at the lumbar level ,  3-6mls at C-spine.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Epidural Steroid Injections

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Fluoroscopy is recommended in the following:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o post-laminectomy patients, obese patients, cervical epidural steroid injections, patients who don't respond to the first injection.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Incorrect needle placement occurs in 20-38% of caudal and 30% of translaminar injections

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 The transforaminal approach is especially beneficial in post-laminectomy patients where the drug may not reach the level of pathology due to scarring from previous surgery.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Injectate - Lidocaine 20-30mg

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Triamcinolone most common (40-80mg), or methylpred 80mg

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 methylprednisolone is not recommended in cervical transforaminal injections because it precipatates and the precipitant may be unintentionally injected into the verterbral artery.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Chase with 2cc NS - avoid seeding the tract with steroid

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Repeat every 2-3 weeks for total of 3 injections

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 PDPH (1-5%), hematoma, increased radicular symptoms (1%), Infection, unintentional subarachnoid injection, intraneural injection

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Outcomes:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Few well controlled studies but reasonable alternative to risks/costs of surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Most reliable studies suggest that injections provide significant benefits to some patients with primarily radicular symptoms but the benefit is of limited duration (2-3months)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Transforaminal injections seem to have predictive value in deciding whether a patient might benefit from surgery.
