<!-- PAGE=? -->
Indications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Sympathetically mediated pain (CRPS, PHN, phantom limb, HSV, reimplantation pain)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Circulatory insufficiency - postembolectomy vasospasm, Raynaud's, Scleroderma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Long QT syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Contraindications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 General: Infection, Coagulopathy, lack of consent, allergy, lack of resuscitation equipment or skill

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Specific: Contra-lateral recurrent nerve injury, severe lung disease (FEV1 < 1L)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Equipment:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Routine monitors, trained assistant, resuscitation equipment, 1.5 inch 25 gauge needle

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Technique:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Place patient's head midline with neck slightly extended. Skin is prepped with antiseptic and the skin injected with local. The C6 transverse process is palpated and the carotid is retracted laterally. Needle is inserted to bone (1-2cm), withdraw slightly and inject 0.5-1 cc of local injected as test dose. The needle is advanced to bone again, retracted slightly again and then further local to a total of 8-10 cc is injected (use Marcaine 0.25% without epi)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Successful Block:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Horner's, ipsilateral nasal congestion & conjunctiva flushing, vasodialated and warm extremity

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Direct trauma: pneumo, esophageal perforation, carotid or IJ puncture;

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Local anesthetic effects: inadvertent epidural, brachial plexus, intrathecal, intravenous or verterbral artery injection with associated seizures, bradycardia, RLN (60%) or phrenic nerve paralysis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Stellate Ganglion Block

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential difficult airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Deforming arthritis, Cricoarytenoid arthritis, RLN palsy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Systemic Complications of SLE

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o CNS - seizure, stroke, mood, organic disease, transverse myelitis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Cardiac Myocarditis (conduction dz, CHF), Pericarditis (effusions), Non- infectious Endocarditis (AI, MR), Accelerated CAD ,  HTN/pHTN

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Respiratory RLD (ILD, pleuritis, effusions), pHTN/RVF ,infection, pulm hemorrhage

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hematologic - hypercoagulable (APA), anemia, thrombocytopenia, abnormal bleeding

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Other - CRF, Nephritic, Nephrotic, vasculitis, arthritis, immobility

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications related to medical management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Steroids (cushings, hyperglycemia, adrenal suppression), Immunosuppressants / antimalarials, NSAIDs, Anticoagulants , ASA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for exacerbation of SLE with surgery, stress, infection and pregnancy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
SLE and Pregnancy:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Increased risk of pre-term, IUGR, PIH, possible contraindications to neuoaxial, risk of neonatal lupus and Anti-Ro mediated congential heart block

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Potentially challenging airway and myocardial dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Coagulation defects / thromboembolism and neuraxial techniques

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid drugs that exacerbate Lupus - Procainamide, Phenytoin, Hydralazine, Penicilline, Isoniazid, Enalapril, Captopril, Clonidine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Systemic Lupus Erythematosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Investigate for end-organ dysfunction as above, in particular renal failure, cardio-respiratory involvement, previous endocarditis (consider prophylaxis), arthritis, thrombo-embolic complications and medical therapy. PE: Detailed A/W exam, Neck & TMJ ROM, laryngeal function, hoarsness, detailed cardioresp exam for effusions, tamponade (rare), valvular pathology, CHF, Document preexiciting neuropathies Investigations: CBC (anemia, thrombocytopenia), E7 (renal dysfun), ECG (conduction Dz, LVH, pHTN); Coags, X-match may have Ab's, Anti-phosholipid Ag/ Lupus Anticoagulant/Anticardiolipin, +/- factor assay if prolonged PTT, LFTs (hepatitis); CXR (CHF, effusions, infiltrates); PFTs (restrictive), Echo (LV/RV dysfunction, valvular dysfunction)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Heme/Rheum/Obs consults; Stress Dose Steroids; SBE prophylaxis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Options: Neuroaxial may be contraindicated (thrombocytopenia, prolonged PTT - not a contraindication if d/t AntiPh Antibody, is a contraindication if d/t factor deficiency)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: Based on end-organ dysfunction; Consider TEA if appropriate with lung disease; Consider smaller ETT if cricoartenyoid arthritis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Depends on underlying organ dysfunction ; Safe and controlled management of potentially difficult airway; Consider potential for myocardial dysfunction on induction; If on cyclophosphamide - prolonged response to SCh and mivacurium due to inhibition of plasma cholinesterase; If renal insufficiency present, avoid renally excreted drugs and renal toxins

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergence: Fully reversed, AWaC, May require prolonged ventilation if severe respiratory dysfunction Post-op: Beware of post-op stridor (steroids), thromboembolic events, CHF & arrhythmias, renal insufficiency, adrenal insufficency, coagulopathy and hemorrhage, seizures, CNS dysfunction, fulminant hepatitis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Tachycardia: Emergency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Most important question is sinus tachycardia or not?

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Sinus Tachycardia DDx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypoxia / hypercarbia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Drugs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 administration  chronotropes, cocaine, MAOI, stimulants

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 withdrawal  opioid, BDZ, EtOH, clonidine,  -blocker

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pain or light anesthesia - surgical or non-surgical (full bladder, tourniquet)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Shock  hypovolemia, PTX, pericardial, sepsis, anaphylaxis, anemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Endocrine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 hypoglycemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 hyperthyroidism

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 MH / NMS

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Pheochromocytoma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency Management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Inform surgeon, Scan monitors: rate, rhythm , BP, EtCO2, SaO2

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hand ventilate with 100% O2

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Examine patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 assess pulse

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 auscultate both lungs and examine trachea

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 examine peripherally and forehead for evidence of anaphylaxis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Develop DDx and treat as per ACLS protocol

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Non-Sinus Tachycardia DDx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
SVT: regular

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Afib: irregular

<!-- PAGE=? -->
MAT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
VT / VF

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Non-Sinus Tachycardia Emergency Management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Determine rhythm and treat as per ACLS

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Reason for arrhythmia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 pre-existing

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 ischemia  rate, ACS

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 electrolyte abnormalities

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Tamponade

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency Situation with potential for cardiovascular collapse on induction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pathophysiologic changes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Impaired diastolic filling

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Fixed stroke volume

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Rate dependent CO

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Maximal sympathetic stimulation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Etiologies / co-existing diseases

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Blood: post-cardiac Sx, post-MI, aortic dissection, trauma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Other: infectious, malignant, radiation, SLE, uremia, autoimmune

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 If hemodynamically significant, drain pericardium prior to anesthesia / PPV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid increases in intrathoracic pressure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Maintain spontaneous ventilation, Avoid coughing & straining

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Cardiovascular: fast, full and tight

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Preload: FULL

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Contractility: maintain

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Rate: maintain / possibly increase

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Rhythm: strict NSR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Afterload: maintain

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o MVO2: monitor for ischemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 These patients are maximally sympathetically stimulated

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o You need to replace the sympathetic drive removed by your anesthetic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Determine underlying etiology (dissection, free wall dissection, trauma, post sx, malignancy, autoimmune

<!-- PAGE=? -->
(SLE/RA/Scleroderma), infectious, radiation). Hx of dyspnea, fatique, CHF, hypotension, tachycardia.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Vitals:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
hemodynamically unstable?

<!-- PAGE=? -->
↓

<!-- PAGE=? -->
BP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
↑

<!-- PAGE=? -->
HR, Sx's of CHF. Distant heart sounds, pulsus paradoxus

<!-- PAGE=? -->
(

<!-- PAGE=? -->
↓

<!-- PAGE=? -->
SBP > 10mmHg with inspiration), narrow pulse pressure, possible friction rub. JVD (Note Kussumaul's sign

<!-- PAGE=? -->
- increase in JVP during inspiration (opposite of normal) occurs with constrictive pericarditis, not with

<!-- PAGE=? -->
tamponade!) AI if aortic dissection.  CVP: Elevated CVP, blunted y descent. PAC- diastolic press equalization

<!-- PAGE=? -->
~15-20mmHg, corresponding to pericardial pressure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: CBC/Lytes/Cr (ATN due to shock), INR/PTT, CXR (enlarged cardiac silhouette). ECG: Electrical alternans, low voltage, ST-T elevation, tachycardia. ECHO: visualize effusion, chamber compression, cardiac output, septal shift, chamber volumes.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Large bore IV access, volume resuscitation, pericardial drain, epinephrine infusion, atropine for

<!-- PAGE=? -->
pericardial manipulation. If unable to drain prior to induction, have patient prepped and surgeon in the room.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Local for pericardial drain/window maintains SV, however can lead to coughing,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
straining. GA: controlled airway, allows sternotomy/thoracotomy, however risk of CVS collapse on

<!-- PAGE=? -->
induction/PPV. Early cardioversion for arrhythmias.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: 5lead, invasive lines, TEE/PAC, drugs: Epi/NE, pericardiocentisis drain, chest prepped. Intraoperative Mgt: fluid / PC Drain then GA for definitive Rx. / LA, opioid, small amount of amnestic, +- paralysis / Consider spontaneous breathing induction, can supplement with airway topicalization but do not delay if unstable. Small TV, inc. RR, observe HD goals

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: HDU, observe for recurrence of tamponade. Consider PCA or T Epidural for sternotomy of post-op pain. Complications: Post-tamponade pulm edema: due to increase RV CO, rx w/ NTG, diuretics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
TCA Overdose

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mechanism of action: Stimulation of catecholamine release and block reuptake, Central and peripheral anticholinergic agents, inhibit Na and K channels in brain and heart, Direct alpha blocking

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multisystem effects: Coma, convulsive, cardiac arrythmias and acidosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CNS: depression, possible seizures (persists ~ 24-48 hrs)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ACh side effects: Dry mouth, constipation, urinary retention, vision

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CVS: Postural hypotension, Dose releated prolonged QT and QRS widening (>100msec)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk of ventricular arrhythmias with QT > 0.16 - serial ECGs (persists for 10 days)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medical Management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Gi decontamination - risk of aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Seizures - Diazepam, Sodium bicarbonate (reduce free fraction), Phenytoin

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Dysrhythmias - Alkalization, Lidocaine, Phenytoin (avoid class 1a, amiodarone)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Heart block - Isoproterenol

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypotension - Volume, Sodium bicarbonate, Sympathomimetics, Inotropes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Usual HCO3- is 1-2 MEQ/kg to keep QRS < 100 msecs goal pH 7.5-7.55

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 ECG - Abnormal QRS, prolonged QRS, abnormal size and ration of R and S waves in AVR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 R/O hypoglycemia, conintoxication, bHCG on lab, monitored setting.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DDx hyperthermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Physiologic (e.g. sepsis)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Drugs

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 MH / NMS

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Pheochromocytoma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hyperthyroidism

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Serotenergic syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Anticholinergic syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Transfusion reaction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Stimulants: cocaine, amphetamines

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Endocrine: Hyperthyroidism

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Exogenous

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Warming blankets, heating pads

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Temperature: Emergency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DDx hypothermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased heat loss

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Environmental Exposure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Drugs  vasodilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Alcohol

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Toxins

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Sepsis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Iatrogenic: CPB, CRRT, Cold infusions

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Decreased heat production

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Endocrine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypopituitarism

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypoadrenalism

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypothyroid

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypoglycemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Malnutrition

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Extremes of age

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Impaired shivering (anesthesia)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Impaired regulation: central vs peripheral

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Other

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 sepsis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 pancreatitis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Tetralogy of Fallot

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complex congenital heart disease characterized by VSD, RVOT obstruction, overriding Ao, RVH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Both fixed and dynamic RVOT obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Fixed RVOT obstruction - variable R to L shunt & pulmonary blood flow

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Dynamic RVOT obstruction (infundibular spasm) - inc. R to L shunting & hypoxia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Associated abnormalities and conditions

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o paradoxical embolus - avoid air bubbles in lines

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Thrombophilia 2' to polycythemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o 25% have another congenital abnormality

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Tracheoesophageal fistula and Trisomy 21

<!-- PAGE=? -->
SBE prophylaxis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hemodynamic Goals

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Full preload - Stiff RV, stent open RVOT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Dec. Contractility to reduce dynamic RVOT obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Maintain afterload to minimize R - L shunt and promote pulmonary blood flow

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Avoid inc. PVR - hypoxia, acidosis, aggressive PPV/PEEP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Tet -spell - sudden hypoxia / acidosis 2' to infundibular spasm or dec. SVR - inc. R to L shunt

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o 100% O2 +/- gental PPV, fluid bolus, sedation (dec. SNS), knee chest position (Inc. SVR & preload), phenylephrine 1-2ug/kg, propanolol 10-20 ug/kg (dec. infundibular spasm)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals / Conflicts

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Thoracic Aneurysm

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency Case:  full stomach, HD unstable patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for OLV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for massive blood loss, fluid shifts, transfusion and hypothermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative hemodynamic changes with potential for ischemia - heart, brain, kidneys, and spinal cord

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Special monitoring for SC ischemia (SSEP, MEP) and techniques to optimize SC perfusion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-operative organ dysfunction:  MI, ARF, SC ischemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Co-morbidities: CAD / DM / CKD / HTN / Smoking/Advanced age

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-operative pain

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 maintain stable hemodynamics throughout peri-operative period

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 maintain favourable myocardial oxygen supply / demand relationship

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 watch for evidence of peri-operative organ dysfunction (SC, kidneys)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 peri-operative pain control

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Co-morbidities:  active cardiac conditions (AHA guidelines), acute vs chronic dissection, symptoms PE: Evidence of HF, LV and RV dysfunction, AR, cardiac tamponade (JVD, distant HS, hTN, pulsus paradoxus), carotid bruit, neurologic exam

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: CBC, PTT, INR, X-match, lytes, BUN, EKG, TTE, Consider PFT/CXR, invasive cardiac testing according to AHA, CT/CTA of Aneurysm - review for location, level of cross clamp

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: correct anemia (maintain Hb>9.0 g/dL), avoid tachycardia, optimize volume status, continue beta-blockers, hold ACEI/ARB, hold anticoagulants/antiplatelet agents and bridge if necessary, Consider: cardiology, nephrology consultation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: GA +/- OLV, PCA vs epidural for post-op analgesia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: CAS (5 lead EKG), IV prox'l to XC, pre-induction A-line, CVP, +/- TEE/PAC/DLETT+FOB, fluid warmer, cell saver, blood, SC monitoring (SSEP, MEP)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Induction Titrated (vs. aspiration) if emergency surgery, pt prepped and surgeon in room prior to induction, Maintenance: volatiles readily titrateable, consider effect of epidural on hemodynamics - Prior to cross clamp :avoid over-resuscitation , heparin and mannitol, Cross clamp → Hypertension (inc afterload), NTG and nitroprusside ready, Removal of cross clamp → Hypotension, volume resuscitation prior, dec anesthetic, prepare for metabolic acidosis with reperfusion - hyperventilate, HCO3, staged release of cross clamp will help minimize effects and if unable to control hypotension, surgeon may have to re-apply cross clamp (be ready for rebound hypertension)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Switch DLT to SLT, to CSICU intubated, gradual slow emergence

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Underlying etiology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Malignancy - 4 M's

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o IPF or COPD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Pleural disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Pericardial disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Requires OLV with good lung deflation (unable to CPAP operative lung)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CO2 insufflation of the thorax and its potential complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o dec. pre-load, inc. LV afterload, potential for CO2 embolism, risk of sudden cardiovascular collapse

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Guided by underlying etiology and comorbidities

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Maintain adequate oxygenation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Post-operative Pain Control

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Multimodal, TEA, paravertebral catheters

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Thoracoscopic Surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx and PE and Investigations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Determine severity and complications of underlying disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Screen and assess comorbidities

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Assess ease of intubation and OLV technique

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Assess ability to tolerate OLV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Side of Surgery (right side has 10% more blood flow than left) / Poor PaO2 on Two Lung Ventilation / Pre-operative FEV1 (inverse correlation) / Supine position

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Contraindications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Extensive pleural adhesions, Extensive inflammatory process, Previous pleural fusion, Unresectable lesion, Coagulation defect, Inability to tolerate one-lung ventilation, Severe COPD, Dependence on mechanical ventilation with high peak pulmonary pressures, Hemodynamic instability, Hypovolemic shock, Cardiogenic shock, Ongoing cardiac ischemia, post acute MI

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Standard for Thoracic and OLV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Standard

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Management: GA usually preferred but TEA is possible with local and intercostal nerve blocks Induction dictated by comorbid illnesses; Maintenance as per usual OLV cases.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: multimodal pain management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Related to DLETT / OLV ; Cardiac: HD instability, arrhythmias ; Conversion to Open (25%) ; Persistent Airleak > 5 days (5%) ; -Down Lung‖ syndrome (inc secretions, atelectasis, re-expansion pulm edema, pneumonia) ; Bleeding, infection etc.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prevent Secondary SCI

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Full spinal precautions - imaging can be delayed until after more urgent management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Safe A/W management, Avoid hypoxia and hypotension

<!-- PAGE=? -->
DDx: Neurogenic vs hypovolemic shock: lose ability to ↑ HR in response to hypovolemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Conflict: SCI, Difficult AW,  CHI (↑ICP)vs Uncooperative patient; RSI vs. Aspiration Risk

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Acute Spinal Cord Injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency Trauma with C/T/L-spine injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Full stomach, Hemorrhage & hemodynamic instability, Intoxication, Additional injuries (CHI with inc. ICP in 25%), Hypothermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potentially difficult airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prevention of secondary spinal cord injury (SCI) from hypoxemia or hypotension

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Goal MAP > 80-85, Volume resuscitate, HD support (Dopamine, pressors)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Specific considerations of acute spine injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 C-spine precautions and airway protection - High aspiration risk (loss of cough ability (T2-L1))

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Respiratory insufficiency w/ injury above T7

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Intercostal paralysis (T1-T11), Diaphramatic paralysis (C3-C5), Pulmonary edema

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Severe ANS abnormalities

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Potential for neurogenic shock (hypotension & bradycardia (vasovagal))

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Thermoregulation loss & poikilothermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Hyperkalemia w/ SCh from 24 hrs to 6 months post-injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Spinal shock (1-3 weeks) = flacidity and areflexia (has nothing to do w/ HD stability) Neurogenic shock = sympathectomy w/ PNS dominance; Vasodilation- hypotension responsive to pressors; Bradycardia and loss of baroreceptor reflex arc to hypotension (responsive to atropine)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ATLS approach : 1' (ABCDE) then 2' survey (AMPLE + head to toe exam)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
AMPLE; Old charts; MOI; Associated injuries; Intoxication; Resus Hx; Comorbid Disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Vitals (HR, BP); C-spine precautions; Monitor; Large IVs; ABCDE; Resp function; Neuro exam

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Canadian C-Spine:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
GCS 15 and stable - Age <65, Normal neuro exam, No dangerous mechanism (fall >3ft;

<!-- PAGE=? -->
MVC >100km/hr, roll-over, ejection, ATV, bicycle; axial load) - low-risk factors present (simple rear-end, sitting

<!-- PAGE=? -->
position, ambulatory, delayed neck pain, absent midline pain - active rotation OK - No x-ray

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: CBC; Coags; E7; Cx Match; ABG (resp insufficiency), vital capacity - 15mls/kg; Tox screen; CXR; C-spine (C1-T1, boney alignment, cartilage spaces, soft tissue - 10mm at atlas, 4mm C2-C4, 15mm below C4, AbN if >5mm inc); CT Head/Spine; FAST; ECG

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: ATLS; Oxyg/Vent/Volume; maintain MAP> 80mmHg; Asp prophylaxis; Antisialogue (AFOI); Steroids - methylpred 30mg/kg within 8hrs (controversial)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: Usually GA for emergency fixation or decompression CAS + 5lead, temp, A-line, CVC (Chronotropes, pressers); Foley; Warming; ER drugs; Cell

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: saver; prone patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: AFOI if possible (assess CNS); RSI + Inline stabilization +/- Cricoid if uncooperative; Watch for ↑ICP (conflict); Avoid SUX >24H; Maintain SCPP; Prone position (most dangerous time); protective vent strategy if ALI; possible SSEP / MEP monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergence

<!-- PAGE=? -->
: Keep intubated vs extubation for neuro assessment; Be wary of aw swelling;

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
HDU/ICU

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Total Spinal

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency requiring prompt diagnosis and simultaneous management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
discontinue local anaesthetics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Supportive management - including sedation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Airway - consider intubation and ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Consider PPV may further reduce preload!

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hemodynamic sequelae (complete sympathectomy)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
severe hypotension, bradycardia (paradoxical Bezold-Jarisch reflex), cardiac arrest

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Consideration in pregnancy - Above PLUS

<!-- PAGE=? -->
FHR monitoring

<!-- PAGE=? -->
left uterine displacement

<!-- PAGE=? -->
leg elevation +/- reverse trendelenburg if hyperbaric LA used

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Support airway with intubation and ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Support circulation with fluid, vasopressors and atropine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid awarenesss with sedation and counsel patient once situation resolves

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Call a code

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Stop injection of LA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Support airway, consider intubation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Support BP with fluids/inotropes: atropine if brady, ephedrine, move quickly to epinephrine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ensure adequate sedation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
If obstetric patient, ensure adequate fetal monitoring and support uterine perfusion pressure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Inform obstetrician

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Discuss what happened with patient once spinal resolves

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Risk factors for unexpected cardiac arrest following spinal: Male, ASA 1, use of beta blockers, resting HR < 60, Age < 50, prolonged PR interval. ? related to high vagal tone

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Paradoxical Bezhold Jarsisch reflex

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 mechanoreceptors in the heart (LV>>Atria) / afferent c-fibers / efferent vagus

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Activation wth nociception  reflex hypotension, bradycardia, coronary artery dilatation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 The paradox - receptors in the wall of the underfilled LV may erroneously STIMULATE - results in paradoxical bradycardia and decreased contractility adding to the sudden arterial hypotension

<!-- PAGE=? -->
-Reverse‖ Bainbridge

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 stretch receptors located in the right atrial wall and the cavoatrial junction → ↑ right-sided filling pressure → vagal afferent signals to the cardiovascular center in the medulla → inhibit parasympathetic activity → increased heart rate

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 The changes in heart rate are dependent on the underlying heart rate before stimulation.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Stereotactic Surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Stage I: localisation of nucleus/seizure foci/tumour.  Stage II: implantation of stimulator. Stage III: tunnelling

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoidance of sedatives (burr hole under local anaesthetic)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Uncontrolled airway at risk of obstruction with challenging access (key for frame immediately available)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Coexisting Disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Parkinson's - aspiration risk, autonomic instability, increased perioperative complications, management of medications - held pre-op, avoidance of beta-blockers as this would decrease tremor, avoid antidopaminergic medications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Seizures - hold anti-epileptics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Tumor, Chronic pain, Depression, neurodegenerative disease (dystonia, MS),

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
intra-cerebral hematoma, Sz,

<!-- PAGE=? -->
hypertension, bradycardia, arrhythmia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Sitting Position - VAE, postural hypotension

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Awake, comfortable and cooperative patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Stable hemodynamics (avoid HTN, hydralazine)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid sedatives as it alters electrophysiologic footprint required for nucleus localization

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: standard anaesthetic history and physical with additional attention to the etiologic considerations, and their medications (e.g. anti-parkinson/seizure medications), history of coagulopathy, antiplatelet medications, herbal, co-existing diseases, hypertension

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: standard physical with special attention to etiological factors requiring surgery Investigations: CBC, coags, lytes, Group & Screen.  CT scan. ECG

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: anti-parkinsonian medications held prior to DBS; avoid anti-dopaminergic meds

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Options: Stage II: monitored anaesthesia care if DBS - must avoid all agents which decrease tremor (end-point of stimulation) as the patient must be very cooperative.  Stage III: GETA

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: standard CAS monitors + 5 lead EKG , emergency resuscitation drugs and airway equipment. Antihypertensives and anticonvulsants available

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: MAC for stage II and GETA for Stage III.  Monitor for complications: haemorrhage, VAE, seizures, cardiac dysrhythmias - especially bradycardia (stimulation of deep structures near the hypothalamus)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: minimal pain post-op.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Tracheal Resections

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Diffucult airway with the potential for obstruction and disruption with induction and PPV

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Delineation of anatomy (CT/spirometry/ECHO)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Maintenance of oxygenation and ventilation in the setting of an open airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Standard orotracheal intubation / Insertion of a tube into the opened trachea distal to area of resection / HFJV through stenotic area / HFPPV / CPB

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Priority on maintaining postoperative integrity of the tracheal anastomosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Immediate extubation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Etiology and complications of disease:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
4M's of cancer (mass, metabolic, metastases, medication)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for anterior mediastinal mass and superior vena cava syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Pulmonary sepsis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Severe co-existing pulmonary disease is a contraindication to surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Preoperative assessment to determine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o the nature, location, and extent of trachea to be resected

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o presence of pre-existing disease (specifically cardiopulmonary reserve)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Attain Anesthesia without causing airway obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Planned approach with surgical team to securing airway distal to obstruction/ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid post-operative ventilation for risk of disrupting tracheal anastomosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Dyspnea, dynamic symptoms, associated co-morbidities (pulmonary), type of lesion (vascular/tumour), functional capacity, degree of obstruction, contraindications to HFJV (peds, COPD, Bullae) PE: Dynamic airway obstruction, stridor/wheeze, vascular compression, evidence of heart failure, COPD, Rt heart failure, pHTN (Loud S2, RV heave, elevated JVP) Investigations: CBC / Lytes / Coag / ABG / ECG / CXR / CT / bronchoscopy / spirometry with flow volume Optimization: Consider pre-op chemo/irradiation/ airway stent; with severe obstruction consider high FiO2, inc. humidity, steroids, racemic epi, Heliox; minimize pre-op sedation; avoid anitisialogues (inspissations) Room Setup: Arterial Line (Lt - no compression), SaO2 on Rt, various ETT tubes (armoured, MLT), FOB, HFJV catheters, Surgeon with rigid bronch, ETT to intubate in the field; Heliox; +/-CVP Intraoperative Mgt: Close communication between surgeon and anesthesiologist.  SV with high FiO2, AFOI vs. SVGA, SLT (endobronchial intubation) vs. DLT, secure distal to lesion, bilateral ETT tubes, or OLV, or ligatures around PA's to decrease blood flow to non-ventilated lung; if unable to secure distal - HFJV or HFPPV SLT: HJV through small bore ETT tubes or catheters and surgeon works aron small catheter >> Must have enough room for gas egress!! Unable to suction debis with this method. Or you can use HFPPV (TV 50250ml) through small catheter at rates of 150/min (minimal movement, and contamination of lungs). HFFPV of one lung is usually sufficient! Finally >> CPB >> risk of heparinization and intrapulmonary hemorrhage precludes it's use! Post-op: Keep head in flexion to decrease tension on suture line. Early extubation desired, but make sure ETT is not near the suture line. Avoid vigorous chest physio Complications: Trach disruption, RLN injury, a/w edema. Massive hemoptysis (usually fatal)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Tracheoesophageal Fistula

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Possible difficult intubation & BMV with gastric distension with increased risk of aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Possible respiratory distress secondary to aspiration - acute and chronic

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Co-existing congenital anomalies

<!-- PAGE=? -->
VATER/VACTERL including CHD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Neonatal/prematurity considerations

<!-- PAGE=? -->
altered airway anatomy, cardiac, respiratory, metabolic, and physiologic changes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
complications of prematurity - revision to fetal circulation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-operative intensive care and pain management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals / Conflicts

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Secure the airway distal to the fistula while avoiding PPV (RSI vs. SV)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
risks of intubating the fistula, inability to PPV, gastric  istula tions and aspiration

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Protect the lungs from aspiration preoperatively

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Identify coexisting anomalies, specifically CHD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Diagnose and treat hypoxemia intraoperatively

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prevent post-operative pain and complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx & Px: OB hx, PCA/GA, premature, Growth, congenital anomalies ( V ertebral, A nal atresia, C HD, TE F, R adial/renal dysplasia, L imb anomalies), CHF (WOB, failure to thrive, heave, murmurs), Shunting (Cyanosis, clubbing), Vitals including pre/post ductal SaO2

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Inv: CBC, lytes,+/- ABG, CXR (pulmonary bld flow, heart shape) +/- ECHO if signs of CHD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: Prevent aspiration (NPO, HOB elevated, consider G-tube pre-op) treat aspiration (Abx, physio - delay case to optimize), Peds cardio consult to r/o CHD, pouch tube / suction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup: Multiple cuffed/uncuffed ETT, ENT with rigid bronch, FOB, fogarty balloon catheter, warming blanket / lights

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Monitors: CAS, temp, Aline, prepost ductal SaO2, precordial stethoscope (L Ax to Dx endobronchial intubation)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Management: Suction oral pharynx, pouch +/- gastric tube, avoid PPV (gstric distension - impaired/imposible ventilation, aspiration, impaired venous return), RSI (intentional endobronchial intubation and withdrawal, FOB to confirm) vs. SV (Sevo vs. TIVA), topicalize a/w, rigid bronch to delineate anatomy, +/- fogarty balloon to occlude fistula, ETT distal to lesion; Maintance with TIVA/Sevo + opioid, titrated FiO2 to maintain preductal SaO2 > 90%, NdMB, minimize PIP (reduce gastric distension), avoid hypothermia/hypoglycemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergence/Disposition: likely postop ventilation (preexisting pulmonary complications, tracheomalacia, tracheal wall defect), extubation if term, healthy, otherwise normal, warm, reversed, stable infant, protect anastomosis (neck flexion, avoid reintubation, avoid gastric suctioning below level of repair, post-op pain - epidural/caudal

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Hypoxemia (malpositioned ETT - (endobronchial,  istula), gastric distension and hypoventilation, surgical retraction, aspiration pneumonitis, cardiac shunting etc..) Hypotension (surgical retraction, gstric distension, hemorrhage, CHF), Post-op (GERD, aspiration, leak, esophageal stricture, tracheomalacia, pneumoTx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Tracheostomy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Emergency case as dictated by the etiology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Trauma - facial smash, penetrating neck injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Upper A/W obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ICU pt with prolonged OETT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Shared airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for catastrophic loss of airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Possible difficult A/W

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for airway fire

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Co-existing disease states

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Critically ill - MOD

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Tauma - CHI, C-Spine injury, occult injuries

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Chronic Tracheostomy - RLD, chronic aspiration, pHTN, Sz, developmental delay, neuromuscular disorders

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Maintain airway patency

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Back-up airway plan

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Good communication with surgical team

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Support/Optimize underlying disease state

<!-- PAGE=? -->
high O2 (desaturation) vs. low FiO2 (protect against A/W fire)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Indication, A/W patency (stridor, dyspnea, wheeze, incr'd WOB), Respiratory reserve, Co-morbidities and implications, Chronic Trach - indication (aspiration, developmental delay, neuromuscular weaknesss) type of trach tube (size, cuffed, single cannula, custom), recent trach change, need for chronic ventilation, vent settings, comorbid disease (RLD, pHTN)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE: vitals, a/w patency/swelling, easy of intubation/re-intubation, Grade of original intubation, vent settings, FiO2, neck circ., cardiopulmonary exam - wheezes, crackles, loud P2, RV heave

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations: CBC, coags, ABG, G+S, PFTs, CXR, ECHO / CT scan dictated by history & physical

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization: GA vs Awake, perform procedure in OR if possible, , NPO/NG to suction, optimize FiO2 & vent. settings, optimize co-morbidities, change trach to cuffed (1/2 size smaller), patient position (shoulder roll) Room Setup: Difficult A/W cart, Cook catheter,  Jet ventilator, +/- Art. Line

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: awake with local infiltration, caution with FiO2

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op: HDU observation initially, humidified O2, caution suctioning of secretions, sterile precautions, cuff pressure 15-20 mm Hg, stoma/track not fully established for 5 days = higher risk, Laryngoscope and small ETT at the bedside

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: loss of A/W - false lumen, hemorrhage, loss of surgical plane; A/W fire; Stoma - infection, hemorrhage, granuloma; Tracheoinnominate fistula - hemorrhage 7 days post-op; laryngeal injury; tracheal stenosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Mass effects

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Neurologic impairment (bitemporal hemianopsia)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Raised ICP (rare, but possible if causes obstructive hydrocephalus)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Neurohormonal effects / Endocrinopathies

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Non-functional adenomas

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Endocrine deficiencies 2  mass - Panhypopituitarism

<!-- PAGE=? -->
(G,L,F,T,A,P) -Go Look For The Adenoma Please‖

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypersecretory  tumors - 60%  (prolactin > GH > ACTH, TSH rare)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cushing's, acromegaly

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Surgical Issues / Complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Head up positioning-Poor pt & a/w access, bleeding (throat pack), VAE risk

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Neurologic injury- optic nerve or chiasm, cranial nerves III, IV, V, VI

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for massive, difficult to access hemorrhage - cavernous sinus involvement

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-operative endocrine dysfunction (DI 40%), CSF leak/meningitis risk

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Crisp emergence-min coughing, N/V

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimize perioperative endocrine function (stress dose steroids), consult endocrinology

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Assess and Manage any inc. ICP, avoiding aggravating factors

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Controlled emergence (minimizing bucking / coughing / vomiting to decrease risk of bleeding and CSF leak

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Monitor for postoperative complications eg: DI (40%)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Transphenoidal Surgery

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx&Px: Sx's of ICP (a.m headache, N/V), mass effects (VF defects - bitemporal hemianopsia), & pituitary deficiency (most non-functional with Sx of Hyopsecretion in the order (Go Look For The Adenoma Please) Hypersecretory prevalence (Please Get Active Tumors ). Prolactin - galactorrhea, amenorrhea, dec libido/impotence; GH - Acromegaly; ACTH - Cushing's Dz; Endo/neurosurg consults Inv: CBC, Lytes, Glucose, BUN, Cr, Group & Screen, (look for anemia,  /  glycemia, lyte abnormalities,  Na 2  to hypocortisolemia, DI, SIADH, renal insufficiency), Ca - r/o  Ca (MEN type I), TSH, T4, ACTH, cortisol level, insulin-like growth factor-1, testosterone, LH, PRL,  HCG - for women with amenorrhea prior to surgery. CT (tumor: sella turcica or suprasellar, mass effects, ICP) Stage I: microadeno (<1 cm) no sella expansion Stage II-IV: macroadeno (>1 cm) may extend beyond sella Optimization: Endocrine consult, hydrocortisone 50-100 mg pre-induction & historically q6-8h until weaned postop (consider Dex), antibiotic prophylaxis against meningitis, PONV prophylaxis Anesthetic Options: GETA and NMB for microsurgery Room Setup: CAS monitors + 5lead , A-line, Large bore IV, Foley to monitor DI (40%), throat pack, VAE risk (precordial Doppler, atrial CVC/Bunegin), +/- Lumbar drain (  surgical exposure/  CSF leak) Intraop Mgt: FOB if acromegaly or Cushing's (difficult ventilation / intubation); oral RAE ETT (smaller if acromegaly). Balanced technique , TIVA if VEPs monitored (or MAC < 0.8, but VEPs sensitive to volatile), no nitrous oxide (pneumocephalus, VAE), NMB ensures pt still . Crisp emergence for neuro assessment. No bucking/coughing/vomiting), remove throat pack & suction carefully +/- laryngoscopy Complications: Intraop - VAE, massive hemorrhage - venous vs. arterial, CN damage, thrombisis & CVA; Post-op - DI (40%), SIADH (usually delayed), Adrenal insufficiency (CV collapse - steroid coverage), Bleeding (inc. ICP, brainstem compression, CN dysfunction), CSF leak (risk of meningitis, consider  lumbar drain), hypothalamic injury, cerebal ischemia, Stroke

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Typically emergency situation with potential hypoxia/hypercarbia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Generally difficult airway with potential for abnormal airway anatomy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential complications: pneumothorax, decreased cardiac output, ALI, subcutaneous emphysema with loss of airway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Need for subsequent definitive management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Big take home points:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Temporizing manuever only Need to ensure adequate exhalation of gas ( place oral/nasal airway and maintain jaw thrust ) Monitor closely for changes in hemodynamics, signs of barotrauma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Contraindications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complete upper airway obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Chronic pulmonary disease (particularly bullous lung disease)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Severe CAD or other cardiac conditions which might result in an exaggerated drop in cardiac outpuet Severe obesity Restrictive lung disease

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Transtracheal Jet Ventilation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Catheter kinking Local hemorrhage Subcutaneous/mediastinal emphysema Esophageal injury Pneumothorax

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Where it fits in difficult airway algorithm:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
If unable to BVM and unable to ventilate with LMA then this is a temporizing maneuver while further airway tools, surgical equipment and surgeon are mobilized.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
How to do it:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Extend neck (roll under neck)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Identify cricothyroid membrane

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Add 15° bend to distal 2.5 cm of 12-16' IV catheter

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Attach 20 cc syringe (+ fluid)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o 12-16' IV catheter inserted 30° caudad off the perpendicular through cricothyroid membrane

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Once in trachea remove needle thread 14' catheter to hub

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Reconfirm position by aspirating air

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Connect to oxygen source (commercial jet ventilator, E cylinder, anesthesia machine.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Ventilate with 1:1 IE ratio if using E cylinder, titrate to chest movement if using commercial jet ventilator

<!-- PAGE=? -->
C-Spine/TBI

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Aspiration risk

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for multisystem injury (and occult injuries)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypovolemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hypothermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential toxic ingestion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 ATLS resuscitation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o ABCDE, Monitors, IV access, Volume resuscitation - look for end points SBP > 100, HR <100, UO > 0.5ml/kg/hr, decreasing lactate, reverse acidosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Normal INR, PTT, maintain platelets > 50, normal serum Ca

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Temp > 35

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Aspiration risk vs C-spine injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 RSI in hypovolemic patient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Cspine injury in uncooperative/combative patient (airway management)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Trauma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: AMPLE, mech of injury (high energy? Eg ejection, ped struck, motorcycle, >100 km/h, fatality at scene…) Px: Rapid primary assessment. Vitals + temp, airway patency, trachea (midline), ensure c-spine stabilization, JVP,  flail segment obvious, AE bilateral/adequate (ie quickly rule out airway obstruction, flail chest, massive hemo, open pneumo, tension pneumo), adequacy of peripheral perfusion, quality of heart sounds (tamponnade). Then secondary survey looking for pulm contusion, simple pneumo, tracheobronchial injury, aortic disruption, esophageal injury (traversing mediastinal injury), myocardial contusion. Ensure appropriate lines and adjuncts being used (eg foley etc…). Assess for evidence of occult bleeding (abd, femurs…), long bone fractures and assess measures to control hemorrhage. Eventually log roll looking for hidden injuries including TLspine.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
C-spine, Trauma labs (CBC, Coags, ABG, Lytes, Bun,Cr, Tox Screen, crossmatch, Calcium

<!-- PAGE=? -->
(if transfusing), CXR (although many of above injuries should not wait for CXR), C-spine films (plain film +/-

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CT), CT chest/abd/head… depending on site of trauma, angio or Echo depending on clinical findings

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
See goals above. Aspiration prophylaxis.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room setup : CAS + 5. Art line, CVP (minor trauma may not require), foley, SCDs, fluid warmer +/- rapid infuser, warming blanket, TEE only for special circumstances (eg significant myocardial contusion or aortic dissection). Severe hypothermia may require active rewarming (venoveno) and correction of metabolic/hematologic status prior to surgical management.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic options: Regional requires euvolemia and correction of coagulation and metabolic status. As result, a GA is generally indicated.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative management: Anticipate exaggerated response to induction. Intraoperatively, goals are unchanged. Aggressive prevention/treatment of hypothermia, acidosis, hypovolemia… Watch for fat emboli, particularly in patient with significant pulmonary injury.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Postoperative disposition: High dependency unit.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Etiology of inc ICP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o mass, edema, hemorrhage

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Monitor & manage inc ICP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o risk of cerebral ischemia and herniation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Prevention of secondary brain injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Seizures, neurogenic pulmonary edema, myocardial dysfunction, DIC, DI, SIADH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations of trauma

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Emergency, Aspiration risk, HD instability, C-spine precautions, life-threatening injuries overt & occult, intoxication/uncooperative

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Conflicts

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o awake intubation (difficult A/W, C-spine) vs. inc ICP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o HD unstable (abruption, hemorrhage) vs. inc. ICP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Non-neurosurgical procedure with coexisting inc. ICP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevent secondary brain injury

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o avoid hypoxia, hypercarbia, hyperglycemia, hyperthermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o maintain CPP (60 mmHg), Hgb

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o elevated HOB

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid abrupt increases in BP and ICP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Traumatic Brain injury & Increased ICP

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx : AMPLE, Etiology of injury/inc. ICP (trauma = ATLS), Stable or unstable, current ICP management, symptoms, identify occult injuries PE: If trauma, primary & secondary survey, C-Spine precautions, GCS , pupils, basal skull #, Cushing's response (HTN, brady), irregular breathing, focal neurologic signs Inv: CBC,G&S, lytes, urea, Cr, serum osmolality, INR, PTT, ABG to assess ETCO2 gradient Imaging: CXR, C-spine film, +/-pelvic X-ray, CT head (+/- C-spine), FAST U/S (CT) if unstable Optimization: Secure A/W, mild hyperventilation  PaCO2 30 - 35 mmHg, promote venous drainage (elevated HOB, head in neutral position), diuresis:  mannitol 0.5-1 g/kg, furosemide 0.25-0.5 mg/kg, consider hypertonic saline: 5 cc/kg 3%, or 2 cc/kg 7.5%, secondary prevention (normothermia, normoglycemia, normocapnia, sodium), ensure adequate resuscitation, large bore IV access, blood products, surgical decompression/EVD Anesthetic Options: GA Room Setup: CAS (5 lead EKG), A-line, CVP, temp, foley, ICP monitoring, CSF drain, vasoactive agents, ICP agents (mannitol, lasix), BIS monitor for assessment of function (SR ratio) Intraoperative Mgt: Secure A/W (RSI vs. awake vs. primary surgical) c-spine precautions, cricoid is controvertial, Avoid ketamine and N2O.   Sux ok.  TIVA (prop/remi) preferred over inhalational agents. IV/tracheal lidocaine.  Maintain CPP 60mmHg (MAP ~ 90mmHg), don't delay for monitoring Post-op: may keep intubated and ventilated to ICU, or smooth rapid emergence for neuro assessment. Monitor and manage DI/SIADH inc. ICP/herniation (HOB, diuretics, coma, NdMB, craniectomy), DIC, SIADH/DI, myocardial

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: dysfunction (ECG changes don't correlate), Seizures, ARDS, ICU prophylaxis (ulcer, DVT)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
TURP & TURP Syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Coexisting disease common in this population

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o IHD, ARF (post-renal), elderly

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Considerations of intraoperative complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o TURP syndrome (2%)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Fluid overload & pulmonary edema; electrolyte abnormalities; hyperglycenemia, hyperammonemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Concealed hemorrhage (avg. 2-4 cc/min, but 2.5% require PRBCs)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Dysrhythmias (1%)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Hypothermia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Bladder perforation - 1%

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Septicemia (usually gram negative)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o DIC (rare complication associated with prostate cancer)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Positioning: Lithotomy  Nerve Injury; Trendelenberg  CVS/Pulm effects

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Optimization of co-existing diseases

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Prevention or early recognition of TURP syndrome

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Attention to blood loss and appropriate replacement

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Conflict:  preference for neuraxial technique to monitor CNS symptoms vs contraindications to neuraxial

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Headache, N/V, agitation, visual changes, dLOC are signs of TURP syndrome. Pre-op hx:  AMPLE with focus on comorbidities and discussion re: neuraxial anesthesia PE: Standard pre-anesthetic physical: vitals, CVS (JVP, Arrhythmia), Mental status, resp, back. Investigations: Lytes (hyponatremia, hyperkalemia), CBC (hrmolytic anemia), ABG, Creatinine, coags, Serum osmolality, ammonium, T&S, ECG, +/- echo, Optimization: As indicated by pre-op assessment, blood available if prostate >40g, Prostatic stenting with laser treatment is an alternative Anesthetic Options: GA (respiratory support, contraindication to regional), Regional (SAB to T9-10 has advantage of detecting CNS changes, pain with bladder perforation - suprapubic (extraperitoneal) or upperabdominal (intraperitoneal)pain Room Setup: Emergency drugs, CAS + 5-lead, temp probe, CVP, a-line if severe co-existing disease Intraoperative Mgt: Regional: T9-10, Lithotomy position  physiologic changes, nerve palsies. TURP Syndrome: hypertension, bradycardia and mental status changes are classic triad.  Resp: pulmonary edema, elevated JVP; CVS:  arrhythmias, hypotension later; CNS:  pupillary reflex sluggish or absent with glycine toxicity but intact with cerebral edema. Prevention: appropriate irrigation agent, minimize resection time, hemostasis, avoid high irrigating pressures (limit bag height to 30-40cm, frequent drainage), avoid hypotonic IV fluids, check lytes in Pts with CRF, metabolic abnormalities (hyponatremia). Treatment : Early recognize, inform surgeon, Oxygenation and circulatory support. Consider invasive monitoring, Investigations (Lytes, BUN, Cr, gluc, CBC, ABG, ECG) Treatment Hyponatremia - no treatment, diuresis with furosemide, hypertonic saline (1-2ml/kg/h - do not correct >1.5mEq/L/h). Sz - midazolam, STP, Propofol, consider phenytoin 10-20mg/kg load; Post-op: for severe cases:  ICU, q1h blood work Special: Problems in PAR include:  post-op delirium, hypotension, respiratory distress.  Need to consider these patients' comorbidities. (See seminar)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Parturient

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Exaggerated physiologic changes of pregnancy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased risk for maternal/fetal complications

<!-- PAGE=? -->
preterm labour; uterine atony and PPH, PIH; fetal distress (especially in 2 nd  neonate), fetal abnormalities (T-T transfusion), malpresentation and cord prolapsed

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Management for twin delivery:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
monitoring of 2 fetuses; resus equip for 2 neonates; possible need for C/S or forceps

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Early labour epidural

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Maintain adequate maternal and uteroplacental hemodynamics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Twins

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: Standard anaesthetic history, previous obstetrical hx and any problems with current pregnancy, current gestation ; Fetal history: number, recent US, position, lung maturity etc.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
PE:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
good airway exam, Vitals, cardiopulmonary exam, lumbar spine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Investigations:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CBC, diff, coags, review U/S report(s)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Optimization:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
labour epidural in place early

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Room Setup:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
standard, monitoring for multiple fetuses

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Intraoperative Mgt: Method of delivery depends on presentation of fetuses; Indication for C-section if: Twin A presentation is breech or shoulder, twin-twin transfusion, discordant growth, congenital abNs. Higher risk for emergent C/S; Mgt as for any OB patient with monitoring for 2 and LUD is especially important; Large IV for risk of PPH; Epidural better than spinal if long C-section is predicted.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Post-op:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Increased risk for PPH

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Special: Multiple gestation puts mom and babies at increased risk for just about every possible complication of pregnancy.  For the list, see the seminar.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Vasculitis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Classified as large, medium and small vessel.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multisystem disease with end-organ dysfunction:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CNS: encephalopathy, vision

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Lung: Pulmonary hemorrhage, cavitation

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 CVS: Aortitis, ischemia from arterial stenosis (claudication, cerebral, RAS, CHF)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Kidney: renal failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Medications:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Immunosuppressive drugs and end organ damage

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Steroids and need for stress dosing

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Diagnosis by angiography/biopsy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Consider short course of steroids, immunsuppressants or cytotoxic agents for symptomatic dx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CNS: Pain / Anxiety

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Respiratory Mechanics

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Lung Parencyhmal or AW obstruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Primary Cardiac

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Neuromuscular weakness

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Treat pain and anxiety

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 R/O Cardiac etiology : Systolic or Diastolic dysfunction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 R/O Neuromuscular weakness: Adequate nutrition, Electrolytes, Phosphate, assess diaphragm function.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 R/O lung parenchymal issues: Bronch, ABG, CXR

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 R/O other factors impairing respiratory mechanics ie Abd Compartment Syndrome.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Failure to Wean DDx

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential difficult a/w

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Laryngeal stenosis, friable bleeding tissue (gental, small ETT)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Multisystem granulomatis disease:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CNS: cerebral aneurysm's, peripheral neuropathy

<!-- PAGE=? -->
CVS: Cardiac valve destruction, abn conduction, myocardial ischemia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Resp: Sinusitis, laryngeal stenosis, epiglottic destruction, VQ mismatch, pneumonia, hemoptysis, bronchial destruction

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Renal: Hematuria, Azotemia, progressive rsenal failure

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Possible contraindication to arterial line due to peripheral arteritis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Consideration for medical therapy and immunosupressants:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Cyclophosphamide (decreases plasma chonlinesterase) = mainstay of treatment

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Careful airway management

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Document neurologic deficits prior to regional techniques

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Wegner's Granulomatosis

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Get early help, call a code

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Notify surgeon and nursing staff, IV, O2 monitor….

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Stable vs Unstable: meds and manuvers vs. immediate synchronized cardioversion

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Cycle monitors with differential diagnosis in mind

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Wide Complex Tachycardia

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Anesthetic emergency with the need to simultaneously diagnose and treat using ACLS treatment algorithm.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Consider the multiple etiologies

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Consider cardiology consult if applicable

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->

<!-- PAGE=? -->

<!-- PAGE=? -->

<!-- PAGE=? -->

<!-- PAGE=? -->

<!-- PAGE=? -->
SVT

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Saca

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Trouna

<!-- PAGE=? -->
WPW

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Potential for acute SVT,VF, sudden cardiac death and hemodynamic compromise or collapse

<!-- PAGE=? -->
ACLS, Defibrillation, Adenosine (if no atrial fib or flutter), Global antiarrhythmics (amiodarone, procainamide)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid sympathetic stimulation/tachycardia-anxiey, hypovolemia, ketamine

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Atrial fibrillation and/or atrial flutter

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Avoid AV nodal blockers - adenosine, BB, CCB, digoxin

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Comorbidities

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ebstein's anomaly

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Identify patients with WPW

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Avoid increased SNS activity, afib/flutter and AV nodal blocking drigs (BB, CCB, Dig)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o enhanced anterograde conduction through the accessory pathways

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 Be prepared to treat tachydysrythmias with cardioversion, or drugs - amiodarone, procainamide infusion (10 mg/kg at 20 mg/min)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Anesthetic Goals/Conflicts:

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Hx: AMPLE, syncope, palpitations, FMHx sudden death, previous arrhythmias / treatments Investigations :   lytes Mg, ECG: delta wave, short PR, widened QRS (antegrade conduction) Optimization : continue antiarrythmic agents (maintain NSR) unless EP studies, anxiolytics preop Room Setup: procainamide, amiodarone, anxiolysis, Crash cart, defib pads, Intraop Management: avoid ketamine and pancuronium;  avoid volatiles if ablation procedures - inc. accessory pathway refractory time; caution with atropine, glycopyyrolate (tachycardia), ensure adequate analgesia; Cardiac monitored bed post-op Special :

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 only a worry when the accessory pathway conducts Atrium  Ventricle AND when the patient goes into AFIB or AFlutter

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o risk that the rapid atrial rate can be conducted into the ventricle and result in hemodynamic collapse from VFIB/Flutter

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o AV node maximal conduction rate = ~ 220 - Pt's age

<!-- PAGE=? -->
o Accessory pathway maximal conduction rate = NO MAXIMUM

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 ECG - very rapid, wide complex tachy (resembeling vtach) with irreg, irreg vent complexes

<!-- PAGE=? -->
 In this situation, you should avoid AV nodal blocking drugs (adenosine, BB, CCB, Dig) as this may result in the impulses being transmitted down the accessory pathway

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Safe to use global antiarrhythmics or cardioversion - Amiodarone (adult dose 150 mg bolus, Peds 5mg/kg over 20 min), Procainamide (may get transient increase in conduction through AV node before blocking down) (adult dose is 10mg/kg IV over 15min, peds 15mg/kg)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Wrist Block and Hand Block(Never use Epi!)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Indicaitons: For surgery on hands and fingers, no specific contraindications: contraindication to brachial plexus blockade: rescue of incomplete brachial plexus block

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Minimal, hematoma/infection/nerve injury possible, wrist tourniquet well tolerated Duration Lido 2% ~ 2-5hrs, Bpv 0.5% 5-15 hrs. Use 4-6 ml per nerve! Onset 10-15mins

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Median Nerve: Located bw flexor carpi radialis and Palmaris longus. At the level of the wrist, the motor branch has already left posteriorly, therefore can't use nerve stim! Inject at the level of the ulnar styloid process at a depth of 1.5 cm (fascial pop) bw the two tendons.  (3-4ml).

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Ulnar Nerve: Lies bw ulnar artery and flexi carpi ulnaris. Volar approach: at the level of the styloid, inject 3 mls bw ulnar artery and FCU tendon. For ulnar approach: Introduce from the ulnar side of the tendon approx 510mm past tendon, inject 3-5ml. Can elicit parasthesias or use N. Stim (only one!) Can also inject 2-3mls above tendon which blocks cutaneous branches which branch off 5cm above styloid.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Radial Nerve: Sensory block only, field block at the anatomic snuff box made by extensor pollicus longus and EP brevis. Inject using 2 injections in an -X‖ shape.  4-6ml.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Digital Nerve Blocks: For surgery on fingers, 2-3 ml per side, do not use epinephrine!

<!-- PAGE=? -->
The main digital nerves are derived from median and ulnar nerves, accompanied by digital vessels and run on the ventrolateral aspect of the finger. Small dorsal digital nerves run on the dorsolateral aspect of the finger and supply innervations to the back of the fingers as far as the proximal joint. (4 small nerves at the base of each corner)

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Technique: 25G 1.5‖ A 23- to 25-gauge needle is inserted at the medial and lateral aspects of the base of the selected digit. A total of 2-3 mL of local anesthetic without epinephrine is injected on each side near the periosteum.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Complications: Nerve injury is primary complication Therefore, avoid epinephrine!

<!-- PAGE=? -->
.

<!-- PAGE=? -->
Tondon

<!-- PAGE=? CONFIDENCE=? BBOX=? -->
**** Approaches to pediatric consent

| Age            | Decision-Making Capacity                          | Technique                                   |
|----------------|--------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------|
| <6 years       | None                                             | Best interests standard                     |
| 6-12 years     | Developing                                       | Informed permission / Informed assent      |
| 12-18 years    | Mostly developed                                 | Informed assent / informed permission      |
| Mature minor    | Developed, as legally determined by a judge     | Informed consent                           |
| Emancipated minor | Developed, as determined by a situation        | Informed consent                           |

Assent
1. Helping the patient achieve a developmentally appropriate awareness of the nature of his or her condition
2. Telling the patient what he or she can expect with tests and treatment
3. Making a clinical assessment of the patient's understanding of the situation and the factors influencing how he or she is responding, including whether there is inappropriate pressure to accept testing or therapy
4. Soliciting an expression of the patient's willingness to accept the proposed care

|------------|--------|
| Neonate    | 40-60  |
| 1yr old    | 24     |
| 18yr old   | 12     |

<!-- PAGE=? CONFIDENCE=? BBOX=? -->
**** Normal BP

| Age                     | Systolic | Diastolic |
|------------------------|----------|-----------|
| Birth (12h, < 1000g)   | 39-59    | 16-36     |
| Birth (12h, 3kg)       | 50-70    | 25-45     |
| Neonate (96h)          | 60-90    | 20-60     |
| Infant (6mo)           | 87-105   | 53-66     |
| Toddler (2yr)          | 95-105   | 53-66     |
| School Age (7yr)       | 97-112   | 57-71     |
| Adolescent (15yr)      | 112-128  | 66-80     |

<!-- PAGE=? CONFIDENCE=? BBOX=? -->
```
| Contraindications       | Miller                                                                 | Barash                                                                 | Chestnut                                                                 | Toronto notes :)                                                                                     |
|-------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Absolute                | Patient refusal, Raised ICP, Inability to remain still                 | Patient refusal                                                        | No definitive list - very surprising and frustrating                      | Patient refusal, Lack of proper equipment, Lack of trained personnel, Lack of IV access, Overlying infection, Hypovolemia, Coagulopathy, Raised ICP |
| Relative                | Coagulopathy, Overlying infection, Severe hypovolemia                  | Hypovolemia/Shock, Increased ICP, Coagulopathy/Thrombocytopenia, Sepsis, Overlying infection |                                                                          | Bacteremia, Pre-existing neurological disease, Aortic/mitral stenosis, Prior spinal surgery, Other back problems, Unstable psychiatric disease or emotional instability |
| Other considerations     | Pre-existing neurological disease (usually medicolegal consideration)  |                                                                        |                                                                          |                                                                                                      |
```

<!-- PAGE=? CONFIDENCE=? BBOX=? -->
**Regimens for a Dental Procedure**

| Situation                                         | Agent                                   | Adults               | Children               |
|--------------------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------|----------------------|------------------------|
| Oral                                             | Amoxicillin                            | 2 g                  |                        |
| Unable to take oral medication                   | Ampicillin OR                          | 2 g IM or IV        | 50 mg/kg IM or IV      |
|                                                  | Cefazolin or ceftriaxone              | 1 g IM or IV        | 50 mg/kg IM or IV      |
| Allergic to penicillins or ampicillin oral      | Cephalexin + OR                        | 2 g                  |                        |
|                                                  | Clindamycin OR                         | 600 mg               |                        |
|                                                  | Azithromycin or clarithromycin         | 500 mg               |                        |
| Allergic to penicillins or ampicillin and unable to take oral medication | Cefazolin or ceftriaxone OR | 1 g IM or IV        | 50 mg/kg IM or IV      |
|                                                  | Clindamycin                            | 600 mg IM or IV     | 20 mg/kg IM or IV      |
